1001 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tangye


Appeal No. 02-1654


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 42; 260 Wis. 2d 602; 658 N.W.2d 88; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 59



January 23, 2003, Decided  
January 23, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Green County: JAMES R. BEER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CT-115.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court for Green County, Wisconsin, for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OMVWI), contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a one-car rollover accident. While speaking with defendant, the driver of the car, the police noticed a strong odor of intoxicants, that defendant's speech was slurred, his eyes appeared glassy, and that his face was flushed. Defendant agreed to submit to a preliminary breath test, which showed his blood alcohol level at .26 percent. At the hospital, defendant agreed to submit to an evidentiary chemical test of his blood, which revealed that he had a blood alcohol level of .10 percent. On appeal, defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) (1999-2000) was unconstitutional, and therefore, the blood test was taken without valid consent or a search warrant. The instant court held that § 343.305(4) was not unconstitutional, as a condition of obtaining a driver's license, a would-be motorist consented to submit to a chemical search for blood alcohol content if arrested for driving while intoxicated. Further, because the bodily intrusion the motorist was being asked to allow was a minimal one, the choice between retaining driving privileges and refusing to submit to an intoxication test was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1002 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


Appeal No. 02-2021


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 42; 260 Wis. 2d 603; 658 N.W.2d 88; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 18



January 14, 2003, Decided  
January 14, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown County: SUE E. BISCHEL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-TR-4329.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Brown County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which revoked defendant's operating privileges because of his refusal to submit to chemical testing after his arrest for operating while under the influence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that Wisconsin's implied consent law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000), to the extent it punished him for refusing to submit to a chemical test, was unconstitutional, as it violated his right to refuse to consent to searches and seizures. Defendant also argued that the State's conditioning of the receipt of a driver's license on the relinquishment of the right to be free from searches and seizures violated his U.S. Const. amend. IV rights. The appellate court rejected defendant's claims. The court concluded that the implied consent law was not unconstitutionally coercive, as there was no constitutional right to operate a motor vehicle, and the State's conditioning of the receipt of a driver's license on consenting to chemical testing was a reasonable measure to combat the problem of drunk driving.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1003 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


City of Watertown v. Wagner


Appeal No. 02-1583


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 22; 259 Wis. 2d 934; 657 N.W.2d 440; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1405



December 26, 2002, Decided  
December 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Watertown v. Wagner, 2003 WI 32, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 323 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: WILLIAM F. HUE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CV-51.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver appealed a judgment convicting him of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, first offense. He claimed the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) erred in denying his motion to suppress the results of a blood test, because the arresting officer: (1) lacked probable cause to arrest him; and (2) failed to honor his request for an alternative test for alcohol concentration.


OVERVIEW: The record established the points the officer relied on in determining that there was probable cause for an operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OMVWI) arrest, and, more importantly, the record supported the factual findings of the trial court. The appellate court concluded that, even if it had not considered the driver's refusal to submit to a preliminary breath test (PBT), probable cause existed to arrest him for OMVWI based on, inter alia: (1) his erratic driving, which caused an oncoming vehicle to slow or move over; (2) his "red and glassy" eyes and the strong odor of intoxicants; and (3) the presence of six out of six clues on the horizontal gaze nystagmus. The appellate court also concluded that the record supported the finding that the driver had not requested an alternative test. The driver testified that his discussion with the officer about a breath test took place at about the time he was read the informing the accused. That occurred before his transport to the hospital for the blood draw, and, thus, well before he submitted to the requested blood test. The driver could not recall making any further mention of a breath test thereafter.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1004 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Koenig


Appeal No. 02-1076-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 12; 259 Wis. 2d 833; 656 N.W.2d 499; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1377


November 7, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
December 18, 2002, Decided  
December 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 29, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:   APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: DARRYL W. DEETS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CF-389.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to forgery, and her probation was later revoked. The Circuit Court for Manitowoc County, Wisconsin, sentenced defendant to 18 months' imprisonment followed by 24 months of extended supervision. A condition of defendant's extended supervision required her to introduce any person she was "dating" to her supervising agent. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the report supporting the revocation of defendant's probation, defendant's supervising agent alleged that she had stolen and forged personal checks from her former and current boyfriends. The trial court determined that the condition was appropriate to protect the public from future crimes that defendant may be inclined to commit. Defendant argued that the ambiguity of the term "dating" rendered the condition unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court ruled that the statutory definition of "dating relationship" set out in Wis. Stat. § 813.12(1)(ag) (1999-2000) provided an objective standard for enforcement, and provided defendant with adequate notice of when she must introduce to her agent any person with whom she was involved in an intimate social relationship. Defendant had fair and adequate notice that, not only did the statute differentiate between a romantic or intimate social relationship and a casual relationship or an ordinary fraternization, but common sense would also lead one to arrive at that distinction. When defendant was involved in something more than a platonic relationship with someone of the opposite sex, she must introduce that person to her agent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kaufman v. Smith


Appeal No. 02-0917


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 22; 259 Wis. 2d 933; 657 N.W.2d 439; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1382



December 18, 2002, Decided  
December 18, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 7, 2003.
Review denied by Kaufman v. Smith, 2003 WI 32, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 291 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: THOMAS J. GRITTON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CV-30.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) that affirmed a prison disciplinary decision and dismissed his certiorari petition for review of two other disciplinary decisions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant petitioned the trial court in November 2001 and January 2002 for a writ of certiorari to review three prison disciplinary sanctions imposed against him between April and October, 2001. The trial court dismissed defendant's writ of certiorari on the grounds that the first petition was not filed timely pursuant Wis. Stat. § 893.735(2) (1999-2000) and dismissed the other writ as defendant had not exhausted his administrative remedies. The trial court affirmed the prison's disciplinary decision as defendant failed to prove that he had not lied about a staff member harassing him. The appellate court upheld the trial court's rulings. The appellate court noted that defendant's challenge that the time limit in Wis. Stat. § 893.735(2) was too short was not a proper subject for review. Also, the instant court affirmed that defendant was not entitled to judicial relief before exhausting his administrative remedies. The appellate court also affirmed the trial court's affirmance of the prison's disciplinary sanction as defendant's First Amendment rights were not violated by a rule that punished prisoners for making false statements against prison staff members.


OUTCOME: The affirmance of a prison disciplinary decision and the dismissal of defendant's certiorari petition for review of two other disciplinary decisions were affirmed.

In re Imposition of Costs on Atty. v. Molle


Appeal No. 02-0481


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 1; 259 Wis. 2d 481; 655 N.W.2d 547; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1314



November 27, 2002, Decided  
November 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: JOHN J. PERLICH, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CT-353.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County, Wisconsin, which imposed sanctions on him for filing what the circuit court deemed to be a frivolous suppression motion in a drunk driving case.


OVERVIEW: The attorney's client was stopped in the early morning hours for operating his motorcycle at 45 miles per hour in a 30 mile-per-hour zone. After the stop, the officer detected an odor of alcohol on the client's breath, and the client admitted to drinking some beer. The officer then detained the client for field sobriety testing. In his suppression motion, the attorney argued that the officers lacked reasonable suspicion to detain his client and administer sobriety tests. The circuit court found that the motion was without a good faith basis in either fact or law. On appeal, the attorney contended that the relevant statute, Wis. Stat. § 802.05(1) (1999-2000), did not apply in criminal cases. The court did not reach that question, determining instead that the attorney had a good faith basis to bring a suppression motion, even if § 802.05(1) applied. The State did not locate any case upholding a temporary detention with the same circumstances presented by the arrest of the attorney's client. The court held, therefore, that the attorney could reasonably have argued that similar cases, though relevant, were distinguishable and should not control the outcome in his client's case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order imposing sanctions on counsel, concluding that, while even a weak odor of intoxicants on a driver's breath, combined with a speeding violation at bar time, constituted reasonable suspicion, it was not frivolous to argue otherwise.

State v. Boedecker (in Re Boedecker)


Appeal No. 02-0497


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 1; 259 Wis. 2d 481; 655 N.W.2d 547; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1310



November 27, 2002, Decided  
November 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-TR-3571.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant motorist sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which ordered the revocation of her operator's license for one year under Wis. Stat. § 343.305(10) (1999-2000) on the ground that she refused to submit to a chemical test of her breath following her arrest for driving under the influence of an intoxicant in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1).


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the Implied Consent Statute, Wis. Stat. § 343.305(2), was constitutional. The motorist contended on appeal that § 343.305(2) was unconstitutional because § 343.305(2) forced an operator of an automobile to choose between abandoning his or her Fourth Amendment protection against unreasonable searches and seizures and suffering the sanction of lost driving privileges. The court reviewed the matter de novo. The court held that § 343.305(2) was constitutional. The court decided that an operator's consent to a chemical test under § 343.305(2) was not involuntary for Fourth Amendment purposes solely because the operator had to choose between submission to the test and loss of driving privileges. The court determined that the motorist conceded the point on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

County of Iowa v. Klinger


Appeal No. 02-0737


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 1; 259 Wis. 2d 482; 655 N.W.2d 547; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1315



November 27, 2002, Decided  
November 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Iowa County: WILLIAM D. DYKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-TR-1179, 01-TR-1233.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court for Iowa County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.163(1)(a) (1999-2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's argument was that the implied consent statute, Wis. Stat. § 343.305, was unconstitutional because it forced him to choose between abandoning his U.S. Const. amend. IV protection against unreasonable searches and seizures and suffering the sanction of lost driving privileges. The trial court concluded the statute was not unconstitutional. The issue properly framed was whether the U.S. Const. amend. IV intrusion authorized by the statute was reasonable. The appellate court concluded that it was. No one was forced to operate a motor vehicle on the roads of Wisconsin; thus, conditioning that privilege on giving consent to the chemical tests as prescribed in the statute was not coercive. The tests authorized by statute were safe, relatively painless, and commonplace, and they may be given only when there was probable cause to believe the person was violating Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1) or similar statutes. Finally, the appellate court found that the State had a compelling interest in keeping intoxicated drivers off the roads.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Bush (In re Bush)


Appeal No. 01-0588


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 1; 259 Wis. 2d 480; 655 N.W.2d 546; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1305



November 26, 2002, Decided  
November 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bush, 2003 WI 16, 259 Wis. 2d 101, 657 N.W.2d 706, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 203 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 97-CI-1. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: WILLIAM M. GABLER, Judge.
State v. Bush (In re Bush), 223 Wis. 2d 800, 589 N.W.2d 455, 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1451 (Wis. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State filed a petition seeking to have respondent inmate committed as a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000). The Circuit Court for Eau Claire County, Wisconsin, granted the petition and entered an order committing the inmate. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued Wis. Stat. § 51.37(8)(b) (1999-2000) disqualified the State's expert witnesses at his commitment hearing because they were associated with certain mental health facilities. He also argued that Wis. Stat. § 51.61 (1999-2000), patients rights, applied to prisoners' initial Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000) proceedings. The appeals court held the inmate's arguments failed for two reasons. First, ch. 980 specifically directed the state's health department to have close connections with the experts who conduct mental health evaluations. The legislature did not intend the evaluators would have no connection with state institutions as would be required if Wis. Stat. § 51.37(8)(b) applied. Second, the right to examination by experts who were not associated with the department was not included in the list of enumerated patients' rights under Wis. Stat. § 51.61. The appeals court also held that failure to apply Wis. Stat. § 51.37(8)(b) to sexual predators did not violate their due process rights, as there was no constitutional right to a court-appointed independent evaluator. Finally, the State presented sufficient evidence that the inmate was highly likely to reoffend.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the cause was remanded for a trial to determine whether the inmate was within 90 days of release or discharge when this action was commenced.

State v. Eggimann (In re Eggimann)


Appeal No. 02-0758


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 1; 259 Wis. 2d 482; 655 N.W.2d 547; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1291



November 21, 2002, Decided  
November 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CT-464.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. After refusing to submit to a blood test, his driver's license was revoked. A refusal hearing was eventually scheduled, and the driver moved to dismiss the proceeding, alleging Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000) was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, denied the driver's motion and entered a final order of revocation. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the driver argued that the implied consent law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000), violated his Fourth Amendment right to refuse consent to searches and seizures by imposing punishment for his refusal to submit to a chemical test for intoxication. Looking to other cases that had already decided the issue, the appellate court determined that the pressure employed by the statute to obtain a motorist's consent was not unreasonable and did not violate Fourth Amendment protections. Because the bodily intrusion the driver was asked to allow was a minimal one, the choice between retaining driving privileges and refusing to submit to an intoxication test was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Nat'l Motorists Ass'n v. Office of the Comm'r of Ins.


Appeal No. 02-0511


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 308; 259 Wis. 2d 240; 655 N.W.2d 179; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1241


September 10, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
November 14, 2002, Decided  
November 14, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 18, 2002.
Review denied by Nat'l Motorists Assoc. v. Comm'r of Ins., 2003 WI 16, 657 N.W.2d 708, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 115 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: JOHN C. ALBERT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CV-2389.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent office of the commissioner of insurance determined that appellant motor vehicle association must cease and desist from marketing and servicing its pre-paid traffic ticket program in Wisconsin until it obtained a certificate of authority pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 601.04(2), 610.11 (1999-2000). The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, affirmed, and the association appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the association contended, inter alia, that its program was a service provided to its members, not insurance, and that it was not doing an insurance business in Wisconsin. The appellate court concluded that the commissioner's decision that the program was insurance was a reasonable interpretation and application of that term as used in Wis. Stat. §§ 610.11, 601.04(2) (1999-2000) in that there was no dispute that the association agreed to reimburse subscribers for loss in the form of traffic fines and forfeitures in exchange for monthly payments. Further, the commissioner had the statutory authority to regulate an entity that met the requirements of "doing an insurance business," as defined in Wis. Stat. § 618.02(2) (1999-2000), even if no Wisconsin resident was an insured. The commissioner had a rational basis for not exempting the association's program from the applicable statutory requirements. Wis. Stat. § 600.03(25) (1999-2000) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the association; the definition of "insurance" applied by the commissioner did not implicate the association's First Amendment rights, and the doctrine of overbreadth had no application.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1012 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Gross v. Woodman's Food Mkt.


Appeal No. 01-1746


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 295; 259 Wis. 2d 181; 655 N.W.2d 718; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1244; 2002-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P73,885


July 25, 2002, Oral Argument  
November 14, 2002, Decided  
November 14, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Gross v. Woodman's Food Mkt., 2003 WI 32, 661 N.W.2d 100, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 232 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DALE T. PASELL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 98-CV-679.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Cause remanded with directions and for a jury trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff competitor filed suit against defendant store, alleging that the store had sold gasoline and diesel fuel at a price below statutory cost and had injured him as a result. The Circuit Court for La Crosse County, Wisconsin, granted the competitor summary judgment, finding that the store had violated Wis. Stat. § 100.30 (1999-2000) of the Wisconsin Unfair Sales Act. The store appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the store challenged the trial court's grant of summary judgment. The appellate court concluded that the competitor was entitled as a matter of law to a judgment that the store violated the Act by selling motor vehicle fuel below the statutory cost with the effect of injuring the competitor. Whether the store was a wholesaler or retailer under the Act was irrelevant as, either way, the proper terminal for computing the "average posted terminal price" was the terminal closest to the store's gas station. The store was a competitor with respect to diesel fuel because both parties offered that fuel for sale to vehicles in the same geographic area. Wis. Stat. § 100.30(3) (1999-2000) prohibited sales below statutory cost with either the proscribed intent or the proscribed effect. It was undisputed that the store did not fall within the exception in Wis. Stat. § 100.30(6)(a)7 (1999-2000) for meeting a competitor's price. The Act was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the store and did not offend due process by prohibiting certain conduct or by its effect, regardless of the seller's intent.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed as to the 293-day violation finding, reversed as to the two-day violation, and remanded to the trial court with instructions to reduce the monetary award.


 

1013 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Lake Country Racquet & Ath. Club, Inc. v. Vill. of Hartland


Appeal No. 02-0198


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 301; 259 Wis. 2d 107; 655 N.W.2d 189; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1236


September 26, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
November 13, 2002, Decided  
November 13, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 18, 2002. As Amended November 19, 2002.
Review denied by Lake Country Racquet & Ath. Club v. Hartland, 2003 WI 16, 657 N.W.2d 708, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 99 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: DONALD J. HASSIN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CV-895.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent village in a declaratory action challenging the village's act of rezoning and conveying property as contrary to village ordinances and state laws.


OVERVIEW: The club contended that the village rezoned and conveyed property to an organization in violation of certain ordinances and statutes. It brought a declaratory action to determine the validity of the conveyance. The trial court determined that the club did not have standing to pursue the action; therefore, it granted the village's motion for summary judgment. The club contended that it had standing as a taxpayer and a property owner to challenge the action. In affirming, the court determined that the club was unable to maintain a declaratory judgment action under Wis. Stat. § 806.04 unless a justiciable controversy existed. The club was required to have a personal stake in the outcome. Moreover, it must have been directly affected by the issues in the controversy. This was measured by whether the club would have sustained some pecuniary loss or substantial injury to its interests. The club failed to present any evidence to suggest that it was adversely affected, financially or otherwise, by the village's actions. The club's disagreement with the legislative decisions of the village was insufficient to confer standing.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment in favor of the village was affirmed.

 

1014 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wintlend


Appeal No. 02-0965-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 314; 258 Wis. 2d 875; 655 N.W.2d 745; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1204


September 24, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
November 6, 2002, Decided  
November 6, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 18, 2002.
Review denied by State v. Wintlend, 2003 WI 16, 657 N.W.2d 708, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 134 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: ROBERT J. KENNEDY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CT-134.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin) denied defendant's motion to suppress the blood alcohol concentration evidence, and defendant pled no contest to operating a vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. The informing the accused form was read to him, and he consented to a blood alcohol test. Prior to trial, he moved to suppress the blood alcohol test evidence, contending, inter alia, that any implied consent to have blood taken from him was a coerced consent by operation of the penalty structure of the implied consent statute, Wis. Stat. § 343.305(2) (1999-2000), and was thereby constitutionally invalid. On appeal, defendant maintained that the state-sponsored coercion in the implied consent statute of either taking a blood alcohol test or losing one's license exerted a psychological toll on motorists at the time the motorists were asked to take the blood alcohol test, overbearing their will, and compelling them to consent to taking a test. The appellate court held that the time of consent to the test was when a driver's license was obtained and not when defendant was arrested; thus, there was no psychological pressure on him when he obtained his license. Also, even if the coercive event took place at the time the informing the accused form was read, it was an entirely reasonable form of coercion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Douglas County, Wisconsin, finding that they violated the City of Superior's disorderly conduct ordinance, Superior, Wis., Code § 23-4(a) (2001), and assessing them each a $ 188 forfeiture.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, husband and wife, along with some family friends, rented a limousine to take them to several restaurants and taverns. After midnight, the party made its way to a bar, where the bouncers refused to admit them, and an altercation developed. Defendants contended their actions did not constitute disorderly conduct under the language of the ordinance. The appellate court ruled that defendants' conduct was not constitutionally protected and that their actions constituted disorderly conduct under the ordinance. The loud abusive language used by defendant, husband, was overheard by others, occurring after he had been drinking, in a public place, and in the presence of the police and others. Considering these circumstances, the trial court did not err by finding his actions were of a type tending to cause or provoke a disturbance. Furthermore, the actions of defendant, wife, tended to cause or provoke a disturbance as well.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Mull


Appeal No. 01-3166-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2003 WI App 1; 259 Wis. 2d 480; 655 N.W.2d 546; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1193



November 5, 2002, Decided  
November 5, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Mull, 2003 WI 16, 259 Wis. 2d 102, 657 N.W.2d 707, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 67 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Mull v. Endicott, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23195 (E.D. Wis., Apr. 14, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Mull, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 699 (Wis. Ct. App., Sept. 29, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. Nos. 99 CF 5822 & 99 CF 5948. APPEAL from judgments and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: BONNIE L. GORDON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment and order entered by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, convicting him of three counts of first-degree recklessly endangering safety with the penalty enhancers of use of a dangerous weapon, habitual criminality and intimidation of a victim, and denying his postconviction motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The victim reported to police that he and his girlfriend, and their four children, parked their car at a grocery store and the girlfriend went inside for a short time. While the girlfriend was in the store, the victim recognized defendant from the neighborhood and exited the car to say hello to him. Eventually, the greeting turned into a confrontation with defendant, defendant's brother and about seven other men. The appellate court ruled that since defendant's conduct endangered three victims, three charges and multiple punishments were constitutionally sound. Also, a jury acting reasonably could have found defendant's threat to "take it up on his own" to infer that defendant was intimidating the victim with a threat of force and the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction for intimidation of a victim with threat of force or violence, Wis. Stat. § 940.45(3) (1999-2000). Furthermore, the First Amendment simply did not protect speech or acts which threatened harm to a victim of crime, which were done with the purpose of thwarting prosecution of a crime. Wis. Stat. § 940.45(3) (1999-2000) did not chill protected speech and was not constitutionally overbroad.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

Martin v. Pers. Review Bd.


Appeal No. 02-0157


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 292; 258 Wis. 2d 983; 654 N.W.2d 95; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1173



October 29, 2002, Decided  
October 29, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM J. HAESE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01 CV 2540.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent Personnel Review Board of the County of Milwaukee (Wisconsin) that discharged the employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee had worked as a forensic investigator. She was responsible for undressing, examining, and photographing corpses. She was suspended after two photographs of the genitals of two male corpses were found at her workstation. The employee claimed that the photographs were planted. The Board held a hearing and determined that she violated ordinance rules. Thus, she was terminated. The trial court affirmed that decision, as did the court. The court rejected the employee's claim that the Board deprived her of her due process rights. The Board was impartial as required, and the employee was not denied a pre-termination hearing or the opportunity to cross-examine witnesses. The Board did not unreasonably infer, without expert opinion, that the employee intentionally took one of the photographs. The Board thoroughly examined all the evidence, which supported the Board's findings that the employee violated various rules, as well as the Board's decision to terminate the employee. Her contention that she was framed lacked evidentiary support.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

State v. Ligon


Appeal No. 02-0611


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 292; 258 Wis. 2d 984; 654 N.W.2d 95; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1138



October 16, 2002, Decided  
October 16, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Door County: D. TODD EHLERS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-TR-2871.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Door County, Wisconsin, revoking his motor vehicle operating privileges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for operating while intoxicated, and refused chemical testing of his alcohol blood content. The officer issued defendant the notice of intent to revoke operating privileges under Wis. Stat. § 343.305(9) (1999-2000) and did not obtain a chemical test. The circuit court revoked defendant's privileges after it concluded he had no basis to refuse to consent to a chemical test of his blood alcohol content. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the implied consent law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000), arguing its provision mandating revocation for an improper refusal to submit to testing punished him for exercising his Fourth Amendment right to refuse to consent to searches and seizures. The appellate court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000) did not punish defendant for exercising his constitutional rights. Defendant was not coerced into consenting to submit to chemical testing or unfairly punished for withdrawing that consent. The State was not punishing defendant for exercising his constitutional right, and any punishment he suffered arose because he revoked his consent to be tested.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kenney

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 292; 258 Wis. 2d 981; 654 N.W.2d 94; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1126



October 15, 2002, Decided  
October 15, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Kenney, 2003 WI 16, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 38 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 00 CF 51. APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN J. DiMOTTO, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, for child enticement, sexual contact and sentenced to four years in prison. Thereafter, the trial court denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer posed as a 13-year-old boy on the internet and discussed erotic wrestling in a chat room with defendant. At defendant's suggestion, they agreed to meet at a restaurant before going to a hotel to engage in erotic wrestling. Defendant then packed his wrestling bag and drove to meet the boy, and was arrested. On appeal, defendant argued Wis. Stat. § 948.07 was unconstitutional because it violated free speech, the evidence was insufficient for conviction, he was essentially convicted of attempting to attempt, the trial court erroneously admitted other acts evidence, and that the trial court erroneously exercised its sentencing discretion. The appellate court held the other acts evidence was properly admitted to negate defendant's potential innocent explanation for his conduct. The appellate court concluded the trial court did not abuse its discretion by sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Burris (In re Burris)


Appeal No. 00-1425


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 262; 258 Wis. 2d 454; 654 N.W.2d 866; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1118


October 5, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
October 10, 2002, Decided  
October 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 20, 2002.
Review granted by State v. Burris, 2003 WI 16, 259 Wis. 2d 100, 657 N.W.2d 706, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 21 (2003)
Affirmed by State v. Burris (In re Burris), 2004 WI 91, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 455 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: JAMES E. WELKER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 96-CF-1436B.
State v. Burris (In re Burris), 228 Wis. 2d 508, 597 N.W.2d 773, 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 578 (Wis. Ct. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a sexually violent person committed under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000), was released on supervision to a community corrections program halfway house. Petitioner Wisconsin Department of Health and Family Services sought to revoke his supervised release. The Circuit Court for Rock County, Wisconsin, revoked his supervised release to the community and committed him indefinitely to the Wisconsin Resource Center. Respondent appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following a hearing, the circuit court found that the safety of the public required respondent's commitment to a secure facility. On appeal, respondent contended that one of the rules of his supervised release was unconstitutionally vague, that the petition provided insufficient notice of the allegations against him, and that the circuit court did not adequately consider alternatives to revoking his supervised release. The court found that respondent's challenge to a rule that required him to avoid all conduct not in the best interest of the public's welfare or his own rehabilitation failed, as his behavior plainly fell within the rule's scope, since an ordinary person would have been cognizant that obtaining a prescription for a sexual-performance enhancing drug was not in the public's or in respondent's best interest. The court also held that the petition afforded respondent adequate notice, and, in any event, that respondent did not alleged prejudice. Lastly, the court held that upon a finding that the safety of others required revocation, Wis. Stat. § 980.06(2)(d) (1997-98) removed any discretion from the circuit court to consider alternatives to revocation.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Gallion


Appeal No. 01-0051-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 265; 258 Wis. 2d 473; 654 N.W.2d 446; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1121


October 5, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
October 10, 2002, Decided  
October 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 20, 2002.
Review granted by State v. Gallion, 2003 WI 16, 259 Wis. 2d 100, 657 N.W.2d 706, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 24 (2003)
Affirmed by State v. Gallion, 2004 WI 42, 270 Wis. 2d 535, 678 N.W.2d 197, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 244 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Gallion, 2007 WI App 162, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 505 (2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Gallion v. Boatwright, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 17498 (E.D. Wis., Feb. 25, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to homicide by use of a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(b) (1997-98). The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) sentenced defendant under truth-in-sentencing to 21 years of incarceration followed by nine years of extended supervision. Defendant appealed and alleged the sentencing court committed a number of errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving drunk when he struck the car in which the victim was riding. The collision killed the victim. Defendant alleged that the sentencing court erred by (1) not stating with great specificity the reason for the sentence that was imposed, (2) considering the victim's good character, and comparing his character to the victim's character, and (3) by imposing a sentence that was too harsh based on his age and background. The appellate court held that while courts are required to state the reasons for imposing a particular sentence, they are not required to state with specificity why they are imposing one set of years as opposed to another. The court noted that as victim impact statements were permitted at sentencing hearings, it was a logical corollary that the victim's character be considered as well. Further, it was unreasonable for the court not to consider both the victim and defendant's character when presented with evidence of both. Finally, given defendant's juvenile history, his unwillingness to deal with his addictions, and his blood alcohol level at the time of the accident, the sentence was not so excessive and unusual to shock public sentiment.


OUTCOME: The sentence of 21 years incarceration followed by nine years of extended supervision was affirmed.

State v. Williams


Appeal No. 02-0384-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 306; 258 Wis. 2d 395; 655 N.W.2d 462; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1096


August 9, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
October 3, 2002, Decided  
October 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 18, 2002. As Corrected October 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 01-CF-1546. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: MICHAEL J. BYRON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to suppress evidence that was seized from his vehicle when he was stopped because a police officer believed he was the suspect in a domestic abuse incident. The Circuit Court for Rock County, Wisconsin, granted defendant's motion to suppress on the grounds that the officer who stopped defendant did not have reasonable grounds for an investigative detention. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Four days before stopping defendant, the officer had responded to a domestic abuse call. The girlfriend described her boyfriend as a black male in his 20's and stated that he was driving a dark blue Chevrolet Euro 90's model with a red pinstripe and tinted windows. The officer observed defendant driving a similar car near the girlfriend's house. Defendant was pulled over and identified himself as someone other than the suspect, but did not have any identification on him. Defendant was subsequently searched and the police asked if they could search his car. Defendant allegedly consented and cocaine was found in the trunk. The appellate court held the officer had sufficient facts to provide reasonable suspicion that defendant was the suspect in the domestic abuse incident as the car was sufficiently similar to that described by the girlfriend, was within a few blocks of the incident, and he met the general description of the suspect. The time between the complaint and the stop was not so great as to render the stop unconstitutional. However, as the facts surrounding the search of the car were unclear, the matter needed to be remanded to determine if the police had consent.


OUTCOME: The order granting the motion to suppress was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Thomas v. Bickler


Appeal No. 01-2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 268; 258 Wis. 2d 304; 654 N.W.2d 248; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1081


June 5, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
October 1, 2002, Decided  
October 1, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL P. SULLIVAN, Judge and WILLIAM D. GARDNER, Reserve Judge. 1 Cir. Ct. Nos. 98 CV 6885, 99 CV 4920.


1 Judge William D. Gardner, who presided over the trial and the motions after verdict, entered the orders for judgment; Judge Michael P. Sullivan entered the judgment.

.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual was injured at a fireworks show and sued defendants, a lake club and a fireworks company, for negligence. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) entered judgment against the lake club for 50 percent of the individual's damages award and against the fireworks company for 19 percent. The individual appealed, contending that the circuit court erred in concluding defendants were not jointly and severally liable.


OVERVIEW: The individual argued that because she was free of any negligence, the 1995 amendment to the comparative negligence statute, Wis. Stat. § 895.045(1) (1999-2000), modifying joint and several liability, did not apply. The individual also maintained that statutes in derogation of the common law had to be strictly construed so as not to alter the common law unless such legislative intent was clear beyond a reasonable doubt, and because the amendment to Wis. Stat. § 895.045 could not be construed to alter the common law, her undisputed lack of any contributory negligence carried her beyond the statute's grasp. The appellate court disagreed, holding that Wis. Stat. § 895.045(1) (1999-2000) was clear on its face. Only a tortfeasor found to be 51percent or more causally negligent could be jointly and severally liable for a plaintiff's total damages. Here, therefore, based on the jury's apportionment of negligence, the circuit court correctly concluded that neither the lake club nor the fireworks company could be held jointly or severally liable for the individual's damages, and properly entered judgment against them for their respective 50 percent and 19 percent portions of the award.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

City of Milwaukee v. Derynda


Appeal No. 01-3186


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 261; 258 Wis. 2d 301; 653 N.W.2d 772; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1061



September 24, 2002, Decided  
September 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MEL FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00 CV 10667.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, granted judgment in favor of plaintiff city and dismissed defendant landowner's counterclaim, in the city's action against the owner to recover the costs incurred or associated with the razing and removing of the owner's building. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that he was denied due process of law, as he was not personally served with a raze order, and because the notice provision of the raze order statute, Wis. Stat. § 66.0413(1) (1999-2000), was unconstitutionally applied to him; he was denied his right to a remedy under Wis. Const. art. I, §9; and the trial court erred in granting summary judgment, as mitigation remained a material factual issue. The appellate court found that the city complied with the statute exactly as it was written. The city attempted personal service at the owner's residence five times. The city published the raze order, posted it on his property, and recorded it with the county register of deeds. The city's posting the raze order on the owner's building presented the owner with the opportunity to seek the statutory remedy of Wis. Stat. § 66.0413(h) (1999-2000). The owner was not denied the right to do so. The owner waived any arguments about mitigation, as he did not bring his assertions of error to the trial court's attention.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Seth


Appeal No. 02-0863-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 261; 258 Wis. 2d 302; 653 N.W.2d 773; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 984



September 4, 2002, Decided  
September 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Calumet County: DONALD A. POPPY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CT-75.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Calumet County (Wisconsin) denied defendant's motion challenging the constitutionality of the statutory provisions establishing the prohibited alcohol concentration for a fourth offense of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration and entered a judgment of conviction upon his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: While defendant's motion was pending, he entered a guilty plea to the charge of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration of .02 percent. Because defendant pled guilty to the charge, the appellate court did not address the substantive issues he raised on appeal. Also, defendant's equal protection argument did not go to the very power of the State to require him to appear in court to answer the charges brought against him. Defendant's equal protection argument was limited to a complaint about a legislatively created classification of prohibited alcohol concentration and not the power of the State to require him to answer drunk driving charges in court. Additionally, in order to have standing to challenge a statute as unconstitutional, defendant had to show that the statute injured him and that he was within the zone intended to be protected by the constitutional guarantee. The appellate court concluded that defendant could not show that he was injured by the constitutional infirmities he alleged as his blood alcohol concentration of .113 percent was sufficient to establish a violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) (1999-2000) even for a first time offender.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

January 24, 2002, Oral Argument

August 15, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Lindsey A.F., 2003 WI 1, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 1076 (2002).
Review granted by State v. Lindsey A.F., 2003 WI 1, 258 Wis. 2d 106, 655 N.W.2d 127, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 1076 (2002)
Affirmed by State v. Lindsey A.F. (Lindsey A.F.), 2003 WI 63, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 429 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. Nos. 00-JV-617, 00-JV-787. APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: MICHAEL N. NOWAKOWSKI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the juvenile, sold drugs. An intake worker referred the case to the district attorney, who filed a delinquency petition. The juvenile moved to dismiss. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, dismissed the petition, and the prosecution was deferred. The district attorney filed a second petition. The juvenile's motion to dismiss and to refer the case for deferred prosecution was granted. Appellant, the State, sought review.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile sold marijuana while in school. Her case was referred to an intake worker, who then referred the case to the district attorney with a recommendation that the district attorney file a delinquency petition and enter into a consent decree. The district attorney filed a delinquency petition, but determined a consent decree was inappropriate. The circuit court granted the juvenile's motion to dismiss the petition and referred the case back to the intake worker for deferred prosecution. The juvenile then entered into a deferred prosecution agreement. Thereafter, the district attorney attempted to unilaterally terminate the deferred prosecution agreement by filing a second delinquency petition containing the same charge and factual allegations as the first petition. Once more, the circuit court granted the juvenile's motion to dismiss and referred the case for deferred prosecution. The State appealed. The court of appeals held that pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 938.21(7) (1999-2000), the circuit court was permitted to order the dismissal and refer the matter for deferred prosecution without the consent of the district attorney, and that the statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

State v. Welch


Appeal No. 02-0208-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 241; 257 Wis. 2d 938; 652 N.W.2d 133; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 881



August 1, 2002, Decided  
August 1, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Iowa County: GEORGE S. CURRY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CM-264.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a complaint charging defendant with violating a harassment injunction. Defendant moved to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that the State brought the case in the wrong venue. The Circuit Court for Iowa County (Wisconsin) denied the motion and convicted defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injunction ordered defendant to refrain from harassing the victim or having any contact with the victim's events. Defendant wrote a letter to a school where one of the victim's events was held. The complaint alleged that a bicycle tour organized by the victim stayed the night at a high school on August 2, 1999, and thus, was part of an event conducted by the victim. The case was brought in the county where the injunction was issued rather than where defendant violated the injunction. The appellate court found that: (1) defendant was barred from collaterally attacking the underlying injunction; (2) the complaint was sufficient, as it contained the facts necessary to allow a reasonable person to conclude that defendant violated the harassment injunction; (3) venue was improper in Iowa County, Wisconsin, as defendant did not engage in acts in Iowa County, Wisconsin, that were requisite to the commission of the offense; and (4) the proper remedy for trial of a criminal case in an improper venue was reversal of the conviction and transfer to the proper venue.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded with directions to transfer the case to the proper venue.

State v. Grimes


Appeal No. 01-1702-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 221; 257 Wis. 2d 620; 650 N.W.2d 559; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 878



July 30, 2002, Decided  
July 30, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AS UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Grimes, 2003 WI 126, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 634 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 00-CM-1812. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown County: SUE E. BISCHEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest in the Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, to carrying a concealed weapon, Wis. Stat. § 941.23 (1999-2000), and was sentenced accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a single-car accident, and, during the investigation, officers discovered a loaded pellet gun in the vehicle. Defendant was charged with, and later convicted of, carrying a concealed weapon. On appeal, defendant argued Wis. Const. art. I, § 25, which provided that people had the right to keep and bear arms, rendered Wis. Stat. § 941.23 (1999-2000) unconstitutional. The appellate court initially noted the unconstitutionality of a statute needed to be established beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held nothing in the amendment to the state constitution cited by defendant granted the right to carry concealed weapons. The appellate court concluded Wis. Stat. § 941.23 (1999-2000) did not impinge on the right to keep and bear arms, it simply limited the manner in which they were carried; therefore, defendant failed to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that Wis. Stat. § 941.23 (1999-2000) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Wilde


Appeal No. 02-0126-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 221; 257 Wis. 2d 622; 650 N.W.2d 560; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 851



July 25, 2002, Decided  
July 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AS UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 97-CT-134. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Green County: JAMES R. BEER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Green County, Wisconsin, denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and found him guilty of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, second offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that an officer hear the loud roar of a truck engine, observed a truck quickly accelerating through an intersection at a high rate of speed, and followed the truck. The officer approached defendant as he exited the truck and smelled alcohol on defendant's breath; defendant failed field sobriety tests and was arrested. On review, defendant argued that his motion to suppress evidence should have been granted because the ordinance under which he was stopped, Monroe, Wis., Ordinance 9-4-20(B), was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court disagreed, finding that not all unnecessary and annoying noise was prohibited; the ordinance only regulated noise created by squealing tires, excessive acceleration of engine or by emitting unnecessary and loud muffler noises. The officer stopped defendant for excessive acceleration. The appellate court concluded that the circumstances were set out with sufficient specificity. Therefore, the ordinance did not fail for vagueness.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1031 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Dotty Dumpling's Dowry v. Cmty. Dev. Auth.


Appeal No. 01-1913


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 200; 257 Wis. 2d 377; 651 N.W.2d 1; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 855


January 11, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
July 25, 2002, Decided  
July 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   Cir. Ct. No. 00-CV-3379, 01-CV-259. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a municipal community development authority (condemnor), petitioned the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, for a writ of assistance under Wis. Stat. § 32.05(8) (1999-2000) to oust defendant, an owner and operator of a restaurant, from premises that had been condemned. The circuit court issued a writ of assistance, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner asserted the circuit court erred in granting the writ because "a comparable replacement property" was not "made available" to it as required by § 32.05(8) in that the cost to purchase and remodel the only property identified by the condemnor which met the owner's criteria far exceeded the amount the owner would receive from the condemnor. It was uncontested that the owner had not waived its right to receive relocation benefits, and was a "displaced person" within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 32.19(2)(e) (1999-2000), and that the condemnor had deposited with the circuit court the maximum business replacement payment allowable under § 32.19(4) for owner-occupied business premises. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 32.05(8) (1999-2000) granted a condemnee no rights beyond those authorized under the relocation assistance statutes, and that by identifying potential replacement properties, obtaining renovation cost estimates, tendering the maximum replacement payment, and offering reimbursement for other statutorily authorized relocation expenses, the condemnor had "made available" a comparable replacement property to the extent required by the relocation assistance law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's issuance of a writ of assistance.

State v. Church


Appeal No. 01-3100-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 212; 257 Wis. 2d 442; 650 N.W.2d 873; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 850


May 13, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
July 25, 2002, Decided  
July 25, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Church, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 820 (2002).
Review granted by State v. Church, 2002 WI 121, 257 Wis. 2d 116, 653 N.W.2d 888, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 820 (2002)
Reversed by State v. Church, 2003 WI 74, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 445 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 96-CF-1408. APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge.
State v. Church, 223 Wis. 2d 641, 589 N.W.2d 638, 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1446 (Wis. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault, child sexual exploitation, delivering a controlled substance, and child enticement. He was sentenced to 13 years in prison for assault, with sentence withheld and probation on the rest. Upon remand for resentencing, the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) followed the first sentence, but increased the assault sentence to 17 years, and denied defendant's motion to modify. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not accept responsibility for his crime or try to get treatment. The appellate court found that the original two convictions for enticement were multiplicitous, reversed one, but then concluded that it had to vacate all the sentences imposed and remand. The trial court ordered an updated presentence report, for which defendant did not cooperate. At resentencing, defendant addressed the trial court, acknowledged responsibility, and apologized. His prison behavior was found to have been good. The appellate court found that the trial court affirmatively stated on the record the grounds for increasing the sentence on the assault conviction, and that the grounds were based on objective, identifiable factual information derived from events occurring after the original sentencing that warranted an increase in sentence. Thus defendant was not denied due process. The trial court could reasonably decide that defendant's positive conduct did not overcome his need for sex-offender treatment, and that longer incarceration was needed given his failure for four years to seek treatment. The trial court did not disbelieve defendant's tardy expression of remorse.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jones


Appeal No. 01-1398-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 196; 257 Wis. 2d 319; 651 N.W.2d 305; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 854


February 12, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
July 25, 2002, Decided  
July 25, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   Cir. Ct. No. 99-CF-1. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marquette County: RICHARD O. WRIGHT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to quash two search warrants and to suppress the evidence obtained. The Circuit Court for Marquette County (Wisconsin) denied the motions, and after a jury trial, convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and without the required tax stamps. Defendant appealed and sought a new trial.


OVERVIEW: A proven confidential informant (CI) told federal drug agents that defendant was a large-scale trafficker using Wisconsin property to conceal narcotics, and had a white semi-trailer with a hidden roof compartment for drugs. The CI gave the agents a phone number connected to a specific property. About six months later, Wisconsin police noticed such a semi on the property with tracks in the snow less than two weeks old, and based on all this information, got a search warrant. They made search; found the compartment, firearms, and drugs; learned from witnesses of activity at another property of defendant's; based on all this, got a second warrant; and discovered 32 marijuana bricks there. The appellate court found that the facts alleged in the warrants sufficiently showed that the CI provided reliable, non-stale information. The facts had been specific and the six-month lag, though a close call, was not too long given the long-term nature of drug trafficking. Wis. Stat. §§ 139.87-139.96 (1997-98), the drug tax stamp law, was constitutional. The two convictions did not constitute double jeopardy. Different fingerprints on the bricks were not inconsistent with defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. A new trial was not ordered.

State v. Pagac


Appeal No. 02-0573-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 221; 257 Wis. 2d 623; 650 N.W.2d 560; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 817



July 16, 2002, Decided  
July 16, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AS UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 01-CM-222. APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Ashland County: ROBERT E. EATON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Ashland County (Wisconsin), convicting him of possession of marijuana, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 961.41(3g)(e) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: A police officer requested a search warrant based upon information he received from a confidential informant. The informant voluntarily offered information regarding drug activity witnessed at a party at defendant's house. The trial judge granted the application and issued a search warrant. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court should have granted his motion to suppress evidence derived from what he contended was an illegally executed search warrant. The appellate court held that the informant's affidavit provided a substantial basis for concluding that probable cause existed, and the judge had sufficient facts to believe that drugs would be found in the house. The veracity and basis of knowledge of the informant were established, because the informant had provided truthful and accurate information in the past, and the information was based on first-hand observations and conversations from the party. Further, the information established probable cause, because there was a close chronological proximity between the informant's observations and a subsequent party, and it was a reasonable inference that there would be drugs at the subsequent party.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

State v. Russell


Appeal No. 01-2946-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 221; 257 Wis. 2d 621; 650 N.W.2d 560; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 826



July 16, 2002, Decided  
July 16, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AS UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 00 CF 6031. APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JACQUELINE D. SCHELLINGER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction entered by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) after defendant pled guilty to two counts of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant also challenged the trial court's denial of her motion seeking sentence modification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with four counts of possession of cocaine, a controlled substance. She pled guilty to two of the charges. The trial court sentenced her to prison, followed by probation and a driver's license suspension. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in giving defendant her sentence. The trial court properly addressed the gravity of the offense and the need to protect the community from drug trafficking. The trial court correctly found good reason to place defendant in a structured environment, given the fact that she failed to avail herself of community-based treatment services. After taking into account the gravity of the offense and defendant's criminal history, the court found no basis for defendant's claim that the sentence was excessive. Because there was nothing to indicate that defendant would have been treated differently by the trial court had she been male, defendant's equal protection argument failed. The conditions of probation did not violate defendant's right to privacy and free association because the conditions were related to her rehabilitation and the protection of the community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, as well as the trial court's denial of defendant's motion seeking sentence modification.

Review or Rehearing denied, Cross Review or Rehearing granted: Raz v. Brown, 2003 WI 1, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 1081 (2002).

Reversed by, Remanded by Raz v. Brown, 2003 WI 29, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 211 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL GUOLEE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 90FA903638. 1


1 Mary Brown appeals from two orders modifying physical placement and child support, entered on May 30, 2001, and July 31, 2001. Jan Raz cross-appeals from the orders entered on May 30, 2001, and July 31, 2001, and from an order denying his motion to preclude the appointment of a guardian ad litem, entered on April 14, 1999.


Raz v. Brown, 213 Wis. 2d 296, 570 N.W.2d 605, 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1032 (Wis. Ct. App., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent wife appealed from two orders modifying physical placement and child support, and petitioner husband cross-appealed from the same orders and from an order denying his motion challenging the constitutionality of Wisconsin child support guidelines and denying his motion to retroactively modify child support, entered in post-divorce proceedings in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: At the time of the original placement order, the parties' minor children were seven and five years of age. They were 17 and 14 when the trial court modified the placement order from a 64/36 percent distribution of time to a 50/50 percent distribution of time, reflecting an increase of placement with the father of 50 days per year. On appeal, the wife contended inter alia that there was insufficient evidence to support the trial court's finding that there was a substantial change in circumstances. The court disagreed, finding that the substantial increase in the ages of the children, and the substantial deterioration in the parent's attitudes towards each other, supported the circuit court's finding. The court also held that substantial evidence supported the circuit court's decision to vacate its previous child support order in view of the change of placement. And, because the wife failed to timely file a reply brief, the court summarily granted, without reaching the merits, the husband's contention on appeal that the trial court erred when it denied his request for costs, and that it erred when it failed to retroactively modify its previous support order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed on the appeal and summarily reversed on the cross-appeal and remanded with directions to the circuit court for a hearing to determine the amount of costs and child support due the husband.
