State v. Miller


Appeal No. 01-1406-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 197; 257 Wis. 2d 124; 650 N.W.2d 850; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 763


May 9, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
July 3, 2002, Decided  
July 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Miller, 2002 WI 121, 257 Wis. 2d 118, 653 N.W.2d 890, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 881 (2002)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Motion for new trial granted by, Cause remanded by State v. Miller, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 687 (Wis. Ct. App., Aug. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:   Cir. Ct. No. 98-CF-539. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: ROBERT G. MAWDSLEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Waukesha County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) of sexual exploitation by a therapist and first degree sexual assault of a child. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the charging period set forth in the complaint, a span of four years, was too expansive to allow him to prepare an adequate defense. The court of appeals disagreed. A meaningful treating relationship between a therapist and patient was built on confidence, trust, and confidentiality. In such a relationship, the patient was extremely vulnerable. When the therapist sexually abused that relationship, it was understandable that the patient might have experienced uncertainty, guilt, embarrassment, or shame. As a result, the patient might have delayed in reporting the matter or might never have reported it. The victim saw defendant numerous times in a treatment setting and indicated that he did not realize at first the sexual nature of defendant's contact with him. When the victim realized the gravity of the situation, he found himself too embarrassed and ashamed to reveal it. Even assuming that that the victim's age and intelligence rendered him able to report the incidents, the nature and circumstances surrounding the events represent the most compelling factor in explaining the victim's delay in reporting the matter.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of sexual exploitation by a therapist and first degree sexual assault of a child was affirmed.

Vill. of Little Chute v. Walitalo


Appeal No. 01-3060


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 211; 256 Wis. 2d 1032; 650 N.W.2d 891; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 750


June 7, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
July 2, 2002, Decided  
July 2, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   Cir. Ct. No. 01CV634. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: HAROLD V. FROEHLICH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Outagamie County (Wisconsin), denied defendant's motion to suppress and entered a judgment of conviction after if found defendant guilty of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, first offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Early one morning, a police officer arrested defendant for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, first offense. The officer read defendant information from the implied consent form taken from Wis. Stat. Ann. § 343.305. Thereafter, defendant submitted to the drawing of a blood sample. The blood test revealed an alcohol concentration in excess of the legal limit. Defendant moved to suppress evidence. He argued his consent through the implied consent law was coerced. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant was then found guilty. After judgment was entered against him, the appellate court found there was no improper coercion or police conduct, and, thus, defendant's consent was voluntarily given. The appellate court first noted that under Wis. Stat. Ann. § 343.305, drivers were deemed to have consented to the testing of their blood for alcohol concentration, and if a driver refused to submit to a lawful request for testing, his or her driving privileges could be revoked. It, therefore, concluded that the officer did not use coercion in truthfully informing defendant that his driving privileges could be revoked for refusing to submit to the testing.


OUTCOME: The judgment, which denied defendant's motion to suppress and convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, was affirmed.

State v. Henrickson


Appeal No. 02-0062-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 193; 256 Wis. 2d 1048; 650 N.W.2d 322; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 747



June 27, 2002, Decided  
June 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 00-CT-14. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOHN R. STORCK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his pretrial motion to suppress the results of the test of his blood for alcohol concentration was denied, defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) of driving while under the influence of an intoxicant, second offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended the trial court erred when it denied his suppression motion. He first contended the draw of his blood was unconstitutional under the U.S. Const. amend. IV because the State could have made a breath test available instead. The appellate court concluded the blood draw did not violate the Fourth Amendment. His second contention was that the testing of his blood for alcohol was a search under the Fourth Amendment and was a separate search from the drawing of his blood. Defendant went on to argue that the separate search violated the Fourth Amendment because it is a warrantless search that was not justified by exigent circumstances and was without consent. The appellate court held, based on precedent, that the seizure of defendant's blood was permitted under the exigent circumstances exception to the warrant requirement of the Fourth Amendment. The appellate court further held the analysis of his legally seized blood was not a separate search for Fourth Amendment purposes, and since his blood was legally seized, the blood analysis was lawful whether he consented or not.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jorgensen


Appeal No. 01-2690-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 193; 256 Wis. 2d 1047; 650 N.W.2d 322; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 743



June 27, 2002, Decided  
June 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Jorgensen, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 819 (2002).
Review granted by State v. Jorgensen, 2002 WI 121, 257 Wis. 2d 116, 653 N.W.2d 888, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 819 (2002)
Affirmed by State v. Jorgensen, 2003 WI 105, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 487 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 99-CT-1250. APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Dane County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, fourth offense. The court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that her counsel was ineffective for failing to move to suppress a statement defendant made to police about another person being the driver of the car. The court of appeals disagreed. It was apparent that the statement did not affect the verdict. Defendant told an uninterested witness that she was alone. Defendant was found in the driver's seat shortly after the engine stopped running. She asked for gasoline so she could drive to town. There was no evidence to corroborate her testimony that someone else was driving. Police officers responding to the call did not observe anyone walking for help in the vicinity of the incident. Defendant failed to produce the alleged driver's name until almost eight weeks after her arrest, and she explained at trial the delay was because she barely knew him. The alleged driver testified that he was not the driver, and that he did not even know defendant at the time of her arrest. There was no reasonable probability that suppressing the statement would have led to a different result in the case. Therefore, counsel was not ineffective for failing to move for suppression.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Grawey


Appeal No. 02-0272-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 193; 256 Wis. 2d 1049; 650 N.W.2d 322; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 746



June 27, 2002, Decided  
June 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Iowa County: WILLIAM D. DYKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CT-33.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Iowa County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), third offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying her motion to suppress evidence of her refusal to submit to a blood draw, as her refusal was justified, because a warrantless seizure of her blood was unreasonable. The court of appeals disagreed. When an officer was faced with an objection to a blood draw based on a fear of needles, even when supported by a prior incident, the officer had very little basis for evaluating the reasonableness of that objection. How was the officer to know whether the objection was based on a genuine and intense fear, or on a very common preference not to have one's skin pierced with a needle, or on a desire not to permit the gathering of evidence of intoxication. If, however, the person objecting also offered to take an alternative test, the officer at least had an objective basis for eliminating the possibility that the person's refusal was based on a desire to prevent gathering evidence of intoxication. Therefore, defendant's objection was not reasonable, and the trial court did not err by denying her motion to suppress evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1043 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Luck


Appeal No. 01-2150-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 193; 256 Wis. 2d 1047; 650 N.W.2d 321; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 672



June 11, 2002, Decided  
June 11, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 01 CF 554. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT C. CRAWFORD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with failure to comply with an officer's attempt to take a person into custody, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.415(2) (1999-2000). Defendant filed a pre-trial motion asking the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) to find § 946.415 unconstitutional on its face, which it did. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife reported to police that he had threatened her with a large knife. She locked herself in the bathroom. When the police arrived at the home, defendant came out and confronted them. At gunpoint, they ordered him to place his hands over his head and lie on the ground. He refused, told them to shoot him, then retreated into the home. His wife was able to escape and advised police that he had a gun and planned on using it. The appellate court found that the trial court erred when it found § 946.415 unconstitutional. Statutes were presumed constitutional. Punishing people for interfering with the police attempting to exercise lawful authority and deterring people from engaging in that interference provided a sufficient rational basis for the statute's enactment. The statute did not infringe on the Fourth Amendment since a person remaining in a house would not violate it if police could not lawfully order the person out. The statute did not implicate free speech or expression and the First Amendment. A phrase in the statute, "lawful arrest," was not impermissibly vague in all of its possible applications.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the cause was remanded.

State v. Zuerner


Appeal No. 01-2337-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 193; 256 Wis. 2d 1047; 650 N.W.2d 321; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 663



June 6, 2002, Decided  
June 6, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 00-CT-157. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sauk County: JAMES EVENSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Sauk County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OWI) as a third offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in sentencing him as a third time OWI offender instead of as a second offender because his waiver of counsel in the prior case was not voluntary. The court of appeals agreed. When a prima facie showing was made that a prior conviction involved a violation of the right to counsel, the State had to overcome the presumption against waiver of counsel and prove that the defendant knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently waived the right to counsel in the prior proceeding. The State did not do so, both because the last minute filing of defendant's motion and supporting documents did not allow the State to obtain additional items from the record of the 1993 conviction (which was in a different county), and because the trial court did not give the State the opportunity to respond to the motion before ruling. The State did not argue that defendant's motion was properly denied as untimely, and thus the record indicated that the 1993 conviction was constitutionally suspect. Therefore, the trial court erred.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Michels


Appeal No. 01-3282


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 193; 256 Wis. 2d 1048; 650 N.W.2d 322; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 650



June 4, 2002, Decided  
June 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 01CV2050. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MAXINE A. WHITE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, forfeiting defendant's rights to a 1957 Triumph automobile and transferring title to the State of Wisconsin, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.65(6) (1997-98).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, third offense. When he was arrested, defendant was driving a 1996 Ford Explorer, one of three vehicles defendant owned. Defendant transferred the title to the Explorer to a third person. Following defendant's guilty plea, the State sought forfeiture of defendant's vehicle, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.65(6) (1997-98). However, because the vehicle used in the commission of the offense was no longer titled to defendant, the State sought forfeiture of defendant's 1957 Triumph automobile. The Triumph was seized, the State commenced a forfeiture action, pursuant to § 346.65(6), and the circuit court granted the State's forfeiture motion. The order was stayed pending appeal. On appeal, defendant contended that § 346.65(6), as applied to the 1957 Triumph, was unconstitutional as violative of the Double Jeopardy Clause of United States Constitution, as well as Wis. Const. art. I, § 8. The court agreed, finding that § 346.65(6) was unconstitutionally applied to defendant, as there was not an adequate nexus between the motor vehicle seized and the underlying offense to justify a forfeiture as a civil remedial sanction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court and remanded with directions to vacate the order forfeiting defendant's 1957 Triumph automobile.

Lakefront Neighborhood Coalition v. City of Milwaukee


Appeal No. 01-2550


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 165; 256 Wis. 2d 694; 647 N.W.2d 468; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 647



May 29, 2002, Decided  
May 29, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 01 CV 3493. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM J. HAESE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A developer sought to develop a vacant lot. Respondent city declared the lot as blighted and transferred the land to respondent redevelopment authority. Appellants, citizens group and individuals, filed suit to challenge the blighted designation and to stop the proposed development. The Circuit Court, Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), found that the appellants lacked standing to sue and dismissed the suit. The appellants challenged the decision.


OVERVIEW: The trial court reviewed the appellants' complaint and determined that the group and the individual plaintiffs failed to allege any identifiable injury and, therefore, did not have standing to sue. The trial court also ruled that the complaint failed to state a claim for which relief could be granted. The appellate court disagreed and reversed. The court found that the complaint stated a claim for which relief could be granted, as it identified a justiciable controversy, whether the vacant land was properly designated as "blighted." The complaint identified parties with adverse interests, alleged that the parties seeking relief had an identifiable interest, and the controversy was ripe for determination. The injuries identified included: the inability of the parties to use and enjoy their residences by decreasing the green space that was used for recreation and aesthetic enjoyment; an increase in potential safety hazards resulting from the removal of the right-of-way while driving to and from the residences; and obstruction of the view of the lakefront.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

County of Fond Du Lac v. Derksen


Appeal No. 01-2870


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 160; 256 Wis. 2d 490; 647 N.W.2d 922; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 643


April 26, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
May 29, 2002, Decided  
May 29, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 01-TR-6480. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: DALE L. ENGLISH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Fond du Lac County moved for forfeiture of appellant driver's operating license. The Circuit Court of Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin) found the driver guilty of operating a motor vehicle after suspension of his operating privileges. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver argued he was a sovereign free man who lived in the country by free choice. With respect to the public highways of the country, he had not entered into any contract whereby he had given up his rights as a sovereign free man in exchange for a license and therefore continued to enjoy his rights without interference of police power. The driver also argued he had a right to confront his accuser, who must be a human being, not a corporate body such as the county. The court ruled that the driver had a privilege, but not a right to drive a motor vehicle upon a public highway. To exercise that privilege the driver had to satisfy the licensing requirements of the state, which were not done. Furthermore, when the county prosecuted traffic code violations, it was really the citizens of the county who were the complainants.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Radke


Appeal No. 01-1879-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 146; 256 Wis. 2d 448; 647 N.W.2d 873; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 622


March 14, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
May 23, 2002, Decided  
May 23, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Radke, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 813 (2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 99-CF-518. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, of repeated acts of sexual assault of the same child, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 948.025(1), 948.02(1) (1997-98). Because defendant had been convicted previously of another child sexual assault, the circuit court sentenced him to life in prison without parole, as required by Wis. Stat. § 939.62(2m)(b)1, (c) (1997-98). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant asserted a facial substantive due process challenge to § 939.62(2m)(b)2, (c), which required a defendant to be sentenced to life in prison without parole upon a second conviction for a "serious child sex offense." Under a rationally related test the court found a legislative purpose of protecting children from sexual assault to be a legitimate government interest, and that the lack of legislative findings that sex offenders have high recidivism rates was not fatal, as the legislature could rationally conclude that an individual who had committed two sexual assaults against a child was likely to do so again and unlikely to be rehabilitated. Having found the "two-strikes" provisions constitutional as applied to defendant, the court it did not determine whether a rational basis existed with respect to all of the crimes classified as "serious child sex offenses" under Wis. Stat. § 939.62(2m)(a)1m. The court also rejected defendant's equal protection argument, finding that a rational basis existed for imposing "two strike" sentencing on defendants convicted of child sexual assault while providing "three strikes" for defendants convicted of Class A serious felonies.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

State ex rel. Garibay v. Circuit Court


Appeal No. 02-0952-W


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 164; 256 Wis. 2d 438; 647 N.W.2d 455; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 609


May 6, 2002, Submitted on Petition  
May 22, 2002, Decided  
May 22, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 02-CF-177. PROHIBITION to the circuit court for Kenosha County: BRUCE E. SCHROEDER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of prohibition against appellee Circuit Court for Kenosha County, Wisconsin, requiring the trial court to grant defendant's request for substitution of the judge, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.20(6) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant were separately indicted on charges of first degree sexual assault on a child arising from the same episode. Defendant turned himself in, but the co-defendant fled and had not been apprehended at the time defendant filed his motion for substitution of the trial judge. The trial court denied the motion on the ground that Wis. Stat. § 971.20(6) (1999-2000), which governed such requests, required that all defendant's join in the request. Defendant argued that, because the co-defendant was not available to join the request, the court should have treated the two cases as separate and allowed the request. The appellate court held that, although the result might be unfair, the plain language of the statute required that all defendants join the request, even where the defendants were separately indicted. It was not the function of the court to correct an unfair result, only to interpret the statute as it was written, and as long as the result was not unconstitutional, the statute must be interpreted as written.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied.

State v. Bogumill


Appeal No. 01-3141-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 165; 256 Wis. 2d 695; 647 N.W.2d 468; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 592



May 21, 2002, Decided  
May 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 00-CM-494. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: LISA K. STARK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest in the Eau Claire County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) to a third offense of operating after revocation (OAR), after her motion to dismiss on the basis that Wis. Stat. § 343.44(2g)(c) (1997-98) was unconstitutional was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by failing to dismiss the case, because § 343.44(2g)(c) denied her equal protection of the law. She argued that the statute resulted in her being treated differently from other similarly situated individuals and that there was no rational basis for the inequity. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant was similarly situated to those who had two prior fine-related OARs and were then charged with a third offense, where the revocation arose out of an operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) conviction. Defendant did not demonstrate that other individuals who were actually similarly situated were treated differently. The rational basis for the statutory scheme was to punish repeat offenders with progressive harshness to deter future violations. Another overarching basis was to deter alcohol-related offenses and impose more severe punishment for operating after a revocation resulting from an OWI conviction. Because defendant was treated the same as similarly situated individuals, the trial court did not err by denying her motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Subsequent appeal at Vill. of Trempealeau v. Mikrut, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 746 (Wis. Ct. App., Aug. 12, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Trempealeau County: JOHN A. DAMON, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 00-FO-567, 00-FO-568, 00-FO-569, 00-FO-570, 00-FO-571, 00-FO-572, 00-FO-573, 00-FO-574, 00-FO-575, 00-FO-576, 00-FO-577, 00-FO-578, 00-FO-579, 00-FO-580, 00-TR-3333, 00-TR-3334, 00-TR-3335, 00-TR-3336, 00-TR-3337, 00-TR-3338.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted in the Trempealeau County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) of violations relating to the storage of junk vehicles and operation of junk and salvage yards. The trial court imposed a forfeiture of $ 153 for the violation of each ordinance resulting in forfeitures of $ 459 per day. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions. The court of appeals disagreed. There was sufficient evidence to find that the defendant was operating junk and salvage yards. The officer testified that he personally viewed the sites before issuing the citations. At one site, he observed rusted trailers with some of the doors cracked, at least one trailer without tires, and some without license plates. The only change in the sites from the time he issued the citations until the time of trial was the change in seasons. Further, he testified that since 1996, the number of vehicles had increased. At the other site, the officer testified that before issuing the citations he observed a couple of pickups, a wrecker, a flatbed with steel on it, a jeep, and a couple of cars from an accident. On the date of trial he observed some trucks and some cars there. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

League of Wis. Municipalities v. Wis. Doc


Appeal No. 01-1035


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 137; 256 Wis. 2d 183; 647 N.W.2d 301; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 563


December 7, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
May 9, 2002, Decided  
May 9, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: GERALD C. NICHOL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CV-1510.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, four environmental organizations and a township, sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, denying their request for a judgment declaring Wis. Admin. Code ch. Comm 83 (Private Onsite Wastewater Treatment Systems) invalid.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue on appeal entailed whether Wis. Admin. Code ch. Comm 83 complied with the statutory requirement that all applicable state regulations ensured compliance with Wisconsin's groundwater protection standards, as established by the Department of Natural Resources under Wis. Stat. ch. 160. The court's task, therefore, was to determine whether Wis. Admin. Code ch. Comm 83 contradicted either the language of Wis. Stat. ch. 160 or the legislature's intent in enacting ch. 160. The court examined sundry provisions of ch. 160, with which appellants claimed Wis. Admin. Code ch. Comm 83 failed to comply. The court found no requirement that the statutory standards be incorporated into the text of an agency rule. In looking to the legislature's intent, the court found that express textual incorporation of, or reference to, the numerical standards was not a requirement of Wis. Stat. ch. 160, so long as the rules in question achieved the required results. The court additionally found that Wis. Admin. Code § 83.24 neither conflicted with the express language of Wis. Stat. § 145.24, nor contravened the legislature's intent regarding the department's authority to grant variances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1053 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


Appeal No. 01-1993-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 150; 256 Wis. 2d 80; 647 N.W.2d 348; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 521


February 12, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
May 2, 2002, Decided  
May 2, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Iowa County: WILLIAM D. DYKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CM-68.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possessing a controlled substance in the Circuit Court for Iowa County (Wisconsin). Defendant appealed contending that police violated her right against unreasonable searches and seizures when they conducted a canine sniff on her car, entered it, and searched her purse.


OVERVIEW: Police executed a search warrant at a duplex. A police officer then checked cars located in that area with a dog trained in detecting the odor of contraband. The dog alerted on defendant's car twice. The officer opened the car door and put the dog inside. When the dog alerted on a purse that was sitting on the driver's seat, the officer took the purse, opened it, and found marijuana inside. Both the car and the purse belonged to defendant. The appellate court examined United States Supreme Court precedent and concluded that current law did not classify canine sniffs as searches within the meaning of the Fourth Amendment. Thus, the officer was not required to have probable cause or reasonable suspicion before walking a dog around defendant's vehicle for the purpose of detecting drugs. As to the requirement of probable cause to conduct the search, an automobile and containers therein could be searched without a warrant so long as there is probable cause to believe that evidence of a crime would be found inside. Accordingly, once the dog sniff indicated that defendant's vehicle contained a controlled substance, the officer had probable cause to search both the car and the purse.


OUTCOME: The decision of the circuit court denying defendant's motion to suppress was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant challenged the judgment of the Winnebago County circuit court (Wisconsin), which entered a forfeiture judgment of conviction for operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration (PAC).

Thus the blood draw was permissible.

April 25, 2002, Decided  
April 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RE JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 01-TR-1927. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: PAUL B. HIGGINBOTHAM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by the State with a statutory forfeiture offense, rather than a misdemeanor, and convicted, after a six-person jury trial, of speeding in excess of 65 miles per hour. Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction entered in the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant argued that: (1) the prosecutor was both obligated to respond to his discovery request, and Wis. Stat. § 345.421 was unconstitutional; (2) the destruction of a videotape from the citing officer's car violated the State's duty in civil forfeiture cases to preserve evidence; and (3) he had a constitutional right to a 12-person jury, and Wis. Stat. § 345.421 (1999-2000) by making a motion to the court requesting discovery. The court also found no error in the trial court's refusal to sanction that State for the destruction of the videotape, as the highway patrol recorded over the videotape as a routine matter and nothing showed that the State had attempted to affect the outcome of litigation or in a willful disregard for the judicial process, and that defendant did not have a constitutional right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds


Appeal No. 01-2595


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 127; 255 Wis. 2d 801; 645 N.W.2d 618; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 496


March 14, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
April 25, 2002, Decided  
April 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 262 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cir. Ct. No. 01-CV-94. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the named beneficiary of a participant in the Wisconsin Retirement System (WRS), filed a complaint as a class action alleging unjust enrichment and a taking without just compensation by defendant Department of Employee Trust Funds (DETF). The beneficiary appealed from the dismissal without prejudice by the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, of her complaint for failure to exhaust her administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The beneficiary, a WRS participant's widow, became entitled upon her husband's death to a lump-sum death benefit which the DETF did not pay for another two years. Her complaint alleged on information and belief that DETF had retained for substantial periods of time the lump-sum death benefits due other beneficiaries after the benefits were distributable, that DETF was unjustly enriched by the time value of the funds during the periods they were retained, and that DETF's retention and use of those funds was an unconstitutional taking under the Wis. Const. art. I, § 13. The trial court dismissed the complaint, finding that the exclusive remedy for class members was an appeal to the DETF board and then review of the board's decision by an action for certiorari review in the circuit court, and the motion was granted. The appellate court, however, determined that an appeal to the board was an inadequate remedy, as the board lacked statutory authority to award interest on either an unjust enrichment or a taking claim, and that the beneficiary was not required to exhaust her administrative remedies before filing her complaint on either exhaustion or sovereign immunity grounds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

State v. Davison


Case No.: 01-0826-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 109; 255 Wis. 2d 715; 647 N.W.2d 390; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 475


March 7, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
April 24, 2002, Decided  
April 24, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Davison, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 807 (2002).
Review granted by State v. Davison, 2002 WI 121, 257 Wis. 2d 115, 653 N.W.2d 888, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 807 (2002)
Reversed by State v. Davison, 2003 WI 89, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 460 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: DAVID M. BASTIANELLI, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 98-CF-636.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and the order denying his postconviction motion in the Circuit Court for Kenosha County, Wisconsin. His motion asserted that his convictions of aggravated battery under Wis. Stat. § 940.19(6) (1999-2000), and battery by a prisoner, under Wis. Stat. § 940.20(1) (1999-2000), both as a repeater, were multiplicitous under Wis. Stat. § 939.66(2m) (1999-2000) and violated the prohibition against double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with kidnapping, false imprisonment, aggravated battery under Wis. Stat. § 940.19(6) (1999-2000), and threats to injure, all as a repeater. A second information added a count of battery by a prisoner, under § 940.20(1) (1999-2000), also as a repeater. After denial of his motion asserting the battery charges were multiplicitous and in violation of the prohibition against double jeopardy, defendant entered a plea agreement whereby the State dismissed the kidnapping and false imprisonment charges, and defendant pleaded guilty, as a repeater, to aggravated battery, battery by a prisoner, and threatening to injure. The trial court denied defendant's postconviction motion re-raising the multiplicity and double jeopardy claim, finding the plea agreement had waived the issue. The appellate court determined that the plea agreement did not waive defendant's double jeopardy challenge; that Wis. Stat. § 939.66(2m) (1999-2000) applied to Wis. Stat. §§ 940.19, 940.20 (1999-2000), making the charges multiplicitous; and remanded for a determination of the appropriate remedy under the circumstances, taking into consideration both defendant's and the State's interests.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings to determine the appropriate remedy.

Hicks v. Nunnery


Appeal No. 01-0751


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 87; 253 Wis. 2d 721; 643 N.W.2d 809; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 390


October 5, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
March 28, 2002, Decided  
March 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 8, 2002.
Review denied by Hicks v. Nunnery, 2003 WI 16, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 37 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 97-CV-3270. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge.
State v. Hicks, 202 Wis. 2d 150, 549 N.W.2d 435, 1996 Wisc. LEXIS 92 (Wis., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an attorney, appealed in a legal malpractice action from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin). The judgment was entered against him in favor of the plaintiff, a former client, on a jury verdict finding the attorney negligent in his representation of the former client in a criminal matter, and awarding damages.


OVERVIEW: The former client was picked out of a line up by the victim after the victim was sexually assaulted. Hair samples were taken from the scene. The former client hired the attorney to represent him. The attorney did not request a DNA analysis of the hair. The former client was convicted of robbery, burglary, and sexual assault. After serving four years in prison, his conviction was reversed. After the State dropped all charges, the former client sued for legal malpractice. The civil jury found the attorney negligent for both not obtaining the DNA analysis, and for not procuring certain alibi witness testimony. On appeal, the court rejected the attorney's claim that the action sounded in personal injury and was thus untimely filed under Wis. Stat. § 893.54 (1999-2000), holding that the legal malpractice action was governed by Wis. Stat. § 893.53 (1999-2000), a statute allowing six years to bring an action for injury to the character or rights of another. However, the court determined that the trial court erred by not instructing the jury that the former client bore the burden of proving his innocence of the criminal charges in order to prevail on his malpractice claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions to limit the retrial to whether the former client committed the offenses of which he was convicted.

1060 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


City of Appleton v. Tyrrell


Appeal No. 01-2846


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 102; 253 Wis. 2d 848; 644 N.W.2d 294; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 368



March 26, 2002, Decided  
March 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Outagamie County: JOHN A. DES JARDINS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-TR-3222.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant driver appealed from the judgment of the Outagamie County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which concluded that he had no basis to refuse to submit to a chemical blood alcohol test.


OVERVIEW: The driver argued that the trial court erred because the threatened sanction of a loss of driving privileges constituted an impermissible coercive measure. The court of appeals disagreed. Driving upon a public highway was a privilege and not an inherent right. When people elected to exercise the privilege of operating a motor vehicle upon a public highway, they had also elected to consent to the taking of a lawfully requested chemical test of their blood alcohol content. By refusing to submit to such testing, thereby effectively withdrawing their consent, they could not be expected to retain that privilege. That was not coercion. Rather, it was simply the result that occurred when one refused to take the lawfully requested test after having initially consented to that condition. Therefore, the trial court correctly rejected the defendant's contention that the Wis. Stat. § 343.305 was unconstitutional and properly found that he had refused the lawfully requested chemical test.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1061 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Town of Delavan v. Suriano


Appeal No. 01-2629


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 102; 253 Wis. 2d 848; 644 N.W.2d 294; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 326



March 13, 2002, Decided  
March 13, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: ROBERT J. KENNEDY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CV-476.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an adult entertainment establishment, sought review from a summary judgment in favor of respondent town by the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin). The judgment permanently enjoined the adult entertainment establishment from operating at its location in the town, because the establishment was operating within 750 feet of a park, in violation of county zoning ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Initially the town asserted the adult entertainment business was an unpermitted use under a prior ordinance. However, the adult establishment sought approval as a retail establishment under the 2000 county ordinance. The county board held that the establishment qualified as an adult establishment under the applicable county zoning ordinance. On appeal, the adult establishment asserted the town was required to exhaust its administrative remedies by challenging that decision through a timely filed certiorari proceeding. However, the appellate court held the board's determination provided the town with the opportunity to invoke the 750-foot setback requirement as the basis for its injunction claim in its amended complaint. Therefore, the town was not aggrieved by the board's determination, and it had no need to seek certiorari review of the board's determination. In short, the town had no administrative remedy to exhaust. Therefore, the town was entitled to seek injunctive relief from the circuit court via direct action. Finally, the adult establishment did not qualify as a legal nonconforming use, because it never qualified as a valid unspecified use under the prior ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Ewing


Appeal No. 01-1921-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 102; 253 Wis. 2d 847; 644 N.W.2d 294; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 296



March 5, 2002, Decided  
March 5, 2002, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99CF4345.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to the crime of armed robbery, party to a crime, and escape. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denied defendant's postconviction motion seeking sentence modification. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and co-defendant approached a man in his car. Defendant pointed a gun at the man and ordered him out of his car. Defendant told the man to lie on the pavement and look the other way as the two suspects drove away. Defendant pled guilty and was sentenced to 35 years for the armed robbery conviction. Two months later, the same court sentenced the co-defendant to 20 years, after being convicted by a jury for the same charge. The appellate court held defendant's equal protection rights were not violated by the different sentences, as defendant and the co-defendant were not similarly situated. Defendant was previously convicted of two misdemeanors and two felonies and was on probation for felony carjacking. The co-defendant only had three misdemeanor convictions. The difference in the sentences was not a new factor that warranted modification of defendant's sentence. Defendant failed to prove ineffective assistance of counsel due to his attorney's failure to request a specific jail term. As the trial court would not have been bound by the defense counsel's recommendations for a specific term, the failure to do so did not prejudice defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order denying sentence modification were affirmed, but the matter was remanded for correction of a clerical error.

Columbia County v. Kloostra


Appeal No. 01-1319


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 85; 252 Wis. 2d 767; 642 N.W.2d 646; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 275



February 28, 2002, Decided  
February 28, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia County: RICHARD REHM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-TR-9640.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OMVWI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and transported to a hospital to obtain a sample of his blood. The officer read defendant the informing the accused information, and defendant agreed to submit to the testing of his blood. Defendant argued that the State should have obtained a warrant prior to analyzing the blood sample and that, because his consent to the testing of his blood was coerced, it could not be relied on as an exception to the Fourth Amendment's warrant requirement. The court determined that defendant was attempting to have it declare portions of the implied consent law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000), unconstitutional. The court rejected defendant's contentions and ruled, because the State had not been given the opportunity to defend the validity of the statute in question, and because the court was therefore deprived of the opportunity to analyze questions of constitutional dimension from a perspective that was not limited to the narrow interests and views of the private parties to the action, it declined to take up defendant's constitutional challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hanson


Appeal No. 01-2069


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 85; 252 Wis. 2d 769; 642 N.W.2d 647; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 264



February 27, 2002, Decided  
February 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: JAMES R. KIEFFER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CT-595.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) convicting her of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated as a repeat offender.


OVERVIEW: The officer arrested defendant and was transported to a local hospital where she was informed of her rights and obligations under the implied consent law. In response, defendant agreed to submit to a blood test, which resulted in a blood alcohol concentration of .219 percent. Defendant argued that the State did not have the constitutional option of requiring her to submit to an intrusive blood test when a breath test, with identical statutory evidentiary weight and admissibility, was available. The appellate court declined to hold the present case until the supreme court issued its opinion in a case involving an objection to a blood test based on a fear of needles. The supreme court would be examining whether a blood draw survived the test of reasonableness under the Fourth Amendment when the suspect expressed a fear of needles and asked for a breath test rather than a blood draw. Defendant could not make that argument under the facts of her case, and the appellate court rejected her constitutional challenges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Bauer v. Deforest


Appeal No. 01-1764


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 85; 252 Wis. 2d 768; 642 N.W.2d 646; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 247



February 21, 2002, Decided  
February 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CV-2064.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner filed a declaratory relief action against the respondent village, seeking a declaration that DeForest, Wis. Municipal Code § 11.08(3), the non-emergency nuisance abatement ordinance, was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court, Dane County (Wisconsin) dismissed the action and assessed attorney fees against her for pursuing a frivolous action. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under the village's non-emergency nuisance abatement ordinance, the village issued several orders requiring the property owner to remove noxious weeds from her property. On appeal, the owner contended, inter alia, that the trial court ignored disputes of material fact, erred by holding the ordinance constitutional, erred by holding the action frivolous and awarding $ 300 in fees. The appellate court affirmed. The case was properly dismissed, as there were no disputed material facts. The issue on the action was whether the ordinance provided due process to a person subject to an abatement order. Prior precedential case law found a similarly written ordinance constitutional, and that case was binding on the trial court. Moreover, the owner's arguments were limited to factual issues that were irrelevant in determining whether the ordinance provided due process. The court further found that the award of attorney fees was not unreasonable, as the record showed that the defendant had substantial equity in her house and income that exceeded her expenses. Additionally, the owner failed to show that the $ 300 exceeded the limits of reasonableness.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lola M. v. City of Milwaukee


Appeal No. 01-1624


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 85; 252 Wis. 2d 768; 642 N.W.2d 646; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 218



February 19, 2002, Decided  
February 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: STANLEY A. MILLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99CV9910.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granting summary judgment in favor of appellee city and police officer and dismissing her claims for sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: The alleged sexual assault occurred when the officer, pursuant to a traffic stop, stopped the driver's vehicle. The driver argued that the trial court erred in concluding that the scope-of-employment issue she raised was appropriate for determination by summary judgment rather than by submission to a jury, and she argued that the trial court erred in dismissing her additional claim that the city violated her civil rights. The appellate court ruled that the circuit court correctly determined that the officer's assault of the driver was outside the scope of his employment. Defendant argued that the question of how much an employee deviated from the employer's purpose before the employee was no longer within the scope of his employment was one of degrees. The appellate court determined that, although it accepted the driver's theoretical premise that the question was one of degrees, it rejected her contention that the officer's assaultive behavior was linked to some service of the city. Furthermore, although the officer encountered the driver while working, his assault of her was, unquestionably, not actuated by an intent to serve his employer, the city.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Beaver


Appeal No. 01-1796-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 85; 252 Wis. 2d 768; 642 N.W.2d 647; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 214



February 14, 2002, Decided  
February 14, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Sauk County: PATRICK TAGGART, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CT-166.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated-second offense and from an order denying his motion to suppress the results of his blood test.


OVERVIEW: After failing field sobriety tests administered by the officer, defendant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant. Defendant submitted to a blood draw after being read the "informing the accused" form. A warrantless draw of defendant's blood was taken at a hospital, and an analysis of the blood sample revealed a blood alcohol content of .269. Defendant argued that analysis of the blood draw was a separate search requiring a warrant. The court ruled that the seizure of blood was permitted without a warrant under the exigent circumstances exception and the analysis of the legally seized blood was not a separate search for Fourth Amendment purposes. Because the State was authorized to analyze defendant's blood with or without his consent, the court did not address defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the implied consent law.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

Bruzas v. Quezada-Garcia


Appeal No. 00-0043


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 57; 251 Wis. 2d 449; 642 N.W.2d 207; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 414; 27 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1727


July 31, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
February 6, 2002, Decided  
February 6, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MARY KAY WAGNER-MALLOY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 97-CV-403.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff's employer, a subrogated party respondent and self-funded insurer under 29 U.S.C.S § 1001-53, paid a portion of plaintiff's medical expenses arising from a car accident. Plaintiff, a plan participant, sued the negligent driver and defendant-appellant, the driver's liability insurer. The circuit court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) declared the employer was entitled to subrogation. The negligent driver's liability insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's employer maintained a self-insured health benefits plan for its employees under the Employee Retirement Income Security Act, 29 U.S.C.S. § 1001 et seq. Under the plan, the claims administrator was empowered to initially determine the entitlement of participants to receive benefits. The committee, which acted as the plan administrator and appointed the claims administrator, had the power to construe and interpret the plan, to determine all questions arising under the plan, and to hear and decide appeals from determinations of the Claims Administrator as to participant's rights to benefits under the plan. The plan administrator determined it was entitled to subrogation. The trial court agreed, and, by declaratory judgment, ordered the negligent driver's liability insurer to reimburse the employer for the medical expenses it paid. On appeal, the insurer contended subrogation was not appropriate under the state's "make whole" doctrine. The court disagreed, concluding that the plan administrator's determination was due substantial deference, and that the plan administrator did not act unreasonably in asserting its right to subrogation under its plan language.


OUTCOME: The appellate court upheld the trial court's decision.

State v. Marshall

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DANIEL L. KONKOL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00CF892.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, entered after he pled guilty to one count of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant also appealed the trial court's order denying his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to move to suppress the blood alcohol evidence, which he alleged was obtained in violation of Wis. Walworth County HHS v. Patricia H. (In re Alexandria H.)

January 30, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Walworth County: JOHN R. RACE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-TP-9.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county department of health and human services filed a petition to terminate appellant mother's parental rights to her daughter, which proceeded to a jury trial based on continuing denial of periods of physical placement or visitation under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) (1999-2000). The Circuit Court for Walworth County, Wisconsin, terminated the mother's parental rights, and the mother sought review.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court took judicial notice of the facts that the mother was denied periods of physical placement or visitation by court order, and, at least one year had elapsed since the court order denying periods of physical placement or visitation was issued. The mother's defense was that a condition precedent to the child's return to the mother's home was that visitation between mother and child be approved by the child's therapist, was impossible to fulfill because the child was not in therapy for part of the period she was placed outside of the mother's home. The appellate court found that: (1) Wis. Stat. § 48.427 (1999-2000) provided sufficient safeguards to protect Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) (1999-2000) from a constitutional challenge; (2) the circuit court did not err in taking judicial notice of the facts because the mother's defense did not challenge the facts judicially noticed; and (3) the court of appeals lacked subject matter jurisdiction to overrule, modify or withdraw language from one of its published opinions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Eugene W. (In the Interest of Eugene W.)


Appeal No. 01-2274


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 54; 251 Wis. 2d 259; 641 N.W.2d 467; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 128


November 30, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
January 30, 2002, Decided  
January 30, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: RICHARD J. KREUL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-JV-158.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) imposing sanctions following his violation of the conditions recited in a juvenile in need of protection or services dispositional order.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was in need of protection or services based on the trial court's prior finding that he was incompetent to participate in the proceedings in an underlying delinquency petition. The juvenile's ability to comprehend the conditions and sanctions was in question at the time of the juvenile in need of protection or services dispositional order. The juvenile argued that the order imposing sanctions violated his right to due process, because the State did not establish, and the trial court did not determine, that he was able to comprehend the conditions of the juvenile in need of protection or services order and the potential sanctions for violating those conditions. The appellate court found that Wis. Stat. § 938.355(6)(a) (1999-2000) required that the trial court assure that the juvenile had the ability to comprehend the conditions of the dispositional order and potential sanctions, whether informed of them at the dispositional hearing or at a later time. The State did not make such a showing, and the trial court did not make a finding as to the juvenile's ability to comprehend the conditions and possible sanctions at the time of the dispositional order.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Maday


Appeal No. 01-1290-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 56; 251 Wis. 2d 482; 640 N.W.2d 565; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 82



January 29, 2002, Decided  
January 29, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rusk County: THOMAS J. SAZAMA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CM-48.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Rusk County (Wisconsin) convicting him of having sexual intercourse with a 17-year old, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.09 (1999-2000), a Class A misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a plea agreement with the State. Pursuant to the agreement, defendant pleaded no contest to the reduced charge, reserving his right to appeal whether he should be able to present a mistake-of-age defense. The State acknowledged that, as part of the plea bargain, defendant retained his right to appeal the issue. The circuit court indicated that defendant would not be allowed to raise the mistake-of-age defense at trial and accepted defendant's no contest plea. The appellate court ruled that defendant could not enter a no contest plea and then pursue a mistake-of-age defense on appeal; however, defendant should have the opportunity to withdraw his plea. Because defendant pleaded no contest with the erroneous understanding that he could challenge the evidentiary issue on appeal, his plea was not knowing and voluntary as a matter of law. Furthermore, because the State did not keep its promise that was an inducement for the plea, due process was violated.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded.

State v. Bergquist (In re Return of Prop.)


Appeal No. 01-0814


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 39; 250 Wis. 2d 792; 641 N.W.2d 179; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 56


November 19, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
January 23, 2002, Decided  
January 23, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: BENJAMIN D. PROCTOR, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CF-415.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order requiring it to return two guns to defendant who pled no contest to one count of disorderly conduct, a Class B misdemeanor. The Circuit Court for Eau Claire County, Wisconsin, found that forfeiture of the guns under Wis. Stat. § 968.20(1m)(b) (1999-2000) was unconstitutional under the Excessive Fines Clause, U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: Two guns were seized from defendant after neighbors reported that he fired the guns toward their property. At issue was whether the nonreturn of weapons used in the commission of a crime, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 968.20(1m)(b) (1999-2000), constituted a forfeiture subject to the Excessive Fines Clause of the Eighth Amendment. The guns were valued between $ 5,000 and $ 7,150, and the maximum fine for disorderly conduct was $ 1,000. The State argued that the Excessive Fines Clause was inapplicable. The appellate court found that: (1) Wis. Stat. § 968.20(1m)(b) (1999-2000), prescribed a forfeiture that violated the Excessive Fines Clause because the forfeiture was partially a punishment; (2) the forfeiture of the guns was grossly disproportionate to the maximum penalty for the crime and thus was unconstitutional under the Excessive Fines Clause; (3) the State failed to argue the factors to show that the Excessive Fines Clause was not violated; and (4) arguments not refuted were deemed admitted.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1076 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Roger D.H. v. Virginia O. (In re Roger D.H.)


Appeal No. 00-3333


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2002 WI App 35; 250 Wis. 2d 747; 641 N.W.2d 440; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 50


July 9, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
January 17, 2002, Decided  
January 17, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Juneau County: JOHN W. BRADY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 87-PA-11.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner grandmother filed a motion to compel respondent mother to comply with a 1996 stipulated visitation order. The mother filed a motion to modify the stipulation, seeking in actuality to vacate the stipulation. The circuit court for Juneau County, Wisconsin, vacated the prior order that established visitation rights on behalf of the grandmother. The guardian ad litem appealed on behalf of the minor child and the grandmother.


OVERVIEW: The minor child was a nonmarital child who had not been adopted and whose paternity had been established. The mother had sole custody of the child. The grandmother was seeking to maintain visitation rights with the minor whose mother opposed the visitation. The guardian ad litem determined that it was in the minor's best interest to maintain visitation with his grandmother. The circuit court concluded that as a fit parent, the mother had the right to make decisions concerning the best interest of her child and the circuit court could not interfere with her decision regarding visitation. The appellate court found that: (1) nothing in Wis. Stat. § 767.245 (1997-98) required a showing of parental unfitness before a circuit court could override a parent's decision regarding grandparent visitation, nor was there any Wisconsin case law holding as much; (2) due process required that circuit courts applied a presumption that a fit parent's decision regarding non-parental visitation was in the best interest of the child; and (3) a circuit court could read this requirement into a non-parental visitation statute, even when the statute was silent on the topic.


OUTCOME: The circuit court applied an erroneous legal standard and the matter was reversed and remanded with directions that the circuit court should reconsider the grandmother's request for visitation under Wis. Stat. § 767.245(3) (1997-98), giving presumptive weight to the mother's decision regarding non-parental visitation.

State v. Gordon


Appeal No. 01-1679-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 53; 250 Wis. 2d 702; 641 N.W.2d 183; 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 31


December 4, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
January 15, 2002, Decided  
January 15, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Gordon, 2002 WI 48, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 252 (2002).
Review granted by State v. Gordon, 2002 WI 48, 252 Wis. 2d 148, 644 N.W.2d 685, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 252 (2002)
Reversed by State v. Gordon, 2003 WI 69, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 439 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: RICHARD J. SANKOVITZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99CF5375.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which convicted him of knowingly violating a domestic abuse injunction, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 813.12(8)(a) (1999-2000), disorderly conduct while armed, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 947.01 and 939.63 (1999-2000), and second degree recklessly endangering safety, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.30(2) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, among other things, the trial court erred in reinstructing the jury on the charge of second degree recklessly endangering safety, in response to the jury's request. The court concluded that the trial court properly reinstructed the jury on the charge of second degree recklessly endangering safety. The trial court's responses to the jury's questions did not prejudice defendant. The court agreed with defendant that defense counsel's statement to the jury conceding defendant's guilt to the charge of disorderly conduct while armed was the functional equivalent of a guilty plea and that defense counsel lacked the power to offer such a "plea" without defendant's consent. Defense counsel was ineffective, and defendant was entitled to a new trial on the "while armed" portion of the disorderly conduct charge. Because the trial court erroneously admitted under the public records hearsay exception certain documents which were not made under oath or attested to in any way, defendant was entitled to a new trial on the charge of violating a domestic abuse injunction. The trial court also erred in assessing costs against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the second degree recklessly endangering safety conviction. However, the court reversed the "while armed" portion of the judgment finding him guilty of disorderly conduct, as well as the judgment for knowingly violating a domestic abuse injunction, and it remanded those charges with directions to the trial court. The court also vacated that portion of the judgment assessing costs against defendant.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Smiley, 2002 WI 48, 252 Wis. 2d 150, 644 N.W.2d 686, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 302 (2002)
Motion for new trial denied by State v. Smiley, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 619 (Wis. Ct. App., July 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DIANE S. SYKES and JOHN J. DiMOTTO, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 97CF972555.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of first-degree intentional homicide while armed with a dangerous weapon entered in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). He also appealed from an order denying his postconviction motion. Defendant claimed in part that the trial court should have granted his motion to suppress his first statement to police and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Police questioned defendant about a homicide and defendant denied any knowledge of the matter. OUTCOME: The appellate court rejected defendant's challenges to the postconviction court's rulings, and defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Neldaughter v. State Bd. of Nursing


No. 00-2257


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2002 WI App 34; 250 Wis. 2d 352; 639 N.W.2d 801; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1332



December 28, 2001, Decided  
December 28, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CV-1442. GERALD C. NICHOL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nurse appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County affirming the decision of respondent Wisconsin Board of Nursing, finding her guilty of violating Wis. Admin. Code § N 7.04, prohibiting misconduct or unprofessional conduct that violated minimum standards for protecting a patient or the public.


OVERVIEW: During dinner at the hospital cafeteria, the nurse told a psychiatric in-patient that the psychiatric unit patients were receiving electro-convulsive therapy (ECT) without their consent, gave her an information sheet on ECT, and asked her to distribute it on the unit. The nurse further stated that staff personnel eavesdropped on patients and asked her to attend a protest rally in front of the hospital. The court ruled that the board reasonably interpreted Wis. Admin. Code § N 7.04 as covering the nurse's conduct and that the provision was not unconstitutionally vague, as applied to the nurse. Also, testimony that a consensus in the field deemed it misconduct and below minimum standards to become friends with former patients, contact, or socialize with them, or communicate personal information to them for other than therapeutic reasons, provided substantial evidence that a consensus of experts would agree that the nurse committed professional misconduct. Furthermore, the court rejected the proposition that the First Amendment protected licensed professionals from meeting minimal professional standards, even if the professional violated those standards by speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
