State v. Kolp


Appeal No. 01-0549-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 17; 250 Wis. 2d 296; 640 N.W.2d 551; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1320


November 6, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
December 27, 2001, Decided  
December 27, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CLARE L. FIORENZA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00CF2080.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), following his guilty plea, for possession of marijuana with intent to deliver. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. The police found drugs on defendant's person during a pat-down search, which occurred after he had knocked on the back door of a house during the execution of a search warrant for drugs.


OVERVIEW: The police were searching a home for drugs and drug-related paraphernalia, pursuant to a search warrant, when defendant knocked on the back door. A detective told defendant to come in and conducted a pat-down search of defendant, which revealed marijuana. On appeal, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the pat-down was unlawful because the search warrant only authorized a search for evidence of the crime of possession of controlled substances, not for the more serious offense of possession of controlled substances with intent to deliver; thus, the pat-down search was unwarranted. The appellate court noted that pat-down searches were justified when an officer had reasonable suspicion that a suspect may have been armed, with the determination of reasonableness made in light of the totality of the circumstances. In this case, the officer who conducted the search had many years of experience and testified that in his opinion it was common to search any person present for weapons. The appellate court held that under the circumstances, the detective had a reasonable suspicion that defendant may have been armed, thereby justifying the pat-down search.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and the circuit court's denial of his motion to suppress evidence were affirmed.

Schroeder v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


Appeal No. 01-0252


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2002 WI App 11; 250 Wis. 2d 269; 640 N.W.2d 215; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1322


December 4, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
December 27, 2001, Decided  
December 27, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DOMINIC S. AMATO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99 CV 6414.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County's (Wisconsin) order granting respondent insured's motion for declaratory judgment that the insured's automobile insurance policy's antistacking provision was ambiguous and did not preclude payment under the policy's uninsured motor vehicle provision, even though payment had been made under the uninsured motor vehicle provision of defendant ex-wife's policy.


OVERVIEW: The insured's daughter was killed in an auto accident while riding as a passenger in an uninsured vehicle. The insured and his ex-wife each had a car insured with the insurance company, and each the policies provided $ 50,000 uninsured motor vehicle coverage per person, and each included an antistacking provision. Thus, the insurance company paid the insured and his ex-wife the $ 50,000 policy limit, but denied the insured's claim for an additional $ 50,000 payment. On appeal, the appellate court rejected the trial court's decision and the argument of the insured that the antistacking provision of his policy was inapplicable to the case. The appellate court noted the antistacking clause tracked verbatim the language of Wis. Stat. § 632.32(5)(f) (1999-2000), which authorized such provisions. The appellate court also rejected the insured's argument that § 632.32(5)(f), as applied to the circumstances of the case, was unconstitutional under Wis. Const. art. I, § 1 and the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution, holding that the insured failed to establish any deprivation of a constitutionally protected liberty or property interest.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order granting the insured's motion for declaratory judgment was reversed.

State v. Burroughs


Appeal No. 01-0738-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 18; 250 Wis. 2d 180; 640 N.W.2d 190; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1291


November 20, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
December 19, 2001, Decided  
December 19, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MICHAEL S. FISHER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 96-CF-150.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered in the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), for kidnapping and attempted first-degree sexual assault with the use of a dangerous weapon, as a habitual criminal, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 939.62(2) (1999-2000). Defendant additionally appealed his life sentence pursuant to the persistent repeater statute, or three strikes law, and the trial court's order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant induced the victim to enter an apartment through a false story and attempted to sexually assault her. On appeal, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that there was insufficient evidence to support a conviction of kidnapping. Specifically, he contended there was insufficient evidence at trial to satisfy the "confinement" element of Wis. Stat. § 940.31(1)(b) (1999-2000). The appellate court held that the definition of "confinement," as set forth in Wis. Stat. § 940.30 (1999-2000), the false imprisonment statute, and in Wis. Jury Instruction Crim. No. 1275, was appropriate in a case of kidnapping. The appellate court also concluded that a reasonable jury could find that defendant confined the victim by depriving her of her freedom of movement and compelling her to remain where she did not wish to remain. The appellate court also rejected defendant's challenge to the "three strikes" law for persistent repeaters who had committed felonies, and defendant's argument that the trial court erroneously relied upon an Alabama conviction of assault with intent to murder because the Alabama statute was comparable to Wisconsin's attempted homicide statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Lowe


Appeal No. 01-1163-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 34; 250 Wis. 2d 354; 639 N.W.2d 802; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1288



December 18, 2001, Decided  
December 18, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lowe, 2002 WI 48, 252 Wis. 2d 151, 644 N.W.2d 687, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 344 (2002)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lowe v. Frank, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 2193 (W.D. Wis., Jan. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for St. Croix County: SCOTT R. NEEDHAM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 98-CF-284.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: During a routine traffic stop, an officer noticed a roach in the ashtray of defendant's car. The officer searched the car and defendant and found other drugs. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the drug evidence asserting that the officer had no probable cause to continue the traffic stop. The Circuit Court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin) denied the motion and defendant was found guilty of several drug offenses. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court agreed with the trial court's ruling on the motion to suppress and held that there was probable cause to stop defendant and reasonable suspicion to continue the traffic stop. There was also probable cause to arrest defendant and search his car. Defendant seemed to argue that the officer improperly expanded the scope of the traffic stop when he asked defendant to pass the ashtray to him. The trial court found, and the evidence supported, a traffic stop supported by probable cause. The officer testified that he saw a roach in the ashtray. He indicated, in essence, that he was familiar with roaches and knew them to usually contain marijuana. The contraband was in defendant's vehicle and in an area within his immediate access. Those circumstances combined to support probable cause to arrest defendant for possession of marijuana. The ensuing search for and seizure of controlled substances were incident to defendant's lawful arrest. The appellate court further agreed that the charges were not multiplicitous under the standards for determining double jeopardy challenges. A presumption therefore existed that the legislature intended to permit cumulative punishments.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

State v. Kahl


No. 01-1771-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 34; 250 Wis. 2d 355; 639 N.W.2d 802; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1262



December 11, 2001, Decided  
December 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Chippewa County: THOMAS J. SAZAMA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CT-56.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Chippewa County (Wisconsin), convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (1999- 2000), second offense.


OVERVIEW: The police arrested defendant and advised him of his rights and obligations under the implied consent law. Defendant consented to the taking of a blood sample, and the test results showed a blood alcohol concentration of 0.257 percent. Prior to trial, defendant filed a motion to suppress the blood test results, contending that even if the initial seizure of his blood sample without a warrant was lawful, the subsequent analysis of the blood sample required a warrant, as there were neither exceptions to the warrant requirement nor exigent circumstances justifying the warrantless analysis of his blood. The court determined that defendant was not permitted to parse the lawful seizure of his blood sample into multiple components, each to be given independent significance for purposes of the warrant requirement. The court ruled that because the testing of the blood sample was not a separate event from the seizure of the sample, the court did not need to address defendant's contention that his consent under the implied consent law did not extend to the subsequent testing of the lawfully seized sample.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mains v. St. Mary's Hosp.


No. 00-3160


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 1; 249 Wis. 2d 488; 639 N.W.2d 223; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1210



November 27, 2001, Decided  
November 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATE, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Douglas County: JOSEPH A. McDONALD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CV-261.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant patient filed a medical malpractice action against the defendant hospital in the Circuit Court for Douglas County (Wisconsin). The hospital filed a motion to dismiss the patient's claim for his failure to request mediation pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 655.445. The circuit court granted the motion to dismiss, and the patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient did not file a request for mediation. The patient argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by dismissing his claim for failure to request mediation. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court dismissed the claim for failure to comply with Wis. Stat. § 655.445(1), which provided that any person having a claim or a derivative claim under this chapter for bodily injury or death because of a tort or breach of contract based on professional services rendered or that should have been rendered by a health care provider shall, within 15 days after the date of filing an action in court, file a request for mediation. The trial court noted that at the time of the hearing on the hospital's motion to dismiss, the patient had still not filed a mediation request. Further, he did not file a brief in response to the motion to dismiss but requested at the hearing that the trial court send the parties to mediation in lieu of dismissal. The trial court recognized that the purpose of mediation was to avoid expenses and intimated that the patient's failure to request mediation had already resulted in great expense to the hospital. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Steil v. Wis. Dep't of Health & Family Servs.


No. 00-2440


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 1; 249 Wis. 2d 488; 639 N.W.2d 223; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1183



November 21, 2001, Decided  
November 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATE, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOHN R. STORCK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, institutionalized individual, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) affirming a decision of respondent, Wisconsin Department of Health and Family Services (Department), denying her application for institutional medical assistance.


OVERVIEW: The institutionalized individual created an annuity agreement transferring approximately $ 600,000 to a limited liability company owned by her son and daughter, and in return she was to receive an annual payment, with 4 percent interest. The Department denied her claim because it concluded that the annuity agreement was a divestment. The institutionalized individual argued that she complied with the requirements for eligibility under Wis. Stat. § 49.453 (1997-98). The appellate court determined that she was ineligible to receive medical assistance for nursing care facilities services because: (1) she conceded at oral argument that the primary purpose of transferring $ 600,000 into the annuity was to make her eligible to receive medical assistance; (2) the transfer was made for less than fair market value; (3) the annuity was unsecured and unassignable, provided a below market interest rate, ceased payments if she died, and made only token annual payments; and (4) she failed to offer any evidence to the contrary, and did not argue in her brief, that she satisfied the test for fair market value.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Schultz v. Natwick


Appeal No. 00-0361


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 281; 249 Wis. 2d 317; 638 N.W.2d 319; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1181


February 12, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
November 21, 2001, Decided  
November 21, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dunn County: ROD W. SMELTZER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 98-CV-108.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, appellant insurers challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin) that 1997 Wis. Laws 89, which increased caps on damages for loss of society and companionship in wrongful death actions, applied to the claims of respondent victims.


OVERVIEW: The insurers contended that applying the increased caps to a cause of action that accrued prior to the effective date of 1997 Wis. Laws 89 was unconstitutional under the due process clauses of the Wisconsin and United States Constitutions. The appellate court determined that the retroactive application of increased damages for loss of society and companionship in wrongful death actions violated the insurers' due process rights. Therefore, the appellate court held that the insurers' liability for loss of society and companionship was capped at $ 150,000 under Wis. Stat. § 895.04(4) (1995-1996), which was the statute in effect on the date the victims' cause of action accrued.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment.

 

1088 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Blanck


No. 01-0282-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 288; 249 Wis. 2d 364; 638 N.W.2d 910; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1198


November 21, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
November 21, 2001, Decided  
November 21, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Waukesha County: J. MAC DAVIS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions entered in the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) for false imprisonment, kidnapping, battery, and three counts of second-degree sexual assault arguing that his constitutional speedy trial and due process rights were violated by the six-year delay in charging him. He further argued that he was entitled to a new trial in the interests of justice and pursuant to the "plain error" doctrine.


OVERVIEW: In 1990 defendant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated criminal sexual assault. Defendant appealed those convictions and in 1994, the aggravated criminal sexual assault charge carrying a 60 year sentence was reversed and vacated. In 1997 a criminal complaint was filed and a warrant issued charging defendant with the offenses in the instant case in connection with the same crime for which his conviction for aggravated sexual assault had been vacated. Defendant argued that the six year lapse violated his right to speedy trial. The appellate court noted that the Sixth Amendment speedy trial right could not be violated by a prearrest delay in charging and its protection was triggered only when a criminal prosecution had begun. Moreover, defendant's speedy trial right attached only when the complaint and warrant on new and different charges was issued in 1997. Further, while defendant's due process rights may have been implicated by the precharging delay, he failed to allege or prove actual prejudice or improper motive for the delay. Finally, the evidentiary rule of "plain error" was inapplicable to an alleged constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the circuit court were affirmed.

 

1089 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


In re Samuel J.R.


No. 01-2034


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2002 WI App 1; 249 Wis. 2d 491; 639 N.W.2d 225; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1168



November 14, 2001, Decided  
November 14, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Calumet County: PATRICK L. WILLIS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parent's rights were terminated by an order of the Circuit Court for Calumet County (Wisconsin). The parent appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parent appealed the termination of his parental rights on three grounds: (1) that Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) (1999-2000) violated his substantive due process rights; (2) that the trial court erred by not making its egregiousness determination in light of a recent appellate decision; and (3) the trial court lost competency to issue a dispositional order when it failed to do so within ten days of taking evidence relating to the disposition. The appellate court held the parent waived his constitutional challenge because the issue was not raised at trial. The appellate court refrained from requiring retrospective application of the recent appellate decision to the parent's case, as it would thrust an excessive burden on the administration of justice. Also, the trial court's determination of the egregious nature of the parent's treatment of his children (including leaving them outside in the cold without clothing and placing them in a dog cage in an unheated basement) was well documented in the record. Finally, as the trial court's delay in issuing its order did not affect the parent's right to timely appeal or the children's stability, the delay did not require a reversal.


OUTCOME: The termination of parental rights was affirmed.

Berghauer v. Heyl (In re Estate of Berghauer)


No. 00-320100-3201


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2002 WI App 1; 249 Wis. 2d 488; 639 N.W.2d 223; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1156



November 13, 2001, Decided  
November 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATE, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: JOHN A. DES JARDINS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, appellants, hospital, physicians and insurers, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) entered in favor of respondents, estate.


OVERVIEW: The hospital, physicians, and insurers argued that: (1) insufficient evidence supported the jury's verdict as to cause and liability; (2) the award for loss of society and companionship was not supported by the evidence; (3) the statutory cap on loss of society and companionship awards applied; (4) the trial court erred when it admitted an alleged suicide note; and (5) the award for loss of society and companionship was excessive. The appellate court held that: (1) credible evidence supported the jury's verdict as the expert's opinion was sufficient to satisfy the burden of production so as to permit the jury to determine cause, and there was substantial evidence from which the jury might have assessed liability; (2) the child was 7 at the time of trial, and was entitled to be compensated for his loss through 18; (3) on the date of the suicide, the wrongful death cap on awards for loss of society and companionship did not apply to medical malpractice cases; (4) even if the trial court erred when it admitted the suicide note, the error was harmless; and (5) the jury's award was proper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Town of Beloit v. County of Rock


No. 00-1231


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 256; 249 Wis. 2d 88; 637 N.W.2d 71; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1100


February 26, 2001, Oral Argument  
October 25, 2001, Decided  
October 25, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Town of Beloit v. County of Rock, 2002 WI 23, 250 Wis. 2d 555, 643 N.W.2d 93, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 27 (2002)
Affirmed by Town of Beloit v. County of Rock, 2003 WI 8, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 9 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: WILLIAM D. JOHNSTON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor environmental group sought a declaratory judgment on the basis that appellant town exceeded its authority in developing a subdivision without a public purpose. The Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) denied the town's motion for summary judgment, and granted summary judgment in favor of intervenors. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The town considered and approved a preliminary plat for a subdivision. The intervenors sought a declaration that the town exceeded its authority by both preparing and approving the subdivision. The lower court concluded that the Town did not act with a public purpose in developing the land. The circuit court erred when it enjoined the town from further acting as a developer of the land. The town had statutory authority to develop the subdivision under the general powers granted to a village in Wis. Stat. § 61.34(1), (3), and (5) (1999-2000). Nothing prevented the town from assuming the dual role of subdivider and reviewer of a proposed plat. The town's actions were not prohibited by the public purpose doctrine. The town's expenditure of tax revenues to develop the land served a public purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the lower court was ordered to enter sum against the intervenors.

State v. Williams (In re Williams)


Case Nos. 00-2899 & 00-3122


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 263; 249 Wis. 2d 1; 637 N.W.2d 791; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1089


October 2, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
October 23, 2001, Decided  
October 23, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by State v. Williams (In re Williams), 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1114 (Wis. Ct. App., Oct. 23, 2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Hogan v. McCulloch, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 80174 (W.D. Wis., May 25, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DENNIS P. MORONEY and JOHN J. DiMOTTO, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendants were committed to institutional care in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) under petitions alleging that they were sexually violent predators. The defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants contended that two changes made to Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000) violated their constitutional rights to equal protection and to substantive due process. They also claimed that the changes should not be applied to them because the petitions alleging that they were sexually violent persons subject to ch. 980 commitment were filed before the effective date of the changes. They argued, inter alia, that the automatic commitment provision in Wis. Stat. § 980.06 (1999-2000), and the 18 month waiting period in Wis. Stat. § 980.08(1) (1999-2000) violated their rights to equal protection because they were treated more harshly than were similarly situated persons committed under Wis. Stat. ch. 51 (1999-2000). The court of appeals disagreed. Although Wis. Stat. ch. 51 (1999-2000) was more "lenient" than was Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000) the differences between the degree of danger posed by each of the two classes of persons, as well as the differences in what must be proven in order to commit under the two chapters, justified on a strict-scrutiny analysis the disparate, but narrowly tailored, procedures about which the defendants complained.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Williams (In re Williams)

State v. Williams (In re Williams), 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1089 (Wis. Ct. App. Oct. 23, 2001) 
State v. Williams (In re Williams), 2001 WI App 263, 249 Wis. 2d 1, 637 N.W.2d 791, 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1089 (Oct. 23, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, entered a judgment and orders committing petitioners, two inmates, to institutional care pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.06 (1999-2000). The inmates appealed, and their appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Both inmates alleged on appeal that two changes made to Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000) violated their constitutional rights to equal protection and to substantive due process. Those sections were not applied retroactively to the inmates. The court of appeals rejected one of the inmate's requests that his commitment be vacated, inasmuch as that request was predicated on his contention that application of §§ 980.06, 980.08(1) to him were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment and orders were affirmed.

State v. Dixon


No. 01-0261-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 280; 248 Wis. 2d 983; 638 N.W.2d 394; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1058



October 16, 2001, Decided  
October 16, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ELSA C. LAMELAS and CLARE L. FIORENZA, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from convictions by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin of one count of arson of a building, party to a crime, and one count of possession of a controlled substance, as well as from the circuit court's denial of her motion to suppress and her motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant complained that: (1) she was denied her constitutional right to confront the witnesses against her; (2) her trial counsel was ineffective; (3) the search warrant affidavit was insufficient to support a finding of probable cause; and (4) the search warrant did not authorize the seizure of two safes from her residence. The appellate court concluded that allowing the testimony of two witnesses who had testified at the preliminary hearing but were unavailable at trial, even if error, was not prejudicial because the evidence was duplicative. It held that defendant had failed to establish that she was prejudiced by counsel's decisions not to call an insurance adjuster and not to cross examine a witness about an immunity agreement she had with the state. The court concluded that the search warrant affidavit set forth sufficient facts to support a finding of probable cause, even absent the paragraph which failed to establish the police detective's basis for his knowledge of insurance coverage. Finally, the police were justified in seizing the safes pursuant to the warrant because they were plausible repositories for financial records, located on the named premise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, the denial the of the motion to suppress and the denial of the motion for postconviction relief.

State v. Tinder


No. 01-0689-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 280; 248 Wis. 2d 984; 638 N.W.2d 394; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1050



October 11, 2001, Decided  
October 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock County: DANIEL T. DILLON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Rock County (Wisconsin), which denied the defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his blood alcohol content, and convicted the defendant for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the defendant challenged the trial court's dismissal of his motions to suppress evidence of his blood alcohol content. The defendant argued that the seizure of his blood was unconstitutional because Wis. Stat. § 343.305 violated U.S. Const. amend IV. The appellate court found that the defendant failed to properly notify the attorney general of his constitutional challenge, and therefore did not preserve the issue for review. Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11) required that when a constitutional challenge to a statute was made, the attorney general must be served with a copy of the proceeding and be entitled to be heard. Failure to do so precluded the defendant from challenging the validity of the statute. The defendant moved to supplement the record with a copy of a letter to the attorney general sent when he filed his trial motions. The court denied the motion to supplement the record, and held that his constitutional challenged was waived even if the motion would have been granted, because none of the trial motions to suppress would have notified the attorney general that the defendant was asserting the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Milwaukee v. Burnette


Case No.: 00-2308


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 258; 248 Wis. 2d 820; 637 N.W.2d 447; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1041


September 4, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
October 9, 2001, Decided  
October 9, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order for judgment, an order for final permanent injunction, and a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellee city sought an injunction against the appellant prostitutes in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) enjoining them from prostitution related activities in the city. The court granted the city's motion for summary judgment and the prostitutes appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held as an initial finding that the trial court had the authority to issue an injunction to abate the prostitute's role in what the undisputed evidentiary submissions proved was a public nuisance. The prostitutes argued, inter alia, that: (1) the parts of the injunction that prohibited loitering in the doorways of the private property of others was unconstitutionally vague; and (2) the parts of the injunction that imposed a twenty-five foot no-intrusion radius from any other person who might have been violating any provisions of the injunction were unconstitutionally vague. The court of appeals held that: (1) there was nothing vague about the injunction's prohibition against loitering in doorways, or sitting on private residential property without the permission of the property owner; the prohibitions were clear and easy to obey; and (2) that provision did not give the prostitutes fair warning of prohibited conduct, there was nothing in the record that indicated that any of the prostitutes were sufficiently familiar with all those subject to the injunction so that compliance with this provision would not have been a haphazard, guessing adventure.


OUTCOME: The injunction was affirmed as to all provisions except those enjoining the prostitutes from being within 25 feet of other prostitutes, and from associating with passersby, and the case was remanded.

Schultz v. Sykes, 248 Wis. 2d 746, 638 N.W.2d 604, 2001 WI App 255, 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1020 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant creditor was awarded attorney fees and cost, as a result of the dismissal of plaintiff wife's defamation action against it. The creditor sought garnishment proceedings against the wife's husband. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) ordered 50 percent of the husband's wages subject to garnishment. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife had no assets, and therefore, the creditor sought wage garnishment against the husband. The husband argued that his wages should be exempt from garnishment because he and his wife had a marital property agreement that classified his wages as individual property. Since the husband's wages were classified as individual property, he claimed that they could not be used to satisfy a judgment against his wife. The creditor asserted that the marital agreement was not binding in this case because it had no notice of the agreement. The court agreed with the creditor, and determined that since the creditor had no notice of the agreement, the marital property agreement was not binding. The husband also argued that the garnishment violated several of his constitutional rights, however, the court refused to make such a finding.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Myartt

NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Myartt, 2002 WI 2, 249 Wis. 2d 582, 638 N.W.2d 591, 2001 Wisc. LEXIS 1711 (2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Myartt, 2007 WI App 130, 301 Wis. 2d 748, 731 N.W.2d 383, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 201 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Myartt, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 361 (Wis. Ct. App., May 14, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) entered after a jury found him guilty of one count of robbery with use of force, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.32(1)(a) (1997-98).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress based on an illegal stop, claiming his Fourth Amendment rights were violated when the police stopped and searched him because the suspect's description only generally matched his appearance. The appellate court found that, under the totality of the circumstances, the officers were justified to conduct an investigatory stop because: (1) out of 10 facts describing the suspect, four of the facts matched defendant exactly; and (2) only three of the ten descriptive facts did not match at all. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred when it refused to grant his motion for mistrial based on a dissenting juror. The appellate court held that the trial court properly denied the mistrial motion because: (1) the verdict was received in open court and announced, but polling had not been completed and judgment had not been entered, so the verdict had not been accepted by the trial court when the dissenting juror spoke; and (2) the individual voir dire was recorded and consisted solely of the trial court asking the juror whether she voted guilty back in the deliberation room.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Bullard


No. 01-3264-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 280; 248 Wis. 2d 982; 638 N.W.2d 393; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1007



October 2, 2001, Decided  
October 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: BENJAMIN D. PROCTOR, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant on eight drug charges involving primarily marijuana, and denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed (1) part of the amended information should have been dismissed because there was no preliminary hearing; (2) two counts were multiplicitous; (3) he was denied effective assistance of counsel; (4) the trial court erred by allowing inadmissible hearsay; and (5) insufficient evidence supported the identity and quantities of marijuana. The appellate court held: (1) by failing to object to the information, defendant was barred by waiver and judicial estoppel from raising it on appeal; (2) the two counts related to defendant's activities on a single day, but they charged two distinct acts: his actual delivery of marijuana to one witness and his continued possession of residual marijuana for later delivery so they were not multiplicitous; (3) counsel acted reasonably, and the alleged omissions were strategic decisions or involved meritless positions; (4) in light of other evidence, the admission of hearsay would have been harmless error; and (5) the evidence, including lay opinion that the substance was marijuana, was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lisney


00-2870-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 254; 248 Wis. 2d 527; 635 N.W.2d 905; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 908



September 6, 2001, Decided  
September 6, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Richland County: MICHAEL KIRCHMAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Richland County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of disorderly conduct while using a dangerous weapon, a violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 939.63(1)(a), 939.22(10) (1995-96). Defendant moved for postconviction relief, which the trial court denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed his right to a fair trial was violated because of prosecutorial misconduct, ineffective assistance of counsel, and the denial of his request to exclude the victim from the trial. The appellate court held: (1) the prosecutor's questions regarding a conversation between defendant and a witness were based upon existing evidence, and were not prohibited; (2) although the prosecutor repeatedly stated in his closing argument that he believed the victim was telling the truth, he also immediately qualified his opinion with the statement that his opinion stemmed from the evidence; (3) statements defendant claimed the State did not disclose were found in a transcript of an interview provided to defendant before trial; (4) defendant did not notify the attorney general of his constitutional challenge to the statute permitting the presence of the victim, so the issue was not addressed; and (5) trial counsel was not ineffective because his decision to refrain from objecting to the prosecutor's statements was not deficient performance, and he exercised his judgment adequately regarding instructions.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

State ex rel. Richards v. Smith


No. 00-3492


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 254; 248 Wis. 2d 528; 635 N.W.2d 906; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 918



September 6, 2001, Decided  
September 6, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PAUL B. HIGGINBOTHAM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) affirming a decision by respondent parole commission to deny him discretionary parole.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner argued that the commission: (1) acted arbitrarily and in violation of his due process rights by denying parole on the record before him; (2) violated his double jeopardy protection by partly basing parole denial on the prior manslaughter conviction; and (3) should have ordered a pre-parole investigation report to verify the information he presented. The appellate court held that the circuit court did not err because: (1) it was neither arbitrary nor unreasonable to conclude that a first-degree murder committed by a repeat offender, with a prior manslaughter conviction, was unduly depreciated by release after 15 years on a life sentence; (2) parole revocation was not deemed punishment for double jeopardy purposes; and (3) the reports were not required by statute or parole commission rules, and the prisoner was not denied parole because of a lack of verification of the information he provided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Reinhard


No. 01-0767-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 254; 248 Wis. 2d 528; 635 N.W.2d 906; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 904



September 5, 2001, Decided  
September 5, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MICHAEL O. BOHREN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) convicting him of a second offense operating while under the influence of an intoxicant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the guilty-plea-waiver rule did not apply because his constitutional challenges focused on the authority, capacity, power, and right by which the lower court compelled him to come before it and whether the trial court could hear and determine the controversy and pronounce sentence. The appellate court concluded that the guilty-plea-waiver rule applied because: (1) defendant could not avoid the guilty-plea-waiver rule by entering a "conditional plea" and reserving the right to appeal; (2) defendant's challenge to the application of the statute did not call into question the subject matter jurisdiction of the trial court; (3) despite the labels defendant attached to the issues, he did not challenge the ability of respondent State to convict him of OWI-he only challenged the ability of the State to seek the imposition of criminal penalties; (4) defendant's guilty plea was voluntary and intelligent; and (5) the appellate court declined to exercise its discretion and relieve defendant of the effect of the guilty-plea-waiver rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Earls


No. 00-2303-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 254; 248 Wis. 2d 526; 635 N.W.2d 905; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 891



September 5, 2001, Decided  
September 5, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Earls, 2002 WI 2, 249 Wis. 2d 581, 638 N.W.2d 590, 2001 Wisc. LEXIS 1650 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Remanded by Earls v. McCaughtry, 379 F.3d 489, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 16735 (7th Cir. Wis., 2004)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Earls, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 266 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 8, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: DALE L. ENGLISH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin) convicting him of sexual assault of a child. Defendant also appealed the trial court's denial of his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) the State presented improper opinion evidence; (2) the trial court erred in admitting videotaped evidence of interview of victim; and (3) the jury instructions which incorporated a stipulation between him and the State were improper. The appellate court held that to the extent there were any errors in the trial, those errors did not shake its confidence in the fairness or outcome of the trial because: (1) defendant could not establish that his counsel was ineffective as he was not prejudiced by any error of trial counsel not objecting to opinion testimony, and the evidence supporting the victim's truthfulness was properly admitted; (2) the videotaped evidence was properly admitted as residual hearsay, and the evidence should not have been excluded as cumulative; and (3) because the stipulation was part of a reasonable strategic decision, and the instruction was based on that stipulation, trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to object.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

 

1104 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Collette


No. 01-0505


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 224; 247 Wis. 2d 992; 635 N.W.2d 28; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 869



August 29, 2001, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Racine County: GERALD P. PTACEK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a pro se postconviction motion alleging that his postconviction counsel was ineffective, the sentencing violated double jeopardy, and the plea agreement was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) denied the petition, and this appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with battery to a law enforcement officer and disorderly conduct. He entered a plea to the second charge. He argued that his postconviction counsel was ineffective for failing to raise the claim that he was pressured him into accepting the plea agreement. The plea bargaining process was not unconstitutional. The trial court was not required to hold an evidentiary hearing on defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of postconviction counsel. Defendant's motion offered no details regarding the alleged pressure applied by his counsel to accept the plea. Defendant failed to provide a transcript of the hearing on his pro se postconviction motion. The trial court's plea colloquy with defendant was thorough and exhaustive. Defendant's claim that the trial court violated his protection against double jeopardy was rejected. Defendant was not punished for battery. He received a single punishment for a single offense, disorderly conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying defendant's pro se petition for postconviction relief was affirmed.

State v. Tutor


No. 01-0602-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 224; 247 Wis. 2d 992; 635 N.W.2d 28; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 867



August 28, 2001, Decided  
August 28, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Bayfield County: THOMAS J. GALLAGHER, Judge. Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pleaded guilty to one count of possession of an untagged deer carcass in the Circuit Court for Bayfield County (Wisconsin). After sentencing, the defendant filed a post-conviction motion seeking to withdraw his guilty plea. The court denied the motion and the defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued that his guilty plea was involuntary. The court of appeals held that because the trial court never made findings of fact about whether the defendant misapprehended what the effect of a guilty plea would have on his right to appeal an evidentiary issue, it had to remand the case for such a finding because it was not in a position to make findings of fact or credibility determinations. The court of appeals further held that if the trial court found that the defendant entered his plea believing he could appeal the trial court ruling on the State's motion in limine, and that he would have insisted upon a trial had he not been misinformed, then he had to be afforded the opportunity to withdraw his plea and have a trial. If the trial court did not make both findings, then the conviction had to stand.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for a determination of whether the defendant's guilty plea was voluntary.

State v. Gray


No. 00-3017-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 224; 247 Wis. 2d 990; 635 N.W.2d 27; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 836



August 21, 2001, Decided  
August 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, and unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ELSA C. LAMELAS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of first-degree reckless homicide while using a dangerous weapon, and recklessly endangering safety while using a dangerous weapon in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred because: (1) it admitted prejudicial character evidence concerning prior incidents the defendant had been involved in; and (2) it denied him a hearing on the alleged ineffectiveness of his counsel. The court of appeals held that the trial court had not erred because: (1) it received all four incidents into evidence, found that the evidence served a variety of permissible purposes by proving the defendant's motive, his identity as one of the shooters, and his preparation or plan to commit the shooting, and by putting the crime in its proper context; the trial court had also concluded that the evidence was extremely relevant to the present murder, and that the high probative value was not substantially outweighed by the potential danger of unfair prejudice; (2) the defendant's counsel was not ineffective because the court properly gave the standard instructions regarding the credibility of witnesses, the weight of evidence, and the state's burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt, therefore, trial counsel's performance was not deficient because an accomplice jury instruction was not necessary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1107 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


No. 00-2546-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 206; 247 Wis. 2d 734; 634 N.W.2d 844; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 849



August 21, 2001, Decided  
August 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MARTIN J. DONALD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) entered a judgment of conviction after defendant pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance (marijuana) with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed, challenging the denial of his suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: Police officers approached defendant in an alley, and he fled into his mother's house. The police pursued him and discovered marijuana on his person. The police officer's warrantless entry into the home was unconstitutional. The State failed to overcome the presumption that the search was unreasonable. There was no evidence that the officers had reason to believe that defendant was a drug dealer or user, and there was no evidence that the officers saw any illegal drugs. The State could not rely on the hot pursuit exception, because there was nothing in the record to indicate that defendant was a suspect being chased from the scene of a crime. The officers did not have probable cause to believe any offense had been committed, and exigent circumstances to support the warrantless entry were not present.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to enter an order granting defendant's suppression motion.

State v. Carpenter (In re Carpenter)


No. 99-1383


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 224; 247 Wis. 2d 993; 635 N.W.2d 28; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 829



August 16, 2001, Decided  
August 16, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Shawano County: EARL SCHMIDT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Shawano County, Wisconsin, committed defendant as a sexually violent person and denied his post-commitment motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the State failed to prove he was within 90 days of release when the petition of commitment was filed. The State was required to prove that element, and that a remand for an evidentiary hearing would not violate defendant's right to be free from double jeopardy. Defendant argued that Wis. Stat. §§ 980.01(7), 980.02(2)(c) (1999-2000), were unconstitutional because they were vague as applied. Defendant did not offer any case law that supported a change in the usual procedure for creating jury instructions. The appellate court declined to remove the burden of requesting the instruction from the party who would benefit from it. A reasonable attorney, comparing the statutory term and the judicial definition, could conclude that the judicial definition would not make a significant difference in the outcome. The exclusion of testimony of one of defendant's experts was harmless. The partial answer was not stricken; the probative value of the parole discussion was modest, because parole supervision would presumably end at some point. Defendant's substantial rights were not affected by the trial court denying his request to strike a juror for cause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the vacating of the commitment judgment and affirmed as to all other issues.

State v. Tomlinson


No. 00-3134-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 212; 247 Wis. 2d 682; 635 N.W.2d 201; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 813


July 3, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
August 14, 2001, Decided  
August 14, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Tomlinson, 2002 WI 2, 249 Wis. 2d 579, 638 N.W.2d 589, 2001 Wisc. LEXIS 1619 (2001)
Affirmed by State v. Tomlinson, 2002 WI 91, 254 Wis. 2d 502, 648 N.W.2d 367, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 494 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Tomlinson, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 11 (Wis. Ct. App., Jan. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) of first-degree reckless homicide. He appealed the conviction as well as the denial of his postconviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of killing a man with a baseball bat. He sought to suppress evidence seized at the time of his arrest. The trial court did not err in finding that the entry was consensual. Defendant's teenage daughter allowed the detective to enter while defendant stood nearby. The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it allowed the State to read into evidence a witness's prior testimony under Wis. Stat. § 908.045(1) (1999-2000). The witness persistently refused to answer questions, and defendant's confrontation rights were not violated. The trial court instructed the jury that a dangerous weapon meant a baseball bat. Defendant approved of the instruction. Trial counsel's failure to object to the instruction was not prejudicial as there was no reasonable probability that the jurors would not have found the baseball bat to be a dangerous weapon.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

State v. Love


No. 99-2831-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 224; 247 Wis. 2d 993; 635 N.W.2d 28; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 801



August 7, 2001, Decided  
August 7, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, second or subsequent offense, as a party to a crime, and possession of cocaine without the tax stamp, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 961.41(1m)(cm)4, 961.48, 939.05, 139.89 (1997-98). Defendant also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car, when the police stopped the car for having an obstructed view. The driver consented to a vehicle search, and the police found a digital scale with white residue, sandwich bags, cell phones, and $ 65. Defendant consented to a search of his person and police found a plastic baggie containing a 40-gram chunk of cocaine. The evidence differed on what exactly hung from the rear view mirror, but there was no conflict that something did. The appellate court found that: (1) defendant failed to show prejudice from ineffective assistance of counsel because the trial court's decision to deny the motion to suppress could not have been changed; (2) the exclusion of the testimony of the driver was error, but it was harmless error because of the overwhelming evidence of guilt; and (3) the convictions did not violate double jeopardy because possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver was not a lesser-included offense of a tax stamp violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order of the circuit court were affirmed.

State v. Ransdell


No. 00-2224


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 202; 247 Wis. 2d 613; 634 N.W.2d 871; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 797


July 3, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
August 7, 2001, Decided  
August 7, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DANIEL KONKOL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, which found respondent to be a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000), and committed him to institutional care pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.06 (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Respondent's sole claim on appeal was that Wis. Stat. § 980.06 (1999-2000) deprived him of substantive due process because it, unlike its predecessor provision, required an automatic initial commitment to institutional care. The appellate court found that respondent was not deprived of substantive due process because: (1) there were compelling State interests to protect the community from the dangerously mentally disordered, and to provide care and treatment to those with mental disorders that predisposed them to sexual violence; (2) that there were many safeguards against arbitrary confinement in Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000); and (3) respondent failed to carry his burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that Wis. Stat. § 980.06 (1999-2000) violated due process.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment and order were affirmed.

Alexander v. City of Madison


No. 00-2692


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 208; 247 Wis. 2d 576; 634 N.W.2d 577; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 985


May 4, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
August 2, 2001, Decided  
August 2, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant liquor license applicant filed suit against the appellee city arguing that city ordinances regulating liquor licenses were unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted the city's motion for summary judgment and the applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued that: (1) the benefits to the public were too indirect and remote to support the common council's action under the public purpose doctrine because the city had not shown that the recipients of the reserve class B licenses would not have opened facilities serving liquor anyway; and (2) the city had not created reasonable regulations for control and accountability. The court of appeals held that: (1) he offered no support for his assertion that the same people would have applied for and received the licenses even without the ordinances, yet, it was his burden to provide such proof; a bald assertion such as was made was insufficient to demonstrate that it was clear that no public purpose would be served; and (2) the regulations controlling the application for a reserve class B liquor license were inextricably tied to the application for the economic development grant and provided sufficient control and accountability to ensure that the public purposes outlined in the ordinances had a reasonable probability of being met.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Splitt


No. 00-2608-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 224; 247 Wis. 2d 989; 635 N.W.2d 26; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1359



August 1, 2001, Decided  
August 1, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY TO BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Walworth County: JOHN R. RACE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial in the Circuit Court for Walworth County, Wisconsin, of one count of sexual contact with a child, as a persistent repeat offender, and one count of repeated acts of sexual contact with a child. The prior offense used to establish his repeat offender status was under the statute of another state. Defendant appealed from the conviction and from the order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court concluded that counsel's failure to object to: the reading of a transcript of an interview that defendant had with the police; a comment made by the prosecutor about defense objections to "other acts " evidence; and to prosecutor's closing argument, were reasonable trial strategy and did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel. It held that, although the prosecutor's closing remarks suggested to the jury that, if it did not convict the defendant he would assault an other child, the remarks, though offensive, did not violate the defendant's right to a fair trial. It noted that the Wisconsin Supreme Court recently decided that under similar circumstance the repeat offender statute was constitutional. Finally, the appellate court held that the repeat offender penalty enhancer was properly applied based on a conviction under a comparable statute from another state. The foreign statute penalized sexual contact with a person who was 16 years old, while Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2) (1999-2000) did not.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief were affirmed.

State v. Wodenjak


No.00-3419-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 216; 247 Wis. 2d 554; 634 N.W.2d 867; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 986


June 26, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
August 1, 2001, Decided  
August 1, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Winnebago County: WILLIAM H. CARVER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant entered a no contest plea to operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) in the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) after the trial court denied his motion to suppress the results of his blood alcohol test. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the defendant was arrested, the officer asked him to submit to a blood alcohol test. The defendant requested a breath test instead. The officer informed him that since he was a repeat offender, the test must be a blood test. The defendant then consented to a blood test. The defendant argued that there was no exigency under the Fourth Amendment permitting the police to perform a blood test because he had previously offered to submit to a breath test. The court of appeals held that the dissipation of alcohol from a person's blood stream constituted a sufficient exigency to justify a forcible, warrantless blood draw. Therefore, the defendant's request for the less invasive breath test and the availability of such a test did not deprive the officer of his authority to obtain a blood sample from the defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dahl


No. 01-0489-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 197; 247 Wis. 2d 499; 633 N.W.2d 279; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 759



July 26, 2001, Decided  
July 26, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL, ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Rock County: MICHAEL J. BYRON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating a motor vehicle under the influence of an intoxicant. Defendant also appealed the circuit court's order denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle under the influence of an intoxicant. The arresting officer read the "Informing the Accused" form to defendant in compliance with Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4). Defendant submitted to a blood draw, and the sample was sent to the Wisconsin State Hygiene Lab for testing. Defendant contended that Wis. Stat. § 343.305, Wisconsin's Implied Consent Law, was unconstitutional under the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution, and that testing blood drawn in compliance with the Implied Consent Law was a separate search, requiring a warrant. The appellate court decline to address the constitutional challenge to the statute because the record did not show that defendant notified the attorney general of his constitutional challenge to the statute. In addition, the court held that the analysis of blood lawfully seized by the State did not constitute a separate search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

 

1116 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tate


No. 99-2948-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 197; 247 Wis. 2d 500; 633 N.W.2d 279; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 764



July 25, 2001, Decided  
July 25, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL, ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Washington County: ANNETTE K. ZIEGLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Washington County, Wisconsin, which convicted him of repeated sexual assault of the same child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.025(1) (1997-98), and from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexually assaulting his former stepdaughter on three or more occasions over a period of three years. The victim made the allegations against defendant only after defendant and the victim's mother were divorced. The defense theory was that the victim's mother manipulated the victim to make the sexual assault allegations. The trial court limited the extent of cross-examination of the victim's mother. The appellate court found that: (1) the complaint was adequate to give the defendant notice of the crimes; (2) the unanimity requirement in Wis. Stat. 948.025 (1997-98) was satisfied where multiple acts constituted one continuous course of conduct; (3) trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the complaint and raising the issue of unanimity because those issues were invalid; (4) § 948.025 was not unconstitutional on unanimous verdict or due process grounds; and (5) the trial court did not err in limiting the scope of cross-examination because there was a reasonable basis for its decision that it would divert the trial to extraneous matters.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and order of the circuit court were affirmed.

State v. Spencer


No. 00-3117-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 197; 247 Wis. 2d 498; 633 N.W.2d 278; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 720



July 17, 2001, Decided  
July 17, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL, ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY BRENNAN and MICHAEL B. BRENNAN, Judges. 1


1  Judge Kitty Brennan presided over the jury trial and heard a portion of the postconviction motion. Judge Michael Brennan (no relation) conducted a hearing on the remaining claims following remand by this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting him of carrying a concealed weapon while masked, as party to a crime; disorderly conduct while armed and masked, as party to a crime; and obstructing an officer while masked, as party to a crime. Defendant also challenged the trial court's order denying his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his attorney was ineffective for failing to object: (1) to a six-person jury; and (2) on confrontational and hearsay grounds, to the admission of the co-defendant's inculpatory statement, in which the co-defendant admitted concealing a gun on his person, through the testimony of an officer. The appellate court held that defendant did not meet his burden of proof on either claim because: (1) defendant failed to prove that his counsel's alleged deficient performance in failing to object to a six-person jury prejudiced him; and (2) the failure to object to the admission of the co-defendant's inculpatory statement was reasonable trial strategy as it was reasonable to believe that the jury might have exonerated defendant after hearing that another person confessed to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

State v. Howell


No. 00-1879-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 197; 247 Wis. 2d 496; 633 N.W.2d 277; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 723



July 17, 2001, Decided  
July 17, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL, ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ELSA C. LAMELAS, Judge. 1


1 Judge Laurence C. Gram presided over Howell's motion to suppress; Judge Lamelas presided over the entry of Howell's guilty plea.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence which was denied, and the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, entered a judgment of conviction after he pled guilty to one count of felon in possession of a firearm in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.29(2)(a) (1999-2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: There was conflicting testimony about whether the police initially used the landlord to unlock the back door, and whether defendant later consented to a search of his apartment. The defendant admitted that he allowed the police to enter his apartment, but he denied giving the officers permission to search. The record revealed no evidence of duress or coercion, misrepresentation or trickery by the police to entice defendant to consent. The appellate court found that: (1) the attempted entry into defendant's apartment violated his Fourth Amendment rights; (2) the trial court's finding that the defendant voluntarily consented to the search was not clearly erroneous; and (3) the trial court's finding that defendant's consent was sufficiently attenuated from the illegal attempted entry was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the motion to suppress evidence and the subsequent conviction were affirmed.
