Shorewood Hills v. McGrew


No. 00-3550


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 166; 246 Wis. 2d 990; 632 N.W.2d 125; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 673



June 28, 2001, Decided  
June 28, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY TO BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) which denied defendant's request for a jury trial pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 756.06(2)(c) (1999-2000) and convicted defendant for a municipal speeding citation.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a 12-person jury trial. Defendant argued that Wis. Const. art. I, § 5, provided a constitutional right to a 12-person jury trial; therefore defendant's six-person jury pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 756.06(2)(c) (1999-2000) was unconstitutional. The court rejected defendant's contentions. The court held that there was no constitutional right to a jury trial in case involving municipal ordinances. Defendant had a statutory right to a jury trial under § 756.06(2)(c), which only provided for a six-person jury. Because defendant had a six-person jury, the court stated that he had nothing to complain about in this regard. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the statute was unconstitutionally vague, because notice of a duty or of prohibited conduct was not an issue in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock County: DANIEL T. DILLON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of placing signs in a public way in violation of Beloit, Wis., Ordinances § 30.16. The Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff city. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: City issued two citations after defendant placed yellow ribbons on poles in support of troops in the Kosovo conflict. The ribbons were signs within the meaning of the Beloit, Wis., Ordinances § 30.03(1), and summary judgement was appropriate. Defendant did not present evidence of either selective enforcement or viewpoint discrimination that would have entitled her to a trial. Even if the yellow ribbons were not animated signs, they came within the general definition of sign and were not permitted on the poles. Defendant did not show intentional, systematic, and arbitrary discrimination.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment entered in favor of city was affirmed and the citations issued against defendant were upheld.

Bishop v. City of Burlington


No. 00-2346


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 154; 246 Wis. 2d 879; 631 N.W.2d 656; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 664


April 20, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
June 27, 2001, Decided  
June 27, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine County: RICHARD J. KREUL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sued defendant city and defendant private citizen to avoid the conveyance of a parking lot from the city to the private citizen. The Circuit Court for Racine County, Wisconsin, rendered judgment in favor of the city. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The purpose of the sale was to promote the rehabilitation of the downtown area. As a condition precedent to the sale of the parking lot, the private citizen was obligated to rehabilitate both the facade and first floor of a building, to close an entrance to the lot to improve vehicular traffic in the downtown area, and to convey a riverfront parcel of land to the city which allowed the city to construct a riverfront walkway plaza. The taxpayers made no claims of fraud. The appellate court found that: (1) the city established that the sale of the parking lot served the legitimate public purpose of revitalizing the downtown area, (2) the city did not misuse its discretion because the private citizen's obligations and the benefits flowing to the city sufficed for consideration, and (3) taxpayers waived their other issues on appeal by not raising them sufficiently in the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Porter


No. 00-2304-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 166; 246 Wis. 2d 989; 632 N.W.2d 124; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 630



June 19, 2001, Decided  
June 19, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY TO BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: M. JOSEPH DONALD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of keeping or maintaining a drug house, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 961.42(1) (1999-2000). Defendant also appealed from an order denying her request for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) she did not voluntarily consent to the warrantless entry into and subsequent search of her home by police, and the trial court erred in denying her motion to suppress the evidence seized from the house; (2) § 961.42 was unconstitutionally vague, ambiguous, and overbroad; and (3) the complaint did not set forth sufficient facts to support defendant's guilty plea. The instant court concluded that the record supported the trial court's determination that defendant voluntarily consented to both the officers' entry into and subsequent search of her residence, and that her consent was not the result of police coercion. While defendant reluctantly consented to the entry into her home, she did not specifically identify what was said or done by the officers to constitute illegal police coercion in connection with the entry. Defendant failed to prove that § 961.42 was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt. The complaint also provided a sufficient factual basis to support defendant's guilty plea.


OUTCOME: Judgment and order were affirmed.

 

1124 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Reisch v. Schwarz


No. 00-0696


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 166; 246 Wis. 2d 987; 632 N.W.2d 123; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 610



June 14, 2001, Decided  
June 14, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY TO BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOSEPH E. SCHULTZ, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner appealed an order of the Dodge County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which dismissed his petition for writ of certiorari challenging the revocation of his parole as untimely filed under the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA).


OVERVIEW: Prisoner argued that the PLRA violated his right to equal protection because it required prisoners in Wisconsin to file petitions for certiorari review within 45 days, but did not require those incarcerated outside of Wisconsin to file within this truncated deadline. Prisoner also contended that the PLRA violated his right to substantive due process. The instant court rejected prisoner's arguments. Regarding equal protection, there was a rational basis for distinguishing between in-state and out-of-state prisoners for purposes of filing deadlines under the PLRA. In-state and out-of-state prisoners were not identically situated because out-of-state prisoners needed more time than in-state prisoners to prepare legal documents. Regarding substantive due process, the instant court noted that the purpose of the PLRA was to restrict frivolous lawsuits and to limit broadly prisoner litigation at taxpayers' expense. The abbreviated deadlines of the PLRA had a reasonable and rational relationship to the goal of limiting prisoner litigation. Thus, the PLRA's filing deadlines did not violate prisoner's right to substantive due process.


OUTCOME: Trial court's order dismissing prisioner's petition for writ of certiorari was affirmed.

 

1125 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ramirez


No.00-2605-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 158; 246 Wis. 2d 802; 633 N.W.2d 656; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 618


May 11, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
June 13, 2001, Decided  
June 13, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: JAMES L. CARLSON, 1 Judge.


1 Although Judge James L. Carlson entered the judgment of conviction, Judge John R. Race made the substantive ruling which we review on this appeal. Therefore, when we allude to the trial court we are referring to Judge Race.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin) convicting him for misappropriating the personal identifying information of another pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 943.201(2) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that § 943.201(2), as applied in the case, represented an unconstitutional ex post facto law. Rejecting defendant's argument, the appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction. Defendant had obtained money in the form of wages as the result of his unauthorized use of another's personal identifying information. This constituted a thing of value within the meaning of § 943.201(2). Also, § 943.201(2) created a continuing offense. Thus, since defendant's identity theft allowed him to obtain wages after the effective date of § 943.201(2), the application of the statute did not violate constitutional ex post facto provisions.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. Since defendant's theft of identity allowed him to obtain wages after the effective date of the applicable statutory provision, which created a continuing offense, the application of that provision did not violate constitutional guarantees against ex post facto laws.

State v. Multaler


No. 00-1846-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 149; 246 Wis. 2d 752; 632 N.W.2d 89; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 602


April 4, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
June 12, 2001, Decided  
June 12, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting him pursuant to his no contest pleas and sentencing him for 28 counts of possession of child pornography, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.12 (1997-98).


OVERVIEW: The search of defendant's property which revealed the incriminating evidence took place pursuant to a search warrant authorizing a search of the property for evidence in the cases of four apparent child murders. Defendant alleged that the affidavit in support of that warrant application was not based on the requisite probable cause. Defendant also alleged that the multiple counts were multiplicitous and, therefore, that his convictions violated his double jeopardy rights. Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The affidavit related both direct and circumstantial evidence which provided solid support for the search of defendant's property. Also, the affiant's research, expertise, and reasonable inferences provided substantial support for the probable cause determination that, despite the passage of many years between the deaths and the search warrant, evidence of the apparent murders remained at defendant's residence. The multiple counts were different in fact and the legislature, via § 948.12, intended to allow multiple punishments for multiple offenses of possession of child pornography, such that the multiple counts were not multiplicitous.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed. Multiple counts charging defendant with possession of child pornography were not multiplicitous because they were different in fact and the legislature had intended to allow multiple punishments for multiple offenses of possession of child pornography.

Gilbert v. Wis. Dep't of Revenue


No. 00-2154


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 153; 246 Wis. 2d 734; 633 N.W.2d 218; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 590


April 6, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
June 6, 2001, Decided  
June 6, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: JAMES R. KIEFFER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer paid a tax assessment in 1993 based upon a tax on controlled substances under Wis. Stat. §§ 139.87-.96 (1995-96). The statute was declared unconstitutional in 1997. In 1997 taxpayer requested a refund. Respondent taxing authority denied taxpayer's claim as untimely, and the tax appeals commission also denied the claim. The Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, reversed. Respondent taxing authority appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer did not seek a refund until after the statute was declared unconstitutional and after the two-year statute of limitations had run. The taxing authority denied taxpayer's claim for refund and dismissed taxpayer's petition for rehearing based on the statute of limitations. The circuit court reversed the taxing authority's order finding that the tax assessment was void ab initio and that the time limitations in Wis. Stat. § 71.75 were therefore inapplicable to taxpayer's refund claim. The appellate court found that: (1) taxpayer's refund claim was untimely because it was not made within the required two-year period, (2) the legislature made compliance with the statute of limitations mandatory, because it was the only method for the filing and review of claims for tax refunds, and (3) the circuit court improperly reversed the taxing authority's ruling.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's decision was reversed.

State v. Farrell


No. 01-0205-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 146; 246 Wis. 2d 672; 630 N.W.2d 277; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 558



May 31, 2001, Decided  
May 31, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: C. WILLIAM FOUST, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied the appellant's motion to suppress the results of his blood test, and convicted the appellant for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OMVWI), in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the appellant claimed that because a breath test was available, the police blood test of him was an unreasonable search and seizure. The court rejected the appellant's contentions. It was uncontested that the blood draw was taken to obtain evidence of intoxication from the appellant, who was lawfully arrested for a drunk driving-related violation. There was also a clear indication that the blood draw would produce evidence of intoxication, based upon the appellant's inability to control his automobile, his stumbling and inability to walk, his strong odor of intoxicants, his admission of alcohol consumption, and his extremely slurred speech. It was uncontested that the blood draw was done in a reasonable manner and that the appellant consented to having blood drawn without objection. Accordingly, the court concluded that the blood draw at issue in this case was not a violation of the appellant's Fourth Amendment rights, and therefore affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Storlie


Nos. 00-1315-CR, 00-2047-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 146; 246 Wis. 2d 669; 630 N.W.2d 275; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 551



May 24, 2001, Decided  
May 24, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLANTE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of injury by intoxicated use of a vehicle, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(a) (1999-2000). He claimed the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) erred in instructing the jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant drove a car involved in an accident which resulted in injuries to his passenger. He argued that the passenger's assault on him, and not his own intoxication or operation of the vehicle, caused the passenger's injuries. He claimed the trial court deprived him of his defense by instructing the jury on the affirmative defense provided under § 940.25(2) (1999-2000). The instructions accurately described the elements of the offense and the State's burden of proof. Appellant raised the affirmative defense under Wis. Stat. § 940.25(2) (1999-2000), despite his disavowals. The trial court did not deprive appellant of his defense. There was no reasonable likelihood that the instructions misled the jury into thinking it could not consider the passenger's conduct in deciding whether the State had proven that appellant's operation of his vehicle caused great bodily harm to the passenger.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The trial court did not err in instructing the jury. The instructions accurately stated the law, and the trial court did not erroneously exercise its discretion in giving them. There was not a reasonable likelihood that the jury was misled.

1132 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Griffin v. Milwaukee Transp. Servs.


No. 00-0861


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 125; 246 Wis. 2d 433; 630 N.W.2d 536; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 501


February 8, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
May 15, 2001, Decided  
May 15, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CHARLES F. KAHN, JR., Judge. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CHARLES F. KAHN, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bus company filed a summary judgment motion seeking dismissal of appellee passenger and her spouse's negligence suit because it was not commenced within six-months of the date the bus company denied the passenger's claim, as required by Wis. Stat. § 893.80(1g). It sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that denied its motion because it found § 893.80(1g) to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The passenger's attorney sent the bus company a notice of injury and claim for damages arising out of an accident. The company sent a notice disallowing the claim. The passenger and her spouse sued the company over 10 months after the company's notice was served. It sought summary judgment because suit was not filed within six months of the date of its notice under Wis. Stat. § 893.80(1g). The trial court denied the motion, finding that § 893.80(1g) violated the Equal Protection Clause by providing different time limits for those whose claims were disallowed and those claims were not. The company appealed; the appellate court reversed. As there was a rational basis for the statute's different time limitations, which afforded governmental bodies an opportunity to investigate, evaluate, and settle claims, the statute did not violate equal protection. Though the notice stated the deadline was six months from the date of the notice, rather than from the date of service, this error did not mislead the passenger, who missed both dates, or did the notice have to be served on the passenger's attorney, as the statute did not require this, or on her spouse, as his claim was derivative.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and case was remanded.

Schwittay v. Sheboygan Falls Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 00-2445


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 140; 246 Wis. 2d 385; 630 N.W.2d 772; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 481

May 9, 2001, Decided  
May 9, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: TIMOTHY M. VAN AKKEREN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review from an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin) dismissing its third-party subrogation complaint on statute of limitations grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a third-party complaint against appellee, an uninsured driver. The complaint alleged that appellee had negligently and intentionally caused the injuries of the underlying action's plaintiff. Appellant sought subrogation, contribution, and/or indemnification from appellee. The appellee affirmatively alleged that the action was time-barred pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 893.54(1) (1999-2000), the three-year statute of limitations governing personal injury actions. The trial court agreed with appellee and dismissed the third-party complaint. The court of appeals held that appellant's claim was subject to the three-year statute of limitations governing subrogation actions and that its subrogation action was untimely under that test. The trial court's application of the statutes and existing case law did not unconstitutionally deprive appellant of its right to a remedy under Wis. Const. art. I, § 9. Finally, the trial court properly dismissed all of appellant's claims, including the indemnification claim.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of appellant's third-party subrogation complaint was affirmed.

State v. Young


No. 00-3298-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 146; 246 Wis. 2d 671; 630 N.W.2d 277; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 468



May 3, 2001, Decided  
May 3, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Police questioned appellant in connection with an investigation of a suspect attempting to cash a forged check. Appellant claimed he did not know the suspect, but in a second interview, appellant admitted to knowing the suspect. Appellant was subsequently charged and convicted by the Circuit Court, Dane County (Wisconsin) of obstructing a police officer in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1) (1999-2000). Appellant challenged the decision.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the appellant contended that the trial court erred in finding him guilty because the police officer did not warn him that lying to the officer could result in criminal charges. The appellate court held that the trial court correctly concluded that the prosecution proved all the elements of the crime of obstructing a police officer, which did not include a prior warning of what conduct contravenes the law. The appellant did not contest that the prosecution proved the elements established in Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1) (1999-2000). Instead, he sought to add another element to the crime: that an officer must warn in advance that lying to police could result in criminal charges. Furthermore, even in the unlikely event that the appellant did not know that lying to police was criminally punishable, his ignorance did not afford him a defense.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

State v. Thomas


No. 00-0927-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 146; 246 Wis. 2d 668; 630 N.W.2d 275; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 451

NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLANTE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DANIEL L. KONKOL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted on his plea of guilty to first-degree reckless homicide and first-degree recklessly endangering safety by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). The court then sentenced appellant as an adult under Wis. Stat. § 938.183(1m)(c). Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to charges of first-degree reckless homicide and first-degree recklessly endangering safety. Appellant was 14 years old at the time of the crimes. The trial court entered judgment and sentenced appellant as an adult, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 938.183(1m)(c) (1997-1998). On appeal, appellant contended that § 938.183(1m)(c) was unconstitutionally ambiguous, and challenged the trial court's denial of his request for a juvenile disposition. The court of appeals affirmed, first electing not to consider the constitutional challenge, because it had not been timely raised for consideration by the trial court, and because by pleading guilty, appellant waived the right to raise such a defense. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in retaining jurisdiction over appellant, and properly determined that the adult facilities would be better able to provide confinement and treatment more suitable to appellant's needs while protecting the public.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1136 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Dorschner v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. 00-2229


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 117; 244 Wis. 2d 261; 628 N.W.2d 414; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 436


February 26, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
April 25, 2001, Decided  
April 25, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: ROBERT A. HAWLEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) granting summary judgment in favor of respondent insurer enforcing the antistacking clause contained in an uninsured motorist policy owned by the decedent at the time of her death.


OVERVIEW: The estate received the full $ 100,000 limits of the car insurance policy, and sought to collect the $ 50,000 limits in decedent's uninsured motorist policy. The estate argued that the uninsured motorist policy was ambiguous and illusory because it had not fulfilled its promise of mandatory coverage. The appellate court held that the inquiry whether the policy was illusory was unnecessary because: (1) the antistacking clause contained in the policy tracked verbatim the language of Wis. Stat. § 632.32(5)(f) (1999-2000) which authorized such provisions; and (2) the court did not find that the antistacking clause, when read together with the rest of the policy, was susceptible to more than one construction. The court determined that the order of summary judgment was proper because the estate already received a $ 100,000 payment from the car insurer which was $ 50,000 more than the maximum coverage allowed under the uninsured motorist policy, and application of the antistacking clause resulted in the estate receiving the highest coverage available under any single policy, which was exactly what the contract promised to do.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Skibinski


Nos. 00-1278-CR & 00-1279-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 109; 244 Wis. 2d 229; 629 N.W.2d 12; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 426


October 6, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
April 24, 2001, Decided  
April 24, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT C. CRAWFORD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed two judgments of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) sentencing him following his guilty pleas to operating a vehicle while intoxicated, second and third offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the sentences that he received following his guilty pleas to operating a vehicle while intoxicated, second and third offenses. Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it interpreted the applicable penalty statutes to permit that court to utilize the penalties set forth for third offense operating a vehicle while intoxicated when sentencing defendant on the second and third offenses. The appellate court reversed and remanded for resentencing on both offenses. Before a judgment of conviction could have properly been used to justify an operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated penalty enhancer, the offender had to have been sentenced. Because, at the time of sentencing, defendant had not previously been sentenced for his second offense, the trial court erred in sentencing defendant as a third offender for his second offense. On remand, the earlier conviction was to be sentenced as a second offense and the latter conviction was to be sentenced as a third offense.


OUTCOME: Judgments were reversed and both cases were remanded for resentencing. Subsequent to defendant's guilty pleas to operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, second and third offenses, the trial court erred in sentencing defendant as a third offender for his second offense.

In re Refusal of Bernard W. Harris v. Harris


No. 00-1765


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


244 Wis. 2d 287; 628 N.W.2d 437; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 379



April 12, 2001, Decided  
April 12, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Grant County: MICHAEL KIRCHMAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin) revoking his operating privileges due to his refusal to provide a sample of his breath, blood, or urine following his arrest for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.


OVERVIEW: After being arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, defendant refused to provide a sample of his breath, blood, or urine. The trial court subsequently issued an order revoking defendant's operating privileges due to his actions. Defendant appealed the trial court's order, contending that the applicable statutory provisions, Wis. Stat. § 343.305(2), (9), and (10) (1999-2000), were unconstitutional because a motor vehicle driver had a constitutional right to refuse consent to a breath, blood, or urine test, and he was being punished for exercising that right. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant failed to show that he raised that issue in the trial court, such that defendant had waived the issue and the appellate court declined to address it. Also, it was necessary for defendant to have notified the attorney general prior to attacking the constitutionality of these statutory provisions. Defendant failed to show in the record that he met that requirement.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order revoking defendant's operating privileges was affirmed. Regarding a driving under influence charge, defendant's failure to originally challenge the constitutionality of the statute providing for revocation of one's driving privileges for refusal to submit to chemical testing precluded appellate review.

State v. Arpke


No. 00-2081-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


244 Wis. 2d 287; 628 N.W.2d 437; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 373



April 11, 2001, Decided  
April 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: JAMES J. BOLGERT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of conviction of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated as a third-time offender pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated as a third-time offender. He was originally charged as a second-time offender. However, the complaint was later amended to allege a third offense because appellant was convicted of a second operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated offense while this action was awaiting trial. Appellant alleged on appeal that this amendment violated his due process right to adequate notice of the charge, exposed him to ex post facto punishment, and violated his equal protection rights. The court of appeals affirmed. Procedurally, contrary to what the State alleged, appellant did have standing to raise his appellate issues. On the merits, appellant was properly held to know that he was in peril of prosecution in this case as a third-time offender under the reduced prima facie levels set out in the statutes. Fundamental fairness notions were not violated. Nor did the amendment subject appellant to unconstitutional ex post facto punishment. Further, the statutory penalty classifications were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The conviction for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated as a third-time offender was affirmed.

 

1140 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Slagoski


No. 00-1586-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 112; 244 Wis. 2d 49; 629 N.W.2d 50; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 350


February 9, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
April 4, 2001, Decided  
April 4, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 25, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1211.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MICHAEL S. FISHER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), denying his motion for sentence modification. He contended that the use of pretrial competency and mental responsibility evaluations at sentencing violated his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary. He was found in a woman's bedroom closet, dressed in her clothes and armed with knives. Competency exams were ordered when defendant pled not guilty by reason of mental disease. When two psychiatrists found defendant was legally sane at the time of the crime, he pled guilty. The psychiatrists' findings were used at sentencing to establish defendant's future dangerousness. Upon denial of defendant's motion to modify his sentence, he appealed, arguing his constitutional rights were violated. The appellate court disagreed. It was within the scope of competency hearings to draw conclusions concerning defendant's future dangerousness. Additionally, defendant waived his constitutional rights when, through counsel, he placed his mental condition into controversy by pleading not guilty by reason of mental defect. Defendant was reasonably put on notice that the clinical impressions of both doctors would be highly relevant to the issue of future dangerousness, a legitimate sentencing consideration; thus, using pretrial psychiatric reports at the sentencing did not violate defendant's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and denial of defendant's motion for sentence modification was affirmed.

Float-Rite Park v. Somerset


No. 00-1610


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 113; 244 Wis. 2d 34; 629 N.W.2d 818; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 347


February 5, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
April 3, 2001, Decided  
April 3, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for St. Croix County: SCOTT R. NEEDHAM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeal, plaintiffs appealed the orders of the Circuit Court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin) dismissing their actions which alleged that Village of Somerset, Wis., Ordinance § 11.09(4) facially violated U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: In a consolidated appeal, plaintiff business and plaintiff patron brought actions alleging that Village of Somerset, Wis., Ordinance § 11.09(4) facially violated the provisions of U.S. Const. amend. IV. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' actions and plaintiffs appealed. The appellate court affirmed. For a search to have been unreasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV, it had to have invaded a justifiable expectation of privacy. Innertube rental businesses such as plaintiff business's did not have a justifiable expectation of privacy in areas open to the public. Section 11.09(4) was construed as providing defendant village no greater right to enter the relevant business premises than that already afforded by U.S. Const. amend. IV, such that the provision was not facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Orders dismissing plaintiffs' actions were affirmed. Defendant's ordinance provided it no greater right to enter relevant business premises than that already constitutionally permitted, such that ordinance was not facially violative of constitutional search and seizure provisions.

State v. Trochinski

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waushara County, Wisconsin, upon a no contest plea, of exposing a child to harmful material as a repeat offender, as well as from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, upon a no contest plea, of exposing a child to harmful material as a repeat offender. The trial court denied his motion for postconviction relief. 1143 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kendell G. (In re Kendell G.)


No. 00-3240-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 95; 243 Wis. 2d 67; 625 N.W.2d 918; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 322


February 13, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
March 28, 2001, Decided  
March 28, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: WAYNE J. MARIK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was adjudicated delinquent and placed under the supervision of respondent State. After violating his supervision, appellant was given a one-year placement at a correctional facility, which the juvenile court stayed. Appellant again violated his supervision. The Circuit Court, Racine County (Wisconsin) lifted the stay and placed appellant at the facility for one year commencing from the date the stay was lifted.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, appellant contended that the juvenile court's order lifting the stay on appellant's placement impermissibly extended the duration of the original dispositional order beyond the one-year limitation set out in Wis. Stat. § 938.355(4) (1999-2000) because that order had not been extended pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 938.365 (1999-2000). The appellate court held that the juvenile court's decision to stay appellant's placement eliminated the need for any extension of the original dispositional order. Wis. Stat. § 938.34(16) (1999-2000) permitted the juvenile court to stay the imposition of appellant's dispositional order, including revisions, in order to give the appellant a second chance to conform his behavior to any conditions imposed by the juvenile court. Failure to comply with the conditions triggered the commencement of the stayed portion of the dispositional order. Therefore the running of the one-year limitation of § 938.355(4) as to appellant's placement commenced when the juvenile court lifted the stay.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kranski v. W. Bend Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 99-2652


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 101; 243 Wis. 2d 117; 627 N.W.2d 549; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 312



March 27, 2001, Decided  
March 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY TO BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICIA D. McMAHON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company appealed an order of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) finding that a reducing clause in respondent insured's automobile insurance policy with appellant was invalid. The trial court also concluded that Wis. Stat. § 632.32(5)(i) (1997-1998), which authorized reducing clauses, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the case of Dowhower v. West Bend Mutual Insurance Co. was dispositive. In that case, the Wisconsin Supreme Court determined that reducing clauses found in automobile underinsured motorist policies are not illusory, and it upheld the constitutionality of § 632.32(5)(i). Appellant also asserted that the underinsured motorist provision of respondent's insurance policy was unambiguous and that summary judgment should have been granted in appellant's favor. The appellate court agreed with appellant, and it overturned the trial court's findings that § 632.32(5)(i) was unconstitutional and that respondent's coverage under her underinsured motorist provision was illusory and contrary to public policy. Despite a typographical error, it was clear that the reducing clause, considered within the context of the whole policy, applied to respondent's underinsured motorist coverage. Because the evidentiary materials contained in the record demonstrated that there was no genuine issue of material fact, appellant was entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: Trial court's order was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to enter summary judgment in appellant's favor.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DIANE S. SYKES and JOHN E. McCORMICK, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting him pursuant to his guilty plea to one count of first-degree intentional homicide, as well as contesting the denial of his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction pursuant to his guilty plea to one count of first-degree intentional homicide, as well as challenging the denial of his postconviction motion. State v. Krueger (In re Krueger)


No. 00-0152


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 76; 242 Wis. 2d 793; 626 N.W.2d 83; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 284


January 23, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
March 20, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Lincoln County: J. M. NOLAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Lincoln County, Wisconsin, dismissed both of appellant's discharge petitions. Appellant sought reinstatement of the order for his supervised release, or, in the alternative, he sought a reversal of the order dismissing his 1997 or 2000 petitions for discharge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a sexually violent person and was committed to the custody of the Department of Health and Family Services for control, care, and treatment. Appellant filed a petition for supervised release pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.08. Eventually, the parties agreed to a stipulation regarding appellant's release, but the department was unable to develop a plan regarding appellant's release because it could not find a place for appellant to live. The trial court then vacated the stipulation and denied appellant's petition for discharge. The trial court had the power to order the department to create facilities and services to provide for a plan to effectuate appellant's supervised release. Thus, the trial court improperly vacated the order for supervised release. The appellate court reversed and remanded with instructions that the trial court reinstate the order for supervised release, and if necessary, amend the release plan to effectuate appellant's prompt supervised release. The appellate court reversed the trial court's order dismissing appellant's petition for discharge and remanded for a hearing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment vacating the order for appellant's supervised release and remanded the cause with instructions that the trial court reinstate the supervised release order and amend the release plan as needed to effectuate supervised release.

Town of Lyndon v. Beyer


No. 00-2125


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 101; 243 Wis. 2d 116; 627 N.W.2d 548; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 265



March 15, 2001, Decided  
March 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY TO BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Juneau County: JOHN W. BRADY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business owner filed an appeal from the judgments of the Circuit Court for Juneau County (Wisconsin) upholding the constitutionality of a town ordinance prohibiting nude dancing in licensed establishments, and convicting the business owner of violations of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The business owner contended that the town ordinance was facially overbroad, thereby infringing upon expressive conduct protected by the First Amendment of the United States Constitution. The appellate court held that the ordinance was facially overbroad because the preamble to the ordinance indicated that it was passed to combat the secondary effects of nude dancing; however, the ordinance encompassed expressive activities that did not implicate the secondary effects that the town could legitimately seek to regulate. The court was unwilling to limit or sever the offending portions of the ordinance because the degree to which the ordinance would need to be reconstructed would require rewriting the ordinance, thereby eliminating the legislative intent of the town, and contravening both the goal of a limiting reading under the overbreadth doctrine and the role of the judicial branch.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments and remanded with directions.

Sheppard v. Starkey

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage County: FREDERIC W. FLEISHAUER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), reducing awarded damages for past and future pain and suffering, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 893.55(4) (1999-2000), on her informed consent claim against defendant, her gynecologist. Defendant cross-appealed from the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought treatment from defendant gynecologist for a cyst. Defendant recommended surgical removal. After surgery, plaintiff experienced considerable post-operative pain near the surgical site as well as secondary pain in a wide radius around it and missed work. Plaintiff sued defendant for negligence and a violation of her right to informed consent. The jury found that defendant had not been negligent, but that he failed to adequately inform plaintiff of other options. They awarded medical expenses, lost wages, and pain and suffering damages. The trial court reduced the noneconomic damage award pursuant to state statute but refused to order a new trial. Plaintiff argued that the statute capping noneconomic damages was unconstitutional and defendant moved for a new trial in the interest of justice. The appellate court disagreed, stating the statute had been recently found constitutional. Since defendant failed to demonstrate a substantial probability of a different result on retrial, the appellate court declined to exercise its own discretionary reversal power.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court capping plaintiff's noneconomic damage award was proper and its denial of a new trial was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees filed a petition to terminate appellant's parental rights to his son. The Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) granted the petition, and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant petitioned to be adjudicated the father of the child in the instant case, when the child was almost three years old. Subsequent to the determination of paternity, appellant still did not make child support payments, cover other costs, or visit the child. Respondents, the child's mother and her husband, filed a petition to terminate appellant's parental rights. The trial court granted the petition, finding both abandonment and failure to assume parental responsibility. On appeal, appellant challenged the trial court's jurisdiction and contended that claim preclusion or issue preclusion barred the action. The court of appeals affirmed, holding that both venue and jurisdiction were proper, based on the child's residence and appellant's previous paternity action, which gave the trial court continuing jurisdiction. The action was not barred by claim or issue preclusion; the instant action was not a collateral attack on the judgment that appellant was the child's biological father, and appellant's paternity action did not address whether he had abandoned the child.


OUTCOME: Termination of appellant's parental rights affirmed. The action was not barred by claim or issue preclusion, venue was proper in the county where the child resided, and the trial court had continuing jurisdiction following appellant's own paternity action.

State v. Paulson


No. 00-2716-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 75; 242 Wis. 2d 473; 625 N.W.2d 360; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 197



February 27, 2001, Decided  
February 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Iron County: PATRICK J. MADDEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decisions of the Circuit Court for Iron County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating a snowmobile with an excessively noisy exhaust system in violation of Wis. Stat. § 350.10(1)(d) (1999-2000) and denying his motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of operating a snowmobile with an excessively noisy exhaust system in violation of Wis. Stat. § 350.10(1)(d) (1999-2000), as well as challenging the trial court's order denying his motion for reconsideration. Defendant contended that, as a matter of law, the evidence was insufficient to support the trial court's finding that his snowmobile made excessive or unusual noise in violation of § 350.10(1)(d). The appellate court reversed. For purposes of § 350.10(1)(d), the standard for a reasonable, usual, or normal amount of noise was that amount of noise emitted by an originally installed snowmobile muffler. The State failed to prove that defendant's exhaust system was excessively loud under the proper objective standard, as opposed to an improper arbitrary or subjective standard.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and trial court's decision denying defendant's motion for reconsideration were reversed. State failed to prove that defendant operated snowmobile with excessively noisy exhaust system since proper objective standard entailed comparison with noise emitted by an originally installed snowmobile muffler.

State v. Logemann


No. 00-2178-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 75; 242 Wis. 2d 472; 625 N.W.2d 360; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 166



February 22, 2001, Decided  
February 22, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: J.R. ERWIN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000), blood samples were drawn and analysis of the blood revealed a blood alcohol content of .186. At trial, appellant objected to the admission of the blood analysis arrest based on an alleged break in the chain of custody. The Circuit Court, Jefferson County (Wisconsin) overruled the objection and convicted the appellant.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the appellant contended that Wis. Stat. § 343.305 (1999-2000) was unconstitutional as applied to him. Second, appellant argued that the prosecution did not sufficiently establish the chain of custody of the blood samples drawn, and therefore they should not have been admitted into evidence at trial. The court rejected the appellant's contentions. The blood draw was taken to obtain evidence of intoxication during the course of a lawful arrest under circumstances in which the appellant was suspected of a drunk-driving related offense. The draw was conducted at the hospital under no objection from the appellant, and he did not argue that the method used was unreasonable. Therefore, the statute was not unconstitutional. Appellant's chain of custody argument centered on the fact that the box containing the samples was at one point opened so that mailing labels could be filled out, and was then resealed with heavy packing tape. The trial court properly held that, because of the consistency of the packaging of the tubes containing the blood samples, the issue of the missing link in the chain of custody went to the weight of the evidence, not to its admissibility.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The court held that the implied consent to testing statute was not unconstitutional as to the appellant. The sample was taken at a hospital, pursuant to a lawful arrest and the method was not unreasonable. The court found that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in the degree of proof necessary to establish a chain of custody and in allowing the blood sample analysis into evidence.

State v. Walter


No. 99-2878-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2001 WI App 75; 242 Wis. 2d 473; 625 N.W.2d 361; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 165

February 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Walworth County: ROBERT J. KENNEDY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Walworth County, Wisconsin, convicting him for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: An officer arrested defendant for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) and issued him a municipal citation. When the State learned that defendant's 1997 municipal court conviction for operating while intoxicated (OWI) was his second offense, the municipal court vacated the conviction. The State followed with a criminal complaint charging defendant as a second-time OWI offender. A jury found defendant guilty and he appealed, contending the belated charging violated his right to a speedy trial. The trial court ruled that the delay did not violate any of his constitutional rights. On appeal, the court affirmed. A determination of whether the defendant's right to a speedy trial was violated depended upon a balancing approach in which several factors were weighed. Among the factors considered included prejudice to the defendant. Defendant did not suffer any prejudice during the delay between the municipal court proceeding and later criminal proceeding because he believed that the matter had been put to rest.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The delay between a municipal court proceeding and a later criminal proceeding did not deny a defendant's right to a speedy trial.

Avoca v. Carr


No. 00-3016-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 75; 242 Wis. 2d 473; 625 N.W.2d 360; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 135



February 8, 2001, Decided  
February 8, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Iowa County: WILLIAM D. DYKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Iowa County (Wisconsin) finding that defendant violated Village of Avoca, Wis., Ordinances § 17.03(2)(c), and imposing a forfeiture including costs against her.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the trial court's decision finding that she violated plaintiff village's ordinance pertaining to residential fences and imposing a forfeiture including costs against her. Defendant contended that the relevant provision, Village of Avoca, Wis., Ordinances § 17.03(2)(c), regulated only fences on property lines and the structure on her property was not on a property line. Additionally, defendant alleged that the provision regulated only fences and the structure on her property was not a fence. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant's first contention was rejected because § 17.03(2)(c) plainly applied to all fences in residential districts. An applicable definition of the term "fence" as used in § 17.03(2)(c) was a barrier intended to prevent escape or intrusion or to mark a boundary. The structure erected on defendant's property constituted a "fence" as that term was defined, as it was admittedly a barrier intended to prevent intrusion on defendant's privacy.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment was affirmed. Relevant ordinance plainly regulated all fences in residential districts and applied to the structure located on defendant's property, since, as a barrier intended to prevent intrusion on defendant's property, structure constituted a fence.

State v. Cordero


Nos. 00-1350-CR, 00-1613-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 58; 241 Wis. 2d 572; 624 N.W.2d 421; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 92



January 30, 2001, Decided  
January 30, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] APPEALS from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Door County: JOHN D. KOEHN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants were convicted in the Circuit Court for Door County (Wisconsin) of various sex crimes. Appellants' motions for a mistrial were denied. Appellants claimed the jury was erroneously exposed to extraneous information contained in a police report that was prejudicial to their defense.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were charged with having sexual contact with their daughter, failing to prevent the sexual assault, and intentionally causing their daughter to view or listen to sexually explicit conduct. At trial, the investigator testified that he found sexually explicit materials in appellants' home. His report was not introduced into evidence and contained extraneous information not mentioned at trial. During deliberation, the trial court gave the jury the police report, without consulting with defense counsel. Giving the report to the jury violated appellants' constitutional rights. The extraneous information was prejudicial. The case was one of credibility, and the information in the report could have had a negative impact on appellants' credibility. The State failed to meet its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that the report did not contribute to the verdict.


OUTCOME: Case was remanded for a new trial. Extraneous information contained in the report was prejudicial and there was a reasonable possibility that the information contributed to the guilty verdicts. The extraneous information painted appellants in a negative light that was not evident otherwise.

State v. Wiedenhoeft (In re Wiedenhoeft)


No. 99-2379


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 58; 241 Wis. 2d 573; 624 N.W.2d 421; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 46



January 17, 2001, Decided  
January 17, 2001, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DIANE S. SYKES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent inmate served prison time for sexual assault. Petitioner State filed a petition for detention alleging that respondent was a sexually violent person. The circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) ordered that respondent be committed to institutional care pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 980. Respondent appealed.


OVERVIEW: Respondent inmate was serving a prison sentence for sexual assault offenses. The day before respondent's mandatory release date, petitioner State filed a petition for detention alleging that respondent was a sexually violent person. After hearing substantial testimony from three psychologists, the trial court concluded that respondent had a mental disorder, which created a substantial probability that he would re-offend if released. The trial court ordered respondent to be committed to institutional care, pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 980. Respondent appealed. The appellate court affirmed. The trial court did not lose competency to handle the matter, because Wis. Stat. ch. 980 was not unconstitutionally applied to respondent. The trial court's findings were not clearly erroneous, and the record reflected that the petition was timely filed. Neither the statutes nor case law required respondent's release where the evidence showed that he was still dangerous, and, much more likely than not, to re-offend. Thus, respondent could be detained.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. The trial court did not lose competency to handle the matter, because the state statute was not unconstitutionally applied to respondent. The trial court's findings were not clearly erroneous, and the record reflected that the petition for commitment was timely filed.

State v. Nord


No. 00-1529-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 48; 241 Wis. 2d 387; 625 N.W.2d 302; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 18


October 31, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
January 17, 2001, Decided  
January 17, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Polk County: ROBERT H. RASMUSSEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Polk County (Wisconsin), which granted the defendant's motion to suppress the results of the defendant's blood alcohol test, in defendant's prosecution for operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration under Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to suppress the results of his chemical test on the grounds that the implied consent statute, Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) (1997-98), violated his due process rights because the statute misled accused persons regarding the consequences for taking or refusing the test. At the suppression hearing, the trial court determined that the officer had probable cause to stop and arrest. However, it concluded that the implied consent statute did materially mislead the defendant in a manner designed to try to convince and persuade him that he will be better off taking the test than not taking the test, which was fundamentally unfair and in contravention of due process. The court reversed. The court held that the statute did not mislead, therefore the defendant's due process argument failed. The informed consent statute alerted the defendant to the penalties that could result from violating Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) (1997-98), and the statute further informed that the test results could be used against the defendant in court. Therefore, the court concluded that the statute adequately advised the defendant of the consequences for consenting or refusing to take the test.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. The defendant failed to overcome the implied consent statute's presumption of constitutionality, therefore the trial court improperly excluded the results of the defendant's blood alcohol test. The informed consent statute alerted the defendant to the penalties that could result from refusing to submit to chemical testing and the statute further informed that the test results could be used against the defendant in court.

State ex rel. Johnson v. Sullivan


No. 00-1922


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2001 WI App 58; 241 Wis. 2d 572; 624 N.W.2d 421; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 54



January 11, 2001, Decided  
January 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ROBERT R. PEKOWSKI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed an order of the Dane County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) dismissing his declaratory judgment action against defendant employees of the Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff argued that Wis. Stat. § 301.21(2m)(a) (1999-2000), which authorized his transfer to a privately run prison in Tennessee, was unconstitutional. The appellate court rejected plaintiff's arguments and affirmed the trial court's dismissal of his action against defendants. Allowing the transfer of Wisconsin inmates to private correctional facilities in other states did not violate the Supremacy Clause by extending Wisconsin's territorial limits. Wisconsin did not extend its territorial limits by contracting with a Tennessee prison to house Wisconsin prisoners. Tennessee could withdraw its authorization to the private correctional corporation to do business within its state if it chose to do so. Plaintiff was mistaken in his supposition that private prison guards were exempt from liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Sending Wisconsin prisoners out of state did not violate an interstate compact agreement because the contract at issue was not one between two states and did not increase Wisconsin's political power in relation to federal authority.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed. Statute authorizing plaintiff's transfer to a privately run prison in Tennessee was not unconstitutional, and trial court properly dismissed plaintiff's declaratory judgment action against defendants.

State ex rel. Saffold v. Schwarz


No. 99-2945


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 56; 241 Wis. 2d 253; 625 N.W.2d 333; 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 51


December 7, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
January 9, 2001, Decided  
January 9, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the Circuit Court, Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), decision dismissing his petition for writ of certiorari following his parole revocation, claiming the circuit court erred in concluding that the Prisoner Litigation Reform Act (PLRA) applied to his challenge to his parole revocation; therefore, the 45-day time limit for filing such a challenge required dismissal of his petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was paroled following imprisonment for burglary convictions. His parole was then revoked. He appealed administratively; the revocation was sustained by respondent. Petitioner, 106 days after the decision sustaining the revocation and 129 days after revocation, filed a petition for writ of certiorari in the circuit court, challenging the revocation. The circuit court entered an order concluding that the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA) required petitions for writ of certiorari to be filed within 45 days of the final decision issued by respondent and dismissing his petition as untimely. The court affirmed. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 893.735, the 45-day time limit applied to a certiorari petition seeking review of a denial of parole. Persons challenging probation revocation were prisoners under the PLRA. Further, there was no equal protection violation. A rational basis existed for distinguishing between in-state and out-of-state prisoners for purposes of filing deadlines under the PLRA.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because Prison Litigation Reform Act applied to petitioner's challenge of his parole revocation and did not constitute an equal protection violation.

Pflughoeft v. American Family Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 00-0348


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 31; 241 Wis. 2d 47; 622 N.W.2d 769; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1208



December 27, 2000, Decided  
December 27, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICIA D. McMAHON, Judge. Judgment reversed and cause remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granted a declaratory judgment awarding plaintiffs stacked underinsured motorist coverage on two automobile insurance policies. Defendant insurer filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' son was injured by an underinsured vehicle. The parties stipulated to damages of $ 225,000, and plaintiffs received $ 50,000 from the underinsured driver's insurance company. Plaintiffs had two vehicles insured with defendant, each with coverage of $ 100,000 per person bodily injury; each had also a clause that reduced coverage by any amount paid from an underinsured motorist's coverage. Each policy also included a provision precluding the stacking of coverage. The trial court ruled that the anti-stacking clauses were invalid. The court of appeals reversed, holding that (1) the policy language clearly, without ambiguity, prohibited stacking; (2) the elasticity clause in the policy conformed the policy to the prevailing statutory law, which had validated the state's anti-stacking provision; (3) an amendment to the insurance statute authorizing reduction by the amount of UIM coverage did not unconstitutionally impair plaintiffs' right to contract; and (4) plaintiffs' coverage was not rendered illusory by the reducing clauses.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment reversed. The policy unambiguously prohibited stacking, and the prohibition was validated by law passed subsequent to the policy date. The reducing clause did not render the contract illusory and did not impair plaintiffs' right to contract. Therefore plaintiffs had $ 100,000 in coverage available for the claim, which was reduced by the $ 50,000 received from the liable party's UIM coverage.

State v. Bare

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to lewd and lascivious behavior, habitual criminality, and disorderly conduct, habitual criminality. He was convicted and sentenced in the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief, which was denied. He then appealed from the judgment of conviction and the order denying postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen masturbating while sitting in a car parked next to a school bus located in front of an elementary school. Defendant pleaded guilty. He was convicted of lewd and lascivious behavior and disorderly conduct. The trial court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed. On appeal, defendant alleged that his convictions were multiplicitous, and that the trial court erroneously exercised discretion in sentencing him to consecutive maximum prison terms totaling six years. Given several factors including defendant's lengthy history of sex offenses, the trial court understandably gave the greatest weight to the protection of children who could have been endangered by defendant's conduct should he not have been incarcerated for as long as possible. The record supported the trial court's conclusion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and order were affirmed. The charges of lewd and lascivious behavior and disorderly conduct were not multiplicitous. Thus, the convictions did not violate defendant's constitutional protection against double jeopardy, or did the trial court err in sentencing defendant, given defendant's lengthy history of sex offenses.

State v. Triggs


No. 99-2502-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2000 WI App 31; 241 Wis. 2d 50; 622 N.W.2d 770; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1247



December 27, 2000, Decided  
December 27, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. CONEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) entered after a jury found her guilty of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, fifth offense. She claimed that her trial counsel was ineffective because he failed to object to her six-person jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion seeking a new trial, alleging that she was denied her constitutional right to a 12-person jury, or in the alternative, that trial counsel provided ineffective assistance for failing to raise the issue. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that counsel's failure to object under the circumstances of the case did not constitute ineffective assistance. The statute authorizing a six-person jury panel at the time defendant was tried was good law, though it was later held unconstitutional. Counsel's failure to raise the issue did not constitute deficient performance. Defendant received an otherwise fair and error-free trial. The use of a 6-person jury rather than a 12-person jury did not undermine the fundamental integrity of her trial. Although it was conceivable that the chances for acquittal or a hung jury were greater with 12 jurors than with 6, that possibility, which was purely speculative, was insufficient to establish prejudice. Ineffective assistance of counsel cases were limited to situations where the law or duty was clear such that reasonable counsel should know enough to raise the issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because trial counsel's decision not to object to a six person jury did not constitute ineffective assistance under the circumstances. Counsel was not required to object and argue a point of law that was unsettled. Even if counsel's failure to object constituted deficient performance, such conduct did not prejudice defendant.
