State v. Volden


No. 00-1026-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2000 WI App 31; 241 Wis. 2d 48; 622 N.W.2d 769; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1258



December 21, 2000, Decided  
December 21, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DALE T. PASELL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OMVWI), contending that the trial court erred in failing to suppress evidence obtained as the result of an allegedly unconstitutional entry into his residence. Concluding that the warrantless entry did not violate defendant's U.S. Const. amend. IV rights, the appellate court affirmed. A warrantless, nonconsensual entry of a home to effect an arrest was reasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV only where there was probable cause coupled with exigent circumstances. Both requirements were met in the case. The facts reasonably led the arresting officer to believe that defendant had been OMVWI, as he caused an accident, the officer was told that he smelled of intoxicants, he fled when informed the police would be called, and he had three prior OMVWI convictions. The rapid dissolution of alcohol from the bloodstream provided exigent circumstances.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. Probable cause and exigent circumstances permitted warrantless entry into defendant's home to effect his arrest where evidence reasonably led arresting officer to believe that defendant had been operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.

Guzman v. St. Francis Hosp.


No. 98-2710


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 21; 240 Wis. 2d 559; 623 N.W.2d 776; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1211


September 5, 2000, Oral Argument  
December 19, 2000, Decided  
December 19, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICIA D. MCMAHON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs brought a negligence action against defendants health-care providers. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, held in a non-final order that a cap imposed by the legislature on the recovery of noneconomic damages in medical malpractice actions within the scope of Wis. Stat. ch. 655 was unconstitutional. The defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the cap violated both the right to a trial by jury recognized by the Wisconsin constitution, and the separation of powers between the judicial and legislative branches. On appeal, plaintiffs made several arguments to support the trial court's ruling that the cap was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed. The cap did not infringe on the right of trial by jury, under Wis. Const. art. I, § 5, because the right to a jury trial was not affected, and the legislature could set the amount of recovery. The provision that the jury's findings were to be made without regard to the cap did not violate the separation of powers. Wis. Const. art. I, § 9, providing for access to courts, was not violated as plaintiffs did have a right to a remedy. Neither the plaintiffs' equal protection or substantive due process rights were violated because the cap was rationally related to the legislature's goal of providing health care, access to the courts was not a fundamental right requiring strict scrutiny, and their claim arose after the cap was enacted.


OUTCOME: The order finding the cap unconstitutional was reversed.

 

1165 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Joseph E. G. v. Joseph E. G.


No. 99-3248


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2001 WI App 29; 240 Wis. 2d 481; 623 N.W.2d 137; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1174


June 23, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
December 7, 2000, Decided  
December 7, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Jefferson County: WILLIAM F. HUE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent juvenile's conviction of false imprisonment of another juvenile as a party to the crime, respondent appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) denying his motion to be excused from the Wis. Stat. § 938.34(15m)(bm) requirement that he register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: After respondent juvenile's conviction of false imprisonment of another juvenile as a party to the crime, respondent appealed an order of the trial court denying his motion to be excused from the Wis. Stat. § 938.34(15m)(bm) requirement that he register as a sex offender. Respondent contended that Wis. Stat. § 301.45(1m) violated his constitutional rights to equal protection and substantive due process. That provision allowed juvenile's convicted of certain offenses not including false imprisonment to be excused from the sex offender registration requirements. The court affirmed the trial court. Section 301.45(1m) did not violate constitutional guarantees of equal protection as applied to respondent since the classification created by that provision was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest of protecting the public. It was rational for the legislature to conclude that a juvenile who engaged in false imprisonment was a greater potential threat to public safety than a juvenile involved in a factually consensual sexual relationship with a child. Respondent's substantive due process argument failed for the same reason.


OUTCOME: Trial court's order was affirmed. Statutory provision allowing juveniles engaging in consensual sexual relationships with children to be excused from sex offender registration requirements but not those engaging in false imprisonment was consistent with constitutional equal protection guarantee.

State v. Jones

NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN and MAXINE A. WHITE, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), convicting him of violating a domestic violence injunction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted in a trial before a six-person jury, under the statute mandating six-person juries in misdemeanor cases. He did not object to being tried by a six-person jury. Appellant challenged, however, the judgment of conviction for violation of a domestic violence injunction, following a six-person jury trial, and from the order denying his postconviction motion for a new trial. He argued: (1) his conviction was obtained in violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 7 because his trial was before a 6-person jury under the statute subsequently declared unconstitutional; (2) Hansford should apply retroactively to provide him a new trial with 12 jurors; and (3) because he did not personally waive his right to a 12-person jury trial, and because he challenged the 6-person jury in his postconviction motion, his failure to object to a 6-person jury before his trial should not be deemed a waiver of his challenge to the 6-person jury. The court, in affirming, noted that defendant waived or forfeited his constitutional claim by not making a constitutional objection at the trial court level.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Appellant was not entitled to a 12-person jury as he had not objected to a 6-person jury at the trial court level.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County, denying her suppression motion and convicting her of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OAWI), as a repeat offender. A blood alcohol sample was taken without defendant's consent, based on a department policy to take a blood sample for a second offense. IV's warrant requirement. Defendant was not required to consent or voluntarily submit to the blood withdrawal.

State v. Taylor (In re Taylor)


No. 98-1030


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2001 WI App 1; 240 Wis. 2d 324; 621 N.W.2d 386; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1117



November 21, 2000, Decided  
November 21, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MEL FLANAGAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a post-commitment order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denying his motion to vacate a Wis. Stat. § 980 judgment which committed him as a sexually violent person.


OVERVIEW: At trial, all four of the State's peremptory strikes were of men. On appeal, appellant described his first claim as a denial of means to obtain a meaningful review because of the trial court's refusal to record the jury selection. The court found, however, his claim was essentially an ineffective assistance of counsel claim for failure to assert a Batson objection based on gender. The court found the trial court acted within its discretion in denying appellant's request to record voir dire, because it provided a mechanism to address any objections that might have arisen during the jury selection process. Nevertheless, the court remanded the case so the trial court could conduct a hearing relative to the failure of appellant's counsel to raise a gender Batson inquiry, and its impact upon the jury selection. The trial court's failure to define the statutory term "substantially probable" did not render the relevant statute unconstitutionally vague, and trial counsel's performance was not deficient for failing to request a definitional instruction. Finally, testimony presented by the State's witnesses was sufficient to support the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: Order was affirmed in part, reversed in part; evidence was sufficient to show a nexus between appellant's particular mental disorder and his predisposition for sexual violence. Denial of appellant's request to record voir dire was proper, as trial court provided a mechanism to address any objections during jury selection process. Cause was remanded to determine whether counsel's waiver of Batson objection constituted ineffective assistance.

Ahrens v. Town of Fulton


No.99-2466(D)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 268; 240 Wis. 2d 124; 621 N.W.2d 643; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1110


May 19, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
November 16, 2000, Decided  
November 16, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock County: MICHAEL J. BYRON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a property tax dispute, plaintiff mobile home owners appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) granting summary judgment to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mobile home owners challenged defendant town's taxation of their mobile homes as realty. They stipulated to having certain plaintiffs treated as representative of the others. The trial court dismissed their claims, holding that the mobile homes may not have been taxable as realty but none of them were exempt from personal property tax, which would have been equal to the tax imposed. The court affirmed in part, but on different grounds. Because the other statutory criteria were satisfied, with one exception, all of the representative plaintiffs' mobile homes could be taxed as improvements to real estate; some part of each mobile home's weight was off its wheels and set upon some other support. The remaining representative mobile home was not exempt from personal property tax as the combined area of the unit and its attached porch exceeded 400 square feet. However, because non-attached structures on a plaintiff's property could not be considered when calculating the mobile home's size, remand was necessary to determine whether any of the non-representative plaintiffs' mobile homes were exempt from personal property tax.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. With one exception, all of the representative plaintiffs' mobile homes were properly taxed as realty. The single exception was subject to personal property tax equal to the real property tax imposed, so the tax imposed was not "unlawful." However, remand was necessary to determine if non-representative plaintiffs' mobile homes were exempt from taxation.

State v. Dorschner


No. 00-1160-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2001 WI App 1; 240 Wis. 2d 324; 621 N.W.2d 385; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1101



November 14, 2000, Decided  
November 14, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: MICHAEL W. GAGE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, third offense, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant with both operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a)(1997-98), and operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration (PAC), pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b)(1997-98). Defendant challenged the State's dual prosecution of both offenses on due process and double jeopardy grounds. The trial court rejected his argument, and subsequently he pled guilty to OWI and the PAC charge was dismissed. The court held simultaneous prosecution under both Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1)(a) and (1)(b) did not violate notions of fundamental fairness and double jeopardy. Defendant did not request the court to declare the statutes unconstitutional. Instead, he argued that the courts should be required to submit only one charge to the jury as a matter of fundamental fairness and avoidance of double jeopardy. There could be no double jeopardy because the legislature did not authorize two convictions. Consequently, there could not be multiple punishments. The court also rejected any suggestion that the State should be required to make a pretrial election between the two charges.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the State's dual prosecution for both operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated and operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration did not violate his double jeopardy protection or his due process rights.

Sukala v. Heritage Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 99-1339


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 266; 240 Wis. 2d 65; 622 N.W.2d 457; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1098


August 24, 2000, Oral Argument  
November 9, 2000, Decided  
November 9, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.
Review denied by Sukala v. Heritage Mut. Ins. Co., 2001 WI 43, 242 Wis. 2d 544, 629 N.W.2d 783, 2001 Wisc. LEXIS 223 (2001)
Subsequent appeal at Sukala v. Heritage Mut. Ins. Co., 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 506 (Wis. Ct. App., June 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Wood County: FREDERIC FLEISHAUER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the Circuit Court for Wood County's (Wisconsin) judgment declaring as valid underinsured motorist reducing clauses in auto insurance policies belonging to them and to plaintiff husband's employer, in plaintiffs' suit over injuries to plaintiff husband from a car crash.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff husband, driving for his employer, was hurt in a two car crash. Both plaintiff husband's policy and that of his employer had underinsured (UIM) coverage with reducing clauses for, among other things, worker's compensation benefits, which plaintiff husband received. Plaintiffs sued defendants, insurers, for compensation and moved for declarations that one UIM reducing clause was invalid for defendant, plaintiffs' insurer's, failure to follow Wis. Stat. § 631.36(5) (1997-98)'s notice requirements as to UIM coverage changes, and that Wis. Stat. § 632.32(5)(i) (1997-98) permitting such clauses, was unconstitutional. The trial court incorporated its denial of plaintiffs' motions in its final judgment. The court affirmed. Even though defendant insurer had gratuitously sent plaintiffs a renewal notice on their policy's UIM coverage changes, § 631.36(5) did not apply as the changes were statutorily initiated rather than by defendant insurer. Section 632.32(5)(i) was constitutional as it did not deprive policy holders of any constitutional right and the policies' provisions unambiguously mimicked the statute; therefore the UIM coverage was not illusory.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The statute permitting underinsured motorist (UIM) reducing clauses was constitutional. Also, even though defendant insurer gratuitously sent plaintiffs a renewal notice on their policy's UIM changes, statutory notice requirements did not apply as the changes had been initiated by a statute rather than by defendant. Thus plaintiffs' coverage was reduced by worker's compensation benefits plaintiff husband had received.

State v. Kramer


No. 99-2580-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 271; 240 Wis. 2d 44; 622 N.W.2d 4; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1080


July 11, 2000, Oral Argument  
November 8, 2000, Decided  
November 8, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: PETER L. GRIMM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment, by the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), convicting him of two violations of the criminal commercial gambling statute, Wis. Stat. § 945.03(5) (1995-96), and from orders denying his motions for suppression and dismissal of the felony charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned a saloon with a video poker machine, in the Village of North Fond du Lac. The county district attorney and sheriff sent a letter to all county bar owners except those in the Village, warning that payouts by video poker machines would lead to criminal prosecution. Defendant's saloon was searched pursuant to a warrant, leading to a charge of commercial gambling. Defendant's motions to dismiss and to suppress evidence were denied, and he was convicted. On appeal, defendant claimed selective prosecution. The court reversed. The letter, sent to all county bars except in the Village, created arbitrary classifications of tavern owners - those who received the letter and those who did not. Defendant did not receive the letter and he was prosecuted, thus the letter had a discriminatory effect. The inequitable distribution of the letter was prima facie evidence of a purposeful intent to discriminate. Thus defendant made a prima facie showing of selective prosecution. Because the State did not offer a valid reason for the inequitable distribution of the letter, it failed to rebut by demonstrating a valid exercise of prosecutorial discretion.


OUTCOME: Judgment and orders reversed due to defendant's unrebutted prima facie showing of selective prosecution; only members of the arbitrary class of bar owners were prosecuted, this arbitrary class was created by the county's warning letter, and the State did not offer a valid reason for the inequitable distribution of the warning letter.

State v. Willenkamp


No. 00-0684-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2000 WI App 256; 239 Wis. 2d 592; 620 N.W.2d 481; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 973



October 3, 2000, Decided  
October 3, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Outagamie County: JAMES T. BAYORGEON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Outagamie County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who sought suppression of blood test results, argued that: (1) the implied consent law was unconstitutional as applied; and (2) a sheriff's deputy's modification of the implied consent warning improperly coerced defendant to submit to the blood test by threatening revocation for lack of compliance. The court rejected defendant's arguments and affirmed his conviction. The court did not need to delineate what sorts of objections might have been considered reasonable objections because defendant did not present any objections, reasonable or otherwise. He did not refuse to take the test, nor did the record reveal that he gave any indication that he would have preferred another test. Defendant's blood test was a reasonable search under U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court rejected defendant's argument that the deputy's additional language in the implied consent warning exceeded the statutory authority. The deputy did not act illegally when she informed defendant that the sheriff's department's policy was blood, and the deputy did not exceed her duty by simply stating what she had authority to do.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; deputy's modification of implied consent warning did not improperly coerce defendant to submit to blood test, and defendant's blood test was a reasonable search.

Hafner v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 00-0511


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 216; 239 Wis. 2d 218; 619 N.W.2d 300; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 967


September 12, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
September 28, 2000, Decided  
September 28, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL L. LA ROCQUE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) affirming a decision of the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission upholding the determination by the Department of Revenue that appellants were not entitled to a refund of Wisconsin income taxes levied on their federal civil service pensions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were federal employees and members of the federal civil service (CSRS) pension fund who had left federal service before the cutoff date, and were reemployed sometime thereafter. Upon reemployment, they exercised the option to reinstate their retirement benefit credits and pension eligibility by paying back the amounts they had withdrawn from the fund. According to the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission (commission), the fact that employees whose service was interrupted could "repurchase" prior years of employment for benefit determination purposes did not erase their absence from federal employment on December 31, 1963, or otherwise retroactively employ them so that they could be considered to have been actually employed on that date. The court found that while appellants could recapture the lost credits for the earlier years of employment by paying back the withdrawal, they could not render themselves "members" of the system on a specific date when they concededly were not employed by the government. Thus, the commission's decision denying them a refund of Wisconsin income taxes levied on their federal civil service pensions was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellants could pay back the amounts they had withdrawn from the federal civil service pension fund upon reemployment, but they could not erase their absence from federal employment or retroactively employ themselves to achieve an exemption from Wisconsin state income taxes. Thus, appellants were not entitled to refund from state income taxes levied on their pensions.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence which were entered by the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin) after defendant pled no contest to delivery of tetrahydrocannabinol.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence after he entered a plea of no contest to delivery of tetrahydrocannabinol. The court placed defendant on probation with a number of conditions, including that defendant was to serve six months in county jail without good time. The court then stayed three months of that six month period and stated that the additional three months could be imposed at the discretion of defendant's probation agent. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court did not have the authority to order that his jail term to be served without good time nor the authority to authorize the probation agent to impose jail time at his or her discretion. The instant court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. Wis. Stat. §§ 302.43 (1997-98), 973.155 (1997-98) did not entitle an offender to earn good time for jail confinement imposed as a condition of probation. However, there was no statutory authority for the Department of Corrections to decide the length of defendant's jail confinement as a condition of probation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed in part and reversed in part. Case was remanded. There existed no statutory authority for defendant's probation agent to decide the length of defendant's jail confinement, which was imposed as a condition of his probation.

Chiroff v. Milwaukee County


No. 99-1023


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2000 WI App 233; 239 Wis. 2d 232; 619 N.W.2d 307; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 905



September 19, 2000, Decided  
September 19, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) which granted summary judgment dismissing all of her claims filed against defendants, two municipalities, their employees, and an insurer. Plaintiff brought statutory and common law claims of negligence and intentional tort, and claims of violations under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff's husband died at home, a funeral home informed plaintiff that the death had to be medically confirmed before the body would be removed from the home. A forensic investigator came to plaintiff's home to pronounce death. Plaintiff gave the investigator consent to enter her bedroom where her husband was located. The investigator withdrew fluid from husband's eyes. After husband's body was taken to the funeral home, cosmetic work was performed so that the eyes no longer appeared depressed. Plaintiff brought claims against defendants and summary judgment in defendants' favor. On appeal, the court held that defendants were entitled to qualified immunity from plaintiff's federal and state law claims. Public employees at the scene were performing their duties. Plaintiff's rights were not violated because she consented to have official enter her home to obtain a pronouncement of her husband's death. The investigator followed lawful procedures set out by a medical examiner, established pursuant to Wis. Admin. Code § 135.08. Therefore, the court held that the trial court did not err in granting summary judgment to defendants. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment to defendants in plaintiff's lawsuit for negligence and constitutional violations was affirmed because defendants were immune from suit in relation to the actions involved in pronouncing the death of plaintiff's husband.

State v. Reed


No. 99-2108-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2000 WI App 233; 239 Wis. 2d 233; 619 N.W.2d 307; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 902



September 14, 2000, Decided  
September 14, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: TIMOTHY G. DUGAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimed the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) erred in denying his motion to suppress the cocaine found in his pocket after determining that the cocaine was admissible under the inevitable discovery exception to the exclusionary rule.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a conviction of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. Responding to a complaint of drug sales, officers obtained consent to search a residence. Police found drugs in the residence and searched appellant's person. Cocaine in appellant's pocket was admissible under inevitable discovery doctrine. Police had probable cause to arrest appellant even without cocaine in his pocket; therefore police would have lawfully been in a position to search his pockets incident to arrest. The police had probable cause prior to the unlawful search of appellant's pockets, and police were obtaining evidence against appellant through the active pursuit of an alternate line of investigation. Under the circumstances, police reasonably could have believed that appellant knew about the cocaine in the apartment. Police had the reasonable suspicion necessary to detain him.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Cocaine was admissible under inevitable discovery exception. Police reasonably could have believed that appellant knew of cocaine in dining room, and that he exercised joint dominion and control over premises. Police had probable cause to arrest when his pockets were searched.

State v. Jones

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR

RULE 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: WILLIAM F. HUE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, claimed that the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a judgment convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OMVWI). He claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence on the grounds that the deputy did not have probable cause to arrest him. He also claimed that Wis. Stat. § 343.303 was unconstitutional. The court did not have the authority to overrule the Wisconsin Supreme Court's interpretation of § 343.303. Appellant's speech was slightly slurred and he did not correctly perform the walk-and-turn test. The deputy requested appellant to submit to a preliminary breath test (PBT). Appellant was then arrested for OMVWI. Appellant's motion to suppress the results of the blood test was properly denied, as deputy was justified in requesting the PBT, even if he did not have probable cause to arrest appellant for OMVWI at the time of the request.


OUTCOME: Trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion to suppress. Arresting deputy had probable cause to request a preliminary breath test, and he had probable cause to arrest. The court did not have authority to overrule The Wisconsin Supreme Court's judgment concerning preliminary breath test statute.

Nankin v. Village of Shorewood


No. 99-1058


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2000 WI App 214; 238 Wis. 2d 841; 618 N.W.2d 273; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 802



August 22, 2000, Decided  
August 22, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DIANE S. SYKES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), denying his request that Wis. Stat. § 74.37(6) (1997-98) be declared unconstitutional contending the exception for taxpayers who resided in counties with a population of 500,000 or more which prevented them from having a de novo circuit court review of property tax assessments was unfair.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was unhappy with the reassessed value of his real property. Instead of pursuing a certiorari review in circuit court, he sought a ruling that Wis. Stat. § 74.37(6) was unconstitutional. Wis. Stat. § 74.37 provided a taxpayer the opportunity for a de novo circuit court review, but Wis. Stat. § 74.37(6) excepted taxpayers who resided in counties with a population of 500,000 or more. The court found a rational relationship between the classification created by the "500,000 or more" language and a legitimate government purpose. The exception did not violate the equal protection clause, did not establish a new form or type of taxation, or set up a method or system for assessment and collection of taxes, or violate the proscription that no private or local bill embrace more than one subject. The court concluded plaintiff failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that Wis. Stat. § 74.37(6) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Exception for taxpayers who resided in counties with a population of 500,000 or more which prevented them from having a de novo circuit court review of property tax assessments did not violate equal protection clause, did not establish new form or type of taxation, or set up method or system for assessment and collection of taxes, or violate proscription that no private bill embrace more than one subject.

State v. Thorstad


No. 99-1765-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 199; 238 Wis. 2d 666; 618 N.W.2d 240; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 793


June 23, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
August 17, 2000, Decided  
August 17, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 20, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 1241.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Richland County: EDWARD E. LEINEWEBER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State claimed the Circuit Court for Richland County (Wisconsin) erred in granting respondent's motion to suppress a warrantless blood test performed to obtain evidence of his intoxication following his arrest for a drunk driving violation.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was arrested at the scene of an accident following his admission that he had been drinking. Respondent was taken to a hospital for a blood test. The arresting officer did not obtain a warrant for the blood test, but respondent did not request that he be given an alternate form of test, nor did he ever refuse to take the blood test. The trial court concluded that appellant failed to meet its burden to justify the warrantless blood test and ordered the blood test suppressed. The blood was taken to obtain evidence of intoxication from a person lawfully arrested for drunk-driving. There was a clear indication that evidence of intoxication would be produced. The method used was reasonable. Respondent presented no objection to the test. Therefore the search was constitutionally permissible, and the trial court erred in granting respondent's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: Trial court erred in granting respondent's motion to suppress. Evidence of the blood test was admissible because it met the constitutional requirements for warrantless blood tests. The blood draw was a reasonable search under the Fourth Amendment.

Fabyan v. Town of Delafield


No. 99-2940


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2000 WI App 214; 238 Wis. 2d 842; 618 N.W.2d 274; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 786



August 16, 2000, Decided  
August 16, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: JACQUELINE R. ERWIN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from judgment of Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), affirming defendants' denial of request for variance from applicable zoning ordinance and dismissing 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim, alleging that setback requirement in ordinance was violative of equal protection, that open meetings law was violated, and insufficiency of evidence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff appealed from the trial court's judgment affirming defendants' denial of his request for a variance from the applicable zoning ordinance and dismissing his cause of action brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Plaintiff contended that the setback requirement in the zoning ordinance violated his equal protection rights, that the variance denial should have been set aside because defendant board of appeals violated the open meetings law, and that the evidence did not support denial of the variance request. The court affirmed. As to the equal protection argument, the court concluded that plaintiff had not overcome the presumption of validity, as the court was not persuaded that the ordinance failed to bear a rational relationship to its essential purpose. It was found that even if a closed session held by defendant board of appeals violated the open meetings law, the decision to deny the variance would still have stood because the vote was held in an open session. Also, the evidence supported denial of the variance request because the reasons advanced for the variance were personal in nature and personal convenience was found not to be a sufficient basis for a variance.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment was affirmed. Court concluded that the reasons advanced in support of plaintiff's request for a variance from the applicable zoning ordinance were personal in nature and that personal convenience was not a sufficient basis for a variance.

Gervais v. MSI Ins. Co.


No. 00-0088


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2000 WI App 214; 238 Wis. 2d 838; 618 N.W.2d 272; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 783



August 15, 2000, Decided  
August 15, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon County: DOROTHY L. BAIN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a summary judgment entered by the Marathon County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which dismissed their claims against defendant insurance company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff pedestrian was severely and permanently injured while walking on a sidewalk when a pickup truck, driven by an underinsured motorist, jumped the curb and drove over her. Defendant's policy limit was $ 250,000; it relied on its "other insurance" policy provision to limit its responsibility. Plaintiffs argued: (1) defendant's policy was ambiguous and should have been construed in favor of $ 225,000 coverage; (2) Wis. Stat. § 632.32(5)(g) did not permit a reduction in coverage; and (3) if construed to permit a reduction in coverage, § 632.32(5)(g) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendant. Defendant's "other insurance" provision defining its proportionate share of its underinsured motorist coverage was not ambiguous. Plaintiffs' interpretation was not reasonably supported by the policy language. Section 632.32(5)(g) did not bar defendant from reducing coverage by its proportionate share ratio. Moreover, § 632.32(5)(g) did not deprive plaintiffs of any state or federal constitutional right to enter into insurance contracts without fraud and, as a result, the statute did not violate substantive due process.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; defendant's "other insurance" provision defining its proportionate share of its underinsured motorist coverage was not ambiguous, and statute did not bar defendant from reducing coverage by its proportionate share ratio.

State v. Harmer


No. 00-0140-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2000 WI App 214; 238 Wis. 2d 838; 618 N.W.2d 272; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 784



August 15, 2000, Decided  
August 15, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for St. Croix County: SCOTT R. NEEDHAM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.025, in the Circuit Court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of engaging in repeated acts of sexual assault of the same child. On appeal, he contended that Wis. Stat. § 948.025 was unconstitutional on its face and as applied. He further contended that he should have been allowed to present testimony that his former father-in-law had solicited someone to have him killed. This was offered to support appellant's theory that his ex-wife and her father wanted him out of their lives. The court affirmed, holding that the jury was properly instructed that it must unanimously agree that appellant committed at least three assaults, but that it need not agree on which acts constituted the required three. This did not unconstitutionally permit the jury to avoid unanimity, because unanimity was required only with respect to the ultimate issue of appellant's guilt or innocence. Appellant's "hit-man" evidence was properly excluded as unfairly prejudicial and confusing.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. The jury was properly instructed on the findings needed to convict under the statute; unanimity was not required as to exactly which acts constituted the required three. The exclusion of appellant's "hit-man" evidence did not violate appellant's right to present a defense; it was properly excluded as unfairly prejudicial and confusing.

State ex rel. Hensley v. Endicott


No. 00-0076


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 189; 238 Wis. 2d 649; 618 N.W.2d 245; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 771


June 23, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
August 10, 2000, Decided  
August 10, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his complaint for declaratory judgment against respondent state corrections department on grounds that he failed to plead exhaustion of administrative remedies, as required by Wis. Stat. § 801.02(7) (1997-98).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner sought a declaratory judgment against respondents, state corrections department and its representative. Upon respondents' motion, the circuit court dismissed his complaint on grounds that he failed to plead administrative remedies exhaustion, under Wis. Stat. § 801.02(7) (1997-98). Appellant's complaint challenged the constitutionality of administrative rules forbidding inmates from receiving, by mail, pornographic tapes and other materials. Appellant claimed the rules were unconstitutional, which was a question for the courts rather than an agency or correctional officials. While failure to plead exhaustion of administrative remedies was generally fatal to a complaint, the appellate court concluded that an attempt to have an administrative agency determine the constitutionality of a statute was "futile." The appellate court reversed, holding that to require the appellant to exhaust institutional and administrative remedies to advance his constitutional challenges, as a precondition to raising them, was unnecessary.


OUTCOME: Order reversed because appellant's allegations of the unconstitutionality of administrative prison rules was question for courts rather than for agency or correctional officials. Failure to plead exhaustion of administrative remedies was not determinative. Requiring appellant to exhaust institutional and administrative remedies in order to bring constitutional challenges, as a precondition to raising them, was unnecessary.

State v. Dismuke

August 8, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: TIMOTHY G. DUGAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment and orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which assessed court costs against him, denied his postconviction motion requesting vacation of the assessment, and denied his motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to prison after his conviction for armed robbery and the trial court also imposed "applicable costs" on the appellant. The amount assessed included fees and travel costs generated by the service of numerous orders to produce him from prison for his court appearances. The appellant asserted that the costs were not authorized by Wis. Stat. Ann. § 973.06 (1997-98) and that the assessment of the costs violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection. On review, the court affirmed. The statutory framework allowed for the costs to be taxed to the appellant and he was unable to overcome the presumptive validity of the contested laws. The appellant's own actions brought about the additional costs. The appellant failed to prove that his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection were violated.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The costs in dispute were necessary disbursements and fees allowed by law and they were properly charged against the appellant as his actions brought about the additional costs. Appellant's due process and equal protection rights were not violated and therefore his constitutional claims were without merit.

Xena X. D.-C. v. Tammy L. D.


No. 99-1962


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 200; 238 Wis. 2d 516; 617 N.W.2d 894; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 738


July 13, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
August 2, 2000, Decided  
August 2, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: BRUCE SCHMIDT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a Child in Need of Protective Services (CHIPS) dispositional order of the juvenile court in the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which placed her daughter in foster care. Appellant asserted that the juvenile court erred in refusing to exercise its discretion whether or not to appoint an attorney to represent her.


OVERVIEW: The court conditionally reversed an order to place appellant mother's daughter in foster care in a Child in Need of Protective Services (CHIPS) proceeding. At the hearing, appellant requested counsel, but was told by the judge that she would have to hire an attorney. The court agreed that the juvenile court did not properly exercise its discretion on whether to appoint an attorney to represent appellant. The court held that when a parent requested counsel, or when the circumstances otherwise raised a reasonable concern that the parent would not be able to provide meaningful self-representation, the court had to exercise its discretion to determine whether or not to appoint counsel. The court found that when appellant requested counsel, displayed erratic behavior, and was evaluated as suffering from a mental disorder, the juvenile court should have considered whether to appoint counsel. The court conditionally reversed the dispositional order and remanded for the juvenile court to address the question of court-appointed counsel for appellant, and either appoint counsel and hold a new hearing, or reenter the dispositional order.


OUTCOME: Order placing appellant's daughter in foster care was conditionally reversed because juvenile court failed to exercise its discretion whether or not to appoint counsel for appellant after she requested one and displayed erratic behavior. The case was remanded for the juvenile court to consider court-appointed counsel, and either to appoint counsel and order a new hearing, or reenter dispositional order.

Crawford County v. Masel (In re Atty. Fees)


No. 99-1055


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 172; 238 Wis. 2d 380; 617 N.W.2d 188; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 710


February 16, 2000, Oral Argument  
July 27, 2000, Decided  
July 27, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Crawford County: MICHAEL T. KIRCHMAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Crawford County Circuit Court, Wisconsin, awarding him attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 (1994) of $ 175 per hour, arguing that the evidence showed that the reasonable rate for his attorney's services was $ 285 per hour.


OVERVIEW: A forfeiture action was brought against appellant by appellee for his failure to comply with its ordinance regulating large assemblies during a political and social gathering that was promoted and organized by appellant. The prosecution against appellant was dismissed, and the trial court awarded him $ 175 per hour as attorney fees. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the record did not support $ 175 as a reasonable rate for appellant's attorney's fees. Appellant presented ample evidence, including his attorney's affidavit outlining his skill and experience and affidavits of four other civil rights attorneys, that his attorney's billing rate of $ 285 per hour was consistent with the current market rate and therefore was presumptively reasonable. The trial court's decision to award $ 175 per hour based on an affidavit of one attorney and its own belief that $ 285 was not reasonable and therefore was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because the record did not support $ 175 per hour as a reasonable rate for appellant's attorney's services as it was based on one attorney's affidavit and the trial court's own belief. Case remanded for determination of appellant's attorney's reasonable rate for services.

State v. Franklin

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed convictions for battery, criminal damage to property, and two counts of disorderly conduct, as well as denial of postconviction relief motions by Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), arguing that convictions violated Wisconsin Constitution because trials were before six-person juries, as well as alleging ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for battery, criminal damage to property, and two counts of disorderly conduct, as well as appealing from the trial court's order denying his motions for postconviction relief. Defendant argued that his convictions were violative of the Wisconsin Constitution because his trials were before six-person juries under a statute that was subsequently declared unconstitutional, as well as arguing that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to object to the six-person juries. The court affirmed. The court held that defendant's failure to make a constitutional objection to the six-person juries at his trials waived or forfeited his constitutional claim presented on appeal. As to the ineffective assistance of counsel claim, the court concluded that the claim necessarily failed, because, even assuming that counsel performed deficiently, the performance did not prejudice defendant. It was found that prejudice could not have been established because defendant's six-person jury trials were otherwise fair and error-free.

As to claim of ineffective assistance of counsel for failures to object to trials by six-person juries, court concluded that prejudice could not have been established because trials were otherwise fair and error-free.

State v. Schmitz


No. 99-3299-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2000 WI App 186; 238 Wis. 2d 448; 617 N.W.2d 908; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 646



July 13, 2000, Decided  
July 13, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DENNIS G. MONTABON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from a judgment by the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) that convicted her of felony bail jumping.


OVERVIEW: As a condition of bail, appellant was to have no contact with a specific individual. Appellant was seen sitting next to the specific individual. Appellant was convicted of felony bail jumping. Appellant filed an appeal alleging that the jury heard insufficient evidence, and that she received insufficient notice of the violated bail condition. Affirming, the court held to commit a bail jumping offense, one had to intentionally violate the condition of a bond. Appellant contended that there was no evidence of her intent because there was no evidence she knew or understood that her close proximity to the specific individual violated the no contact provision. The court found a reasonable jury could infer, using its common knowledge and ordinary experience, that appellant understood that the "no contact" provision barred close physical proximity as well as express communication or physical touching with the named individual. That appellant testified otherwise was of no consequence. The jury was free to disbelieve that testimony.


OUTCOME: Conviction for felony bail jumping affirmed; appellant understood that the "no contact" provision of a condition of her bail barred close physical proximity as well as express communication or physical touching of the named individual.

City of Milwaukee v. Bell


No. 99-2541


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2000 WI App 186; 238 Wis. 2d 447; 617 N.W.2d 907; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 633



July 11, 2000, Decided  
July 11, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MARY M. KUHNMUENCH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction which was entered in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited blood alcohol concentration, alleging error in refusal to take judicial notice of defendant's previous acquittal on a companion charge and in jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction in the trial court for operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited blood alcohol concentration. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to take judicial notice of his previous acquittal of the companion charge of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated and when it instructed the jury regarding the effects of defendant's blood alcohol test results. The court affirmed. The court held that a trial court would have discretion to decide whether to take judicial notice of a fact, such that the trial court's refusal to take judicial notice of defendant's acquittal of a companion charge in this case was a proper exercise of discretion. It was also held that the trial court properly exercised its discretion when it instructed the jury regarding the effects of defendant's blood alcohol test results.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. Court concluded that trial court had discretion to decide whether to take judicial notice of a fact, such that trial court's refusal to take judicial notice of defendant's prior acquittal on companion charge was proper exercise of discretion.

Barry v. Employers Mut. Cas. Co.


No. 98-2557


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 168; 238 Wis. 2d 125; 617 N.W.2d 493; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 623


May 2, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
July 5, 2000, Decided  
July 5, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed judgment of Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) awarding him $ 36, 225 plus costs in his action against defendant communications company resulting from his fall on stairway at defendant's offices. Defendant communications company cross-appealed, alleging error in denial of motion for judgment notwithstanding verdict.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment awarding him $ 36, 225 plus costs in his action against defendant communications company resulting from his fall on a stairway at offices of defendant communications company. Defendant communications company cross-appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in denying its motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The appellate court reversed, concluding that the trial court erred in denying defendant communications company's motion. The court held that if a condition that caused injury was not "a structural defect," but rather, was "associated with the structure," no liability would attach to the owner or employer until he or she had either actual or constructive notice of such defect. It was found that the condition of the stairs was "an unsafe condition associated with the structure," and that plaintiff had failed to prove that defendant communications company had actual or constructive notice of the condition.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court was reversed. Court held that condition causing plaintiff's injury was "associated with the structure" and plaintiff failed to prove, as was required, that defendant communications company had actual or constructive notice of the condition.

County of Jefferson v. Newkirk


No. 00-0106


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2000 WI App 161; 238 Wis. 2d 92; 617 N.W.2d 676; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 608



June 29, 2000, Decided  
June 29, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: JOHN ULLSVIK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), convicting him for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1). Appellant contended the trial court erred in concluding that the initial stop was constitutionally permissible.


OVERVIEW: Appellant moved to suppress evidence, arguing he was detained without reasonable suspicion. The trial court denied appellant's motion, concluding from the arresting officer's testimony that dispatch information regarding a possible drunk driver, combined with the officer's observations of appellant's poor driving, provided reasonable suspicion to stop appellant. Once stopped, appellant's bloodshot eyes, slurred speech, and difficulty in removing his driver's license, in addition to a strong alcoholic odor, justified further detaining and questioning. Appellant was convicted and appealed. Affirming, the court concluded that the officer had reasonable suspicion at that time, based on the information he received from dispatch, and his subsequent observations of appellant's driving. Those additional observations increased the likelihood that appellant was driving while under the influence of an intoxicant, and provided ample basis for the officer to ask appellant to provide his driver's license and to question him about his drinking. Thus, appellant's motion to suppress was properly denied.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The call to dispatch describing the operator of the vehicle as a "possible drunk driver," in combination with the officer's observation of the vehicle fishtailing, constituted a reasonable suspicion that appellant was under the influence of an intoxicant.

State v. Anderson


No. 99-2128


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2000 WI App 161; 238 Wis. 2d 94; 617 N.W.2d 677; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 612



June 29, 2000, Decided  
June 29, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Portage County: FREDERIC FLEISHAUER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant filed an appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), denying her motion to vacate a judgment convicting her of misdemeanor bail jumping. Appellant asserted numerous issues, including ineffective trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, charged with disorderly conduct, was released on bond, however, she could not possess or consume any intoxicants. Appellant was charged two more times with misdemeanor bail jumping due to violating "no intoxicant" conditions. She pled no contest. The circuit court accepted appellant's plea, finding her guilty. Appellant's motion for postconviction relief was denied and she appealed. Affirming, the court held that the circuit court sufficiently reviewed the record for facts to substantiate appellant's ineffective assistance claim. However, the record conclusively demonstrated that appellant was not entitled to relief. Additionally, there was no evidence that the State unconstitutionally suppressed evidence of appellant's alcoholism, because, from the record, it appeared that appellant's attorney was aware that appellant had an alcohol problem and wanted to assert an "alcoholism defense." Appellant failed to identify what additional evidence available to the State, but not revealed to defense counsel, would have aided her defense; thus, her conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Appellant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was not supported by the record. Although appellant claimed the State unconstitutionally suppressed evidence of her alcoholism, she failed to establish what additional evidence that was not revealed to her attorney would have helped in her defense.

 

1197 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Scullion v. Wisconsin Power & Light Co.


No. 98-3221


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2000 WI App 120; 237 Wis. 2d 498; 614 N.W.2d 565; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 460


May 2, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
May 18, 2000, Decided  
May 18, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Iowa County: GEORGE S. CURRY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Motion for relief from partial stay pending appeal denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from an order of the circuit court for Iowa County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant corporation a partial stay of the execution of a money judgment for damages pending defendant's appeal of jury verdict in plaintiffs' case alleging nuisance and negligence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff husband, wife, and father sued defendant corporation alleging nuisance and negligence for stray voltage that had damaged their dairy farm operation. A jury verdict found in favor of plaintiff and the lower court granted defendant's motion for a stay of execution of the judgment pending appeal. The court remanded the case for consideration of the Gudenschwager factors. The lower court issued a partial stay and plaintiffs appealed arguing that that because defendant had met only two of the four factors, it was not entitled to any stay. That plaintiff did not meet the first of the Gudenschwager factors was irrelevant to a stay of a money judgment because the tests were not independent tests, but, rather, interrelated factors that the court was to weigh. Also, the lower court had a wide range of discretion in deciding whether to grant a stay.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the Gudenschwager factors were interrelated, but not independent tests, and the court had wide discretion in deciding whether to grant the stay.

State v. Reed


No. 99-0480


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2000 WI App 143; 237 Wis. 2d 695; 616 N.W.2d 923; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 442



May 16, 2000, Decided  
May 16, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by State v. Reed, 2000 WI 102, 237 Wis. 2d 263, 618 N.W.2d 752, 2000 Wisc. LEXIS 749 (2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Reed, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 746 (Wis. Ct. App., Aug. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, acting pro se, sought review of a judgment in the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his postconviction motion after his conviction for felony-murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for felony murder, after his accomplice committed an armed robbery in which the victim was killed. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, finding that appellant's postconviction counsel was not ineffective and the record supported that counsel advised appellant of his options concerning the no merit report; that appellant was fully advised of the operation of the felony murder statute and the maximum sentence; that appellant's double jeopardy argument was meritless, as he was not sentenced for the armed robbery, but the maximum armed robbery sentence did affect the sentence he could receive for felony murder; there was nothing in the trial court's remarks to suggest that the trial court was following a preconceived rigid sentencing policy or that it failed to exercise its discretion; and the trial court properly exercised its discretion in sentencing appellant to the maximum term of imprisonment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Appellant's postconvicton counsel was not ineffective and appellant was fully advised of his options concerning the no merit report. Double jeopardy did not attach because appellant was not sentenced for armed robbery, but armed robbery sentence was properly considered in computing maximum sentence. Trial court did not improperly exercise its discretion in sentencing.

 

1199 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


No. 00-0096, In re the Termination of Parental Rights to Victoria R.S. v. Jacob A.S.


No. 00-0096, No. 00-0097, No. 00-0098, No. 00-0099


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2000 WI App 143; 237 Wis. 2d 693; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 436



May 11, 2000, Decided  
May 11, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Waushara County: LEWIS MURACH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed the orders of the Circuit Court for Waushara County, Wisconsin, terminating his parental rights to his four children in favor of petitioner county.


OVERVIEW: Respondent's parental rights to his four children were terminated. Respondent claimed the statute that allowed termination of parental rights to one child based upon the commission of a serious felony against another child violated due process, and he challenged the determination of the trial court that termination of parental rights were in the best interests of the children. The record showed that the trial court weighed each of the applicable factors of Wis. Stat. § 48.426 for each child. The trial court emphasized that respondent seemed to lack a basic understanding of the children's needs and how his conduct was dangerous to their well-being. The trial court properly concluded that termination would not cause harm to the children by severing a substantial relationship.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; trial court weighed each of the applicable statutory factors for each child in deciding best interests; trial court properly concluded that termination would not cause harm to the children by severing a substantial relationship.

 

1200 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


City of Onalaska v. Prien


No. 99-3056


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2000 WI App 143; 237 Wis. 2d 698; 616 N.W.2d 924; 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 433



May 11, 2000, Decided  
May 11, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] Pursuant to WIS. STAT. Rule 809.23(3) of Appellate Procedure, an unpublished opinion is of no precedential value and for this reason may not be cited in any court of this state as precedent or authority except to support a claim of res judicata, collateral estoppel or law of the case.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: RAMONA A. GONZALEZ, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) dismissing his appeal from a municipal court conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the municipal court impermissibly required him to pay his forfeiture for conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant before the circuit court would have jurisdiction over his appeal. The court held that appellant's assessment of the requirements to perfect his appeal was incorrect. Wis. Stat. § 800.14(2) required appellant to execute a bond for the payment of his forfeiture, should he not prevail on appeal. This was not a request to pay the forfeiture. Precedent holding that failure to pay the filing fee did not deprive an appellate court of jurisdiction was inapplicable, because the issue was the posting of a bond, not the payment of a filing fee. Any analogy to the rules for Wisconsin appellate courts was also inapposite, because the rules for appeals to a circuit court from a municipal court fell under a different statutory scheme.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of his municipal court appeal, because appellant did not post the forfeiture bond required by statute. Appellant's posting of this bond was a requirement for appeal, without which the lower court properly dismissed the appeal.
